Faith and Disbelief
beginner
6 min
The First Ten Characteristics of the Saved Group
The author lists the first ten characteristics that define a follower of the Sawad al-Azam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first ten characteristics that define a follower of the Sawad al-Azam and how they promote unity, orthodoxy, and avoid extremism.

Core Idea
The saved group is known by specific traits that emphasize unity, tolerance, and acceptance of orthodox practices.

Imam al-Samarqandi begins enumerating the sixty-two characteristics of the Saved Group. The first ten set the foundation: firm faith without doubt, unity with the community, tolerance in prayer leadership, not excommunicating sinners, affirming divine decree, and more. As you read, notice how these traits protect against sectarianism and extremism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the English translation to get a sense of the full list.
Note the ordinal numbers (first, second, etc.) that structure the list.
2
Identify the structure and scope
The passage introduces the sixty-two traits, then lists the first ten. Notice how each trait is introduced with 'that' (an) and a verb.
This is a clear enumeration; each trait is a distinct point.
3
Cluster the traits by theme
Group the ten traits into themes: faith (1, 10), community unity (2, 7), prayer leadership (3, 9), excommunication (4), funeral prayer (5), divine decree (6), and practices (8).
This helps see the breadth of the Saved Group's characteristics.
4
Examine the 'if Allah wills' issue
The first trait warns against saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' as a sign of doubt. Discuss how this relates to certainty of faith.
This is a key point distinguishing orthodox Ahl al-Sunna from those who doubt.
5
Reflect on the overall purpose
Consider how these ten traits together define a moderate, united community that avoids extremes in theology, practice, and politics.
These are foundational for the remaining fifty-two traits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلامة السواد الأعظم ان يكون الانسان متصفا باثنتين وستين خصلة ) أولاها ( أنه لا يشك فى ايمانه ولا يقول انا مؤمن ان شاء الله تعالى ) والثانية ( ان لا يخالف جماعة المسلمين ) والثالثة ان يصلى خلف كل بروفاجر ويرى ذلك حقا ) والرابعة ( ان لا يكفر احدا من اهل القبلة بالذنب مالم يستحله ) والخامسة ) ان يصلى على جنازة كل صغير وكبير من اهل القبلة ويراه حقا ( والسادسة ) ان يرى تقدير الخير والشر من الله تعالى ( والسابعة ) ان لا يخرج على احد من المسلمين بالسيف من غير حق ) والثامنة ) أن يرى المسح على الخفين فى الحضر و السفر حقا ( والتاسعة ) ان يصلى خلف كل امير صلاة العيدين والجمعة وبراه حقا ( والعاشرة ) ان يرى ان الايمان عطاء الله تعالى عز وجل
The sign of the greatest majority (al-Sawad al-Azam) is that a person possesses sixty-two traits. The first: that he does not doubt his faith and does not say 'I am a believer if Allah wills.' The second: that he does not oppose the Muslim community. The third: that he prays behind every pious and wicked person and considers that permissible. The fourth: that he does not excommunicate anyone from the people of the qibla due to a sin as long as he does not deem it lawful. The fifth: that he prays over the funeral of every young and old from the people of the qibla and considers that permissible. The sixth: that he believes the decree of good and evil is from Allah Almighty. The seventh: that he does not rise against any Muslim with the sword without justification. The eighth: that he considers wiping over the socks (khuffayn) permissible both at home and while traveling. The ninth: that he prays behind every ruler the prayers of the two Eids and Friday and considers that permissible. The tenth: that he believes that faith (iman) is a gift from Allah Almighty.
Source pages p. 2

Commentary
This passage begins the enumeration of the 62 traits of the follower of the Sawad al-Azam. The author states that the sign of the saved group is possessing these traits. He then lists the first ten. These include: (1) not doubting one's faith or using the conditional 'if Allah wills' to express uncertainty about being a believer; (2) not opposing the Muslim community; (3) praying behind any imam, whether pious or sinful; (4) not declaring fellow Muslims to be disbelievers because of sin, unless they consider the sin lawful; (5) praying funeral prayers for all Muslims, young and old; (6) affirming that both good and evil decree come from Allah; (7) not rebelling against Muslim rulers with weapons without just cause; (8) accepting the practice of wiping over leather socks in ablution, both in residence and travel; (9) praying Eid and Friday prayers behind any ruler; (10) believing that faith is a gift from Allah, not a human acquisition. These traits emphasize unity, avoidance of extremism, and acceptance of sound practices.

Key Terms
السواد الأعظم
المسح على الخفين
أهل القبلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that saying 'I am a believer if Allah wills' shows humility, but this passage teaches it indicates doubt about one's own faith.
Correction: The Saved Group affirms certainty of faith and avoids conditional statements that imply uncertainty.

Checkpoint
According to the eighth characteristic, what practice is affirmed?
A) Praying behind any ruler
B) Wiping over socks
C) Not excommunicating sinners
D) Believing faith is a gift

Key Takeaway
The first ten traits of the Saved Group establish a baseline of orthodox belief and practice that avoids extremes, fosters unity, and upholds key Sunni positions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of these first ten characteristics challenges your current attitude or practice most directly? What specific change will you make this week to align with it?
?
Have you ever doubted your faith or said 'insha'Allah' to express uncertainty in your belief? How does the first trait confront that habit, and what step can you take to strengthen your certainty?
?
Do you find it difficult to pray behind leaders whose piety you question? How does the third and ninth trait reshape your responsibility toward communal prayer, even when you disagree with the imam's character?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
5 min
Faith Requires Heart and Tongue
Definition of disbelief and hypocrisy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that true faith requires both inner conviction and verbal confession, and the difference between a disbeliever and a hypocrite according to Imam Samarqandi.

Core Idea
Faith is not complete without both heart and tongue.

Imam Samarqandi begins article 43 by distinguishing between two types of deficient faith: one who knows in the heart but does not confess with the tongue is a disbeliever, while one who confesses with the tongue but lacks heart knowledge is a hypocrite. This article establishes the essential components of true faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the article uses a conditional structure: 'man... fa...'.
2
Identify the two categories
The passage presents two types: disbeliever and hypocrite. Find how each is defined based on heart knowledge and tongue confession.
Disbeliever lacks tongue confession; hypocrite lacks heart knowledge.
3
Reflect on the necessity of both
Ask yourself why both heart and tongue are required for true faith. Consider the implications for practical belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( الثالثة والاربعون ) ان يعلم ان من عرف الله تعالى بالقلب ولم يقر باللسان فهو كافر و من أقر باللسان ولم يعرف بالقلب فهو منافق ( الرابعة والاربعون ( ان لا يثبت لله تعالى مكانا ولا زمانا ولاعياً ولاذهابا ) الخامسة والاربعون ( ان لا يشبه الله بشيء ويقول ليس كمثله شئ ( السادسة والاربعون ان يرى، إن الكسب يفترض في بعض الاوقات ( السابعة والاربعون ( ان يعلم ان الإيمان بائن من العمل ( الثامنة والاربعون) ان يعلم ان ايمان المحسن والمسيء سواء ) التاسعة والاربعون ( أن يرى ان البعث بعد الموت حق
(43rd) That he know that whoever knows Allah Almighty in his heart but does not confess with his tongue is a disbeliever, and whoever confesses with his tongue but does not know in his heart is a hypocrite. (44th) That he not affirm for Allah Almighty a place, nor a time, nor a direction, nor going. (45th) That he not liken Allah to anything, and say 'There is nothing like unto Him.' (46th) That he consider that acquisition (kasb) is obligatory at some times. (47th) That he know that faith is separate from action. (48th) That he know that the faith of the good-doer and the evil-doer is the same. (49th) That he consider that resurrection after death is true.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage covers articles 43-49. Article 43 defines a disbeliever as one who knows Allah in heart but does not verbally confess, and a hypocrite as one who confesses verbally without heart knowledge – implying both heart and tongue are necessary for true faith. Article 44 denies Allah a place, time, direction, or movement (dhahab – going), affirming divine transcendence. Article 45 negates any likeness to Allah, citing the Qur'anic verse 'laysa kamithlihi shay'. Article 46 states that 'acquisition' (kasb) is obligatory at some times – a reference to the Ash'ari concept of kasb, where humans acquire their acts while Allah creates them. Article 47 separates faith (iman) from action (amal), indicating faith does not increase or decrease by deeds. Article 48 states that the faith of the good-doer and evil-doer is the same – faith is identical in essence regardless of deeds. Article 49 affirms resurrection after death.

Key Terms
منافق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Verbal confession alone makes one a believer.
Correction: The passage states that one who confesses with the tongue but lacks heart knowledge is a hypocrite, not a believer.

Checkpoint
According to article 43, what is the status of a person who knows Allah in his heart but does not confess with his tongue?
A) Disbeliever
B) Hypocrite
C) Believer
D) Sinner

Key Takeaway
True faith requires both inner knowledge and verbal confession; lacking either results in disbelief or hypocrisy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were in a situation where declaring your faith could cost you your life, would you still confess with your tongue? This lesson says that withholding confession makes you a disbeliever in Allah's sight. What does your answer reveal about the state of your heart?
?
Have you ever recited the Shahada or said you believe, but in your heart you harbor doubts or do not truly know Allah? This lesson calls that hypocrisy. What will you do today to ensure your inward knowledge matches your outward words?
?
When you say 'I believe in Allah,' do you actually sense that you know Him? If not, what is one step you can take this week to move from mere tongue confession to heart knowledge?

Allah Transcends Place, Time, and Likeness
Negation of physical attributes and likeness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah is beyond physical attributes such as place, time, direction, and any similarity to creation.

Core Idea
Allah is not confined by place, time, or likeness.

Articles 44 and 45 affirm Allah's absolute transcendence. Article 44 denies that Allah has a place, time, direction, or movement. Article 45 negates any similarity between Allah and His creation, citing the Quranic verse 'laysa kamithlihi shay'. Together they establish the foundational principle of tanzih.

Guided Path
1
Read the two articles
Read articles 44 and 45 together. Notice the explicit negation of place, time, direction, and going.
2
Understand the negations
Reflect on why place, time, direction, and movement are denied for Allah. Consider the implications for Allah's transcendence.
3
Grasp the principle of tanzih
Article 45 and the verse 'laysa kamithlihi shay' establish that Allah is unlike anything in creation.
This is a core tenet of Islamic theology.

Source Text

Article 46 states that 'acquisition' (kasb) is obligatory at some times – a reference to the Ash'ari concept of kasb, where humans acquire their acts while Allah creates them. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah is in the sky or on the Throne in a physical sense.
Correction: Article 44 denies place and direction, so Allah is not located in any place.

Checkpoint
Which of the following should not be affirmed for Allah according to article 44?
A) Power
B) Place
C) Mercy
D) Will

Key Takeaway
Allah transcends all physical and spatial limitations and is unlike anything in creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about Allah, do you unconsciously imagine a 'place' where He is, like a throne or heaven? How does this lesson challenge that habit, and what specific step will you take today to train your mind to think of Him as beyond all places?
?
If someone asked you 'Where is Allah?' and you answered based on this lesson, would you feel confident? Are you willing to let go of comfortable mental images of Allah, even if it feels strange at first?
?
The verse 'There is nothing like unto Him' is easy to recite but hard to live by. When do you most feel tempted to compare Allah to something in your life? Will you commit to catching yourself and repeating this verse whenever you do?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
6 min
Acquisition, Faith, and Action
Three articles on kasb, faith-action separation, and equality of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari concept of kasb, that faith is separate from action, and that faith is identical for all believers.

Core Idea
Acts do not change faith; all believers share the same faith.

Articles 46-48 address human action and faith. Article 46 introduces 'acquisition' (kasb) as obligatory at times. Article 47 separates faith from action, meaning deeds do not increase or decrease faith. Article 48 states that the faith of the righteous and the sinner is the same. These articles clarify the relationship between iman and amal.

Guided Path
1
Read the three articles
Read articles 46, 47, and 48. Note the key statements: 'kasb is obligatory', 'faith is separate from action', 'faith of good and evil-doer is same'.
2
Understand kasb
Reflect on the concept of acquisition: humans acquire their acts while Allah creates them. The phrase 'obligatory at some times' indicates moral responsibility.
This is a distinctively Ash'ari position.
3
Grasp faith-action separation
Article 47 explicitly separates faith from action. This means deeds do not affect the reality of faith.
4
Recognize equality of faith
Article 48 states all believers have identical faith in essence, regardless of their deeds.
This reinforces the previous article.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(43rd) That he know that whoever knows Allah Almighty in his heart but does not confess with his tongue is a disbeliever, and whoever confesses with his tongue but does not know in his heart is a hypocrite. (44th) That he not affirm for Allah Almighty a place, nor a time, nor a direction, nor going. (45th) That he not liken Allah to anything, and say 'There is nothing like unto Him.' (48th) That he know that the faith of the good-doer and the evil-doer is the same. (49th) That he consider that resurrection after death is true.

Commentary
This passage covers articles 43-49. Article 43 defines a disbeliever as one who knows Allah in heart but does not verbally confess, and a hypocrite as one who confesses verbally without heart knowledge – implying both heart and tongue are necessary for true faith. Article 44 denies Allah a place, time, direction, or movement (dhahab – going), affirming divine transcendence. Article 45 negates any likeness to Allah, citing the Qur'anic verse 'laysa kamithlihi shay'. Article 46 states that 'acquisition' (kasb) is obligatory at some times – a reference to the Ash'ari concept of kasb, where humans acquire their acts while Allah creates them. Article 47 separates faith (iman) from action (amal), indicating faith does not increase or decrease by deeds. Article 48 states that the faith of the good-doer and evil-doer is the same – faith is identical in essence regardless of deeds. Article 49 affirms resurrection after death.

Key Terms
الكسب
الإيمان بائن من العمل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith increases with good deeds and decreases with sins.
Correction: Article 47 says faith is separate from action, and article 48 says the faith of the good-doer and evil-doer is the same, so faith does not change with deeds.

Checkpoint
According to article 48, how does the faith of a good-doer compare to that of an evil-doer?
A) The good-doer has more faith
B) It differs
C) It is the same
D) It is unknown

Key Takeaway
Faith is unchanged by actions; all believers have identical faith in essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If faith is separate from action, do you truly rely on your faith for salvation, or do you secretly depend on your good deeds to earn Allah's pleasure? How would your daily life change if you fully internalized that your deeds do not increase your faith?
?
The faith of the good-doer and the evil-doer is the same. How does that make you look at a person you consider sinful? Do you still feel superior in faith, or can you see their faith as equal to yours? What would it take for you to treat them as a full brother or sister in faith?
?
Article 46 says kasb is obligatory at some times. When was the last time you consciously performed an act of obedience purely as an acquisition from Allah, feeling your own responsibility? Are you lazy in acquiring good deeds when they are demanded of you?

Resurrection After Death Is True
Affirmation of resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that resurrection after death is a fundamental belief according to Imam Samarqandi.

Core Idea
Resurrection after death is undoubtedly true.

The final article in this section affirms the reality of resurrection after death. This is a core tenet of Islamic faith, establishing the afterlife and accountability.

Guided Path
1
Read the article
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the simple affirmation: 'al-ba'th ba'd al-mawt haqq'.
2
Reflect on its importance
Consider why belief in resurrection is essential in the Islamic creed and how it relates to the other articles.

?
If you truly believed that you will be resurrected and held accountable, what would you change about how you spend your time today?
?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
5 min
The First Issue: Certainty of Faith
Imam Samarqandi prescribes certainty in professing one's faith and prohibits doubt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a believer must affirm his faith with certainty and not express doubt, based on the Qur'anic command to avoid doubt.

Core Idea
Faith and doubt cannot coexist in a believer's heart.

This lesson addresses a foundational issue in Islamic creed: how should a believer speak about his faith? Some people say 'I am a believer if Allah wills' out of humility, but this text argues that such phrasing implies doubt, which contradicts the Qur'anic description of true believers. We will examine the evidence and the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the English translation. Let the author's words sink in before interpreting.
Notice the concise style of the Imam's ruling.
2
Identify the ruling
The passage gives a clear command: a believer should not doubt his faith and should not say 'insha'Allah'. Instead, he must say 'I am a believer truly'. Identify this prohibition and affirmation.
3
Understand the Quranic proof
The Imam quotes Quran 49:15, which states that true believers are those who believe and then do not doubt (lam yartabu). The word 'yartabu' means doubt. Reflect on how this verse supports the ruling.
The term 'lam yartabu' is the negation of doubt.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why saying 'insha'Allah' is considered doubt. How does this shape our understanding of faith? The lesson shows that faith requires certainty, not conditional hope.
This connects to the broader theme of certainty in Aqeedah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة الاولى مما ذكرنا انه ينبغي للمؤمن ان لايشك فى ايمانه ولا يقول انا مؤمن ان شاء الله بل يقول انا مؤمن حقا لان الله تعالى قال انما المؤمنون الذين آمنوا بالله ورسوله ثم لم يرتابوا يعنى لم يشكوا فى ايمانهم ) واعلم ( ان الله تعالى ذكر الخلق على ثلاثة اصناف (ذكر)
The First Issue: From what we have mentioned, it is proper for the believer not to doubt his faith and not to say 'I am a believer if Allah wills,' but rather he should say 'I am a believer truly,' because Allah Almighty said: 'The believers are only those who believe in Allah and His Messenger then do not doubt' – meaning they do not doubt their faith. And know that Allah Almighty mentioned creation as three types. (He mentioned).
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage begins a new section titled 'The First Issue'. It addresses the ruling on expressing one's faith. The author argues that a believer should not doubt his faith nor say 'ana mu'min in sha' Allah' (I am a believer if Allah wills). Instead, he should affirm 'ana mu'min haqqan' (I am a believer truly). The proof is Qur'an 49:15: 'Indeed, the believers are only those who believe in Allah and His Messenger and then do not doubt.' The word 'yartabu' means 'doubt'. Thus, doubt is incompatible with faith. The author then says that Allah has created people into three categories, but the text is cut off at the end of the page. This marks a transition from listing articles of faith to a detailed discussion of a specific issue.

The Effect of Istithna' on Faith and Contracts
Ruling that istithna' invalidates faith and contracts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why using the phrase 'in sha Allah' as an exception in statements of faith and legal contracts invalidates both faith and the associated rulings.

Core Idea
Making an exception with 'in sha Allah' in matters of faith or contracts nullifies them completely.

The author of al-Sawad al-A'zam addresses a critical issue: does adding 'in sha Allah' to statements of belief or legal agreements affect their validity? The passage establishes that such an exception, whether in Persian or Arabic, renders the statement invalid—both in matters of faith and in worldly contracts. This lesson explores the ruling and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once and compare it with the English translation. Note the examples given.
The Arabic has some unclear words due to OCR, but the meaning is clear.
2
Understand the ruling on faith statements
Focus on the first part: saying statements of faith in Persian with 'in sha Allah' makes one a disbeliever. The author extends this to Arabic as well.
3
Examine the application to contracts
Look at the examples: divorce, freeing slaves, oaths, and sales. In each case, adding 'in sha Allah' prevents the ruling from taking effect.
This shows the principle applies beyond faith.
4
Grasp the general principle
The passage concludes that both legal rulings and faith are invalidated by exception. Reflect on why this is significant.
The principle is that istithna' indicates uncertainty, which is incompatible with the certainty required in faith and contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لان احد الوقال [؟] بالفارسية خداهست انشاء الله فرشتگان و جنیان هست ان شاء الله تعالی رستخیز بودان شاء الله تعالى فيصير كافرا بلا خلاف فلما لم يجز ان يقول بالفارسية فكذلك لا يجوز ان يقول بالعربية الأخرى الى وجوه الاحكام لو ان رجلا قال لامر أنه أنت طالق ان شاء الله تعالى او قال لعبده انت حر ان شاء الله او قال الله على كذا و كذا او قال بمت او اشتريت ان شاء الله لا يجب عليه شيء فالاحكام تبعال [؟] بالاستناء وكذلك بطل الايمان بالاستثناء وفى هذا القدر كفاية للعاقل
Because if one says in Persian 'Khuda hast' (there is a god) 'in sha Allah', or 'Farishtagan' (angels) 'in sha Allah', or 'Jinniyan' (jinn) 'in sha Allah', or 'Rastikhiz bavad' (resurrection will occur) 'in sha Allah', he becomes a disbeliever without dispute. So when it is not permissible to say in Persian, likewise it is not permissible to say in Arabic. Other rulings: if a man said to his wife 'You are divorced, in sha Allah', or said to his slave 'You are free, in sha Allah', or said 'Upon me is an oath for such and such, in sha Allah', or said 'I sold' or 'I bought, in sha Allah', nothing is binding on him. Thus rulings are invalidated by exception, and similarly faith is invalidated by exception. And in this amount is sufficient for the intelligent.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling (hukm) concerning the effect of making an exception (istithna') using the phrase 'in sha Allah' on various statements. It begins by stating that saying things like 'There is a god' or 'Angels exist' or 'Jinn exist' or 'Resurrection will occur' with 'in sha Allah' in Persian makes one a disbeliever without dispute. The author argues that if it is not permissible to say such things in Persian, then it is also not permissible in Arabic. The ruling then extends to other areas of law: divorce, freeing slaves, vows, and sale contracts. If a man says 'You are divorced, in sha Allah' or 'You are free, in sha Allah' or makes an oath with 'in sha Allah' or says 'I sold' or 'I bought, in sha Allah', nothing becomes binding on him. The principle is that exceptions (istithna') nullify the rulings (ahkam) in these matters. Similarly, making an exception in matters of faith (iman) invalidates one's faith. The author concludes that this explanation is sufficient for an intelligent person.

Key Terms
الاستثناء (istithna')
الإيمان (iman)
الاحكام (ahkam)
ان شاء الله (in sha Allah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think saying 'in sha Allah' out of humility or hope does not affect faith.
Correction: The author rules that using 'in sha Allah' as an exception in statements of faith invalidates faith, regardless of intention.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if someone makes an exception (istithna') in a statement of faith by saying 'in sha Allah'?
A) Their faith is still valid because it is a sign of humility.
B) Their faith becomes invalid because exception invalidates faith.
C) It is permissible only in Persian but not in Arabic.
D) Only the worldly contracts are affected, not faith.

Key Takeaway
Using 'in sha Allah' as an exception in matters of faith or contracts invalidates them entirely.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you used 'in sha Allah' to avoid absolute certainty in a belief, perhaps thinking it shows humility? How does this lesson challenge that assumption, and what change must you make in your speech today?
?
Do you ever catch yourself using 'in sha Allah' in a way that suggests you are not fully convinced of Allah's power or the truth of His promises? What would it mean for your iman if you continued that habit after knowing this ruling?
?
This passage equates saying 'in sha Allah' in matters of faith with outright disbelief. Can you identify any area of your aqeedah where you harbor a slight hesitation that you cover with 'in sha Allah'? How will you eliminate that hesitation and affirm your certainty with your tongue and heart?

The Ruling on Excommunication and the Analogy of Faith
States the condition for excommunication and provides rational and Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that a believer does not exit iman by committing major sins unless he deems them lawful, based on rational analogy and Quranic proof.

Core Idea
Sin does not undo iman; only istihlal (deeming it lawful) does.

This lesson establishes a foundational principle of Ahl al-Sunna: a Muslim remains a believer even after major sins, as long as he does not consider them permissible. The author uses a striking analogy with disbelief and good deeds, then backs it with Quranic verses where Allah calls sinners 'believers' and commands their repentance. We will break down this argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the core ruling
Read the opening statement: a believer should not excommunicate anyone from the qibla for a sin unless he deems it lawful. Notice the condition of istihlal.
Takfir is a serious matter; only istihlal makes one leave the fold.
2
Understand the analogy
The author draws a symmetry: just as a disbeliever's good deeds don't make him a believer, a believer's sins don't make him a disbeliever. What is the underlying logic?
This shows that iman and kufr are not determined by acts alone but by inner conviction.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Allah addresses sinners as 'O you who have believed' when commanding repentance. Why would He call them believers if they had become disbelievers?
The Quran itself treats sinners as believers.
4
Consider the prophetic examples
Adam disobeyed but was not called a disbeliever. Harut and Marut drank wine and intended fornication yet remained believers. What do these examples teach?
Sins, even major ones, do not remove iman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة الرابعة م وما ذكرنا انه ينبغي للمؤمن ان لا يكفر احدا من اهل القبلة بالذنب مالم يستحله ( اعلم ( ان المؤمن لوزنى بمائة الف مسلمة اوقتل مأةالف مسلم اوشرب الفدن من الحمر فانه لا يخرج من الايمان ما لم يستحله كما ان الكافر لو عمل جميع الخيرات والطاعات لا يخرج من الكفر حتى يؤمن بالله فكذلك المؤمن لو فعل جميع المعاصى لا يخرج من الايمان حتى يكفر بالله وهذا من وجه العقل والنظر الأترى [؟] ان الله تعالى امر المؤمنين بالتوبة لمن كان مشتغلا منهم بالفسق والفجور والمعصية سماهم الله تعالى مؤمنين فقال تعالى يا ايها الذين آمنوا توبوا إلى الله توبة نصوحا ولو كانوا هؤلاء كفروا بالذنوب لماسماهم مؤمنين وكان يقول ياايها الذين كفروا توبوا الى الله وقال تعالى ايضا وتوبوا الى الله جميعا ايها المؤمنون وما قال ايها الكافرون وكذلك لما دخل آدم صلوات الله عليه الجنة فنها ء الله عن قرب الشجرة فاكل منها فقال الله تعالى وعصى آدم ربه فنوى [؟] وماقال وكفر آدم بربه وكذلك شرب هاروت و ماروت الحمر فقصدا الزناء ثم اختارا عذاب الدنيا على عذاب الاخرة ولم يكفرا ) واعلم ( ان المؤمن لم يكفر بالذنوب ) اخبرنا ( الثقات بإسنادهم عن اربعين نفسا من التابعين كلهم ممن شهد بدرا واجمع واكلهم [؟] على ان الرسول عليه السلام قال سبعة من الهدى وفيهن الجماعة. ومن خرج منهن خرج من الجماعة لا تشهدوا على اهل القبلة بكفر ولا يشرك ولا بنفاق وذر واسر آثرهم [؟] الى الله تعالى وصلوا على من مات من اهل القبلة واشهد وا الصلوات الخمس والجمع وصاوا خلف كل بروفاجر وجاهدوا عدوكم مع كل امير ولا تخر جوا على المتكم بالسيف وان جاروا قادء والهم بالصلاح والعافية وجانبوا الاهواء كلها فان اولها وآخرها باطل وهذا القدر كفاية للعاقل
The fourth question. And what we have mentioned, that it is befitting for the believer not to excommunicate anyone from the people of the qibla due to a sin unless he deems it lawful. Know: if a believer commits adultery with one hundred thousand Muslim women, or kills one hundred thousand Muslims, or drinks a large amount of wine, he does not leave faith as long as he does not deem it lawful. Just as a disbeliever, if he does all good deeds and acts of obedience, does not leave disbelief until he believes in Allah, likewise a believer, if he does all sins, does not leave faith until he disbelieves in Allah. And this is from the perspective of intellect and consideration. Do you not see that Allah, the Most High, commanded the believers to repent, while they were engaged in sin and immorality and disobedience, and He called them believers? He said: 'O you who have believed, repent to Allah with sincere repentance.' If those had become disbelievers by sins, He would not have called them believers, and He would have said: 'O you who have disbelieved, repent to Allah.' And He also said: 'And repent to Allah, all of you, O believers,' and He did not say 'O disbelievers.' Similarly, when Adam (peace be upon him) entered Paradise and Allah forbade him from approaching the tree, and he ate from it, Allah said: 'And Adam disobeyed his Lord and so he erred.' He did not say: 'And Adam disbelieved in his Lord.' And similarly, Harut and Marut drank wine and intended to commit fornication, then they chose the punishment of this world over the punishment of the Hereafter, and they did not become disbelievers. And know that the believer does not become a disbeliever by sins. The trustworthy informed us with their chains from forty individuals among the Tabi'un, all of whom were present at Badr, and they all agreed that the Messenger, peace be upon him, said: 'Seven things from guidance, and among them is the congregation. Whoever leaves them leaves the congregation: do not testify against the people of the qibla with disbelief, nor with shirk, nor with hypocrisy; and leave their hidden matters to Allah; and pray over those who die from the people of the qibla; and witness the five prayers and the Friday prayer; and pray behind every righteous and sinful; and fight your enemy with every ruler; and do not rebel against your rulers with the sword even if they are unjust; and supplicate for their righteousness and well-being; and avoid all desires, for their beginning and end are false.' And this amount is sufficient for the intelligent.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal ruling on the status of a Muslim who commits major sins. The author asserts that a believer should not excommunicate (takfir) any Muslim for sins unless that person deems the sin lawful (istihlal). The reasoning is analogous: just as a disbeliever does not become a believer by doing good deeds, a believer does not become a disbeliever by committing sins. This is supported by intellectual proof: Allah addresses sinners as believers in the Quran when commanding repentance, e.g., 'O you who have believed, repent to Allah.' If they were disbelievers by sin, He would have addressed them as disbelievers. Additionally, the examples of Adam and Harut and Marut show that sin does not constitute disbelief. The passage concludes with a hadith from forty Tabi'un who were present at Badr, listing seven principles of guidance: not excommunicating Muslims for sins, not labeling them as polytheists or hypocrites, leaving their hidden matters to Allah, performing funeral prayers for them, attending the five prayers and Friday prayer, praying behind any imam, performing jihad with any ruler, not rebelling against authorities even if unjust, praying for their well-being, and avoiding all heretical innovations.

Key Terms
التكفير (takfir)
الذنب (dhanb)
الاستحلال (istihlal)
أهل القبلة (ahl al-qibla)
الإيمان (iman)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that committing a major sin automatically removes a person from iman.
Correction: The passage clarifies that only istihlal (deeming it lawful) removes iman; the sin itself does not.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition causes a Muslim to leave iman?
A) Committing a major sin
B) Deeming a sin lawful
C) Repeating the sin
D) Not repenting

Key Takeaway
A believer remains in iman despite major sins unless he considers them lawful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever considered another Muslim to be a disbeliever because of a sin they committed? How does this passage challenge that attitude, and what does it mean for your relationship with them? What step will you take to change that judgment?
?
Think of a sin you have committed. Do you fear that it has taken you out of the fold of faith? According to this lesson, what is the real danger to your iman? Are you more concerned about avoiding sins or about avoiding istihlal? How does this shift your focus in your daily struggle?
?
The lesson teaches that a disbeliever's good deeds do not bring iman without belief. Reflect on your own good deeds: do you rely on them for your salvation, or on your faith in Allah? How can you ensure that your deeds are built on the foundation of iman, and what will you change in your practice starting today?

The Prophetic Guidance on Unity and Community
Prophetic tradition listing seven principles of guidance for community unity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seven principles of guidance from the Prophet that preserve the unity of the Muslim community.

Core Idea
The Prophet taught how to keep the community united despite differences.

The passage concludes with a prophetic tradition transmitted by forty Tabi'un who fought at Badr. This hadith outlines seven principles for maintaining community cohesion, including not excommunicating fellow Muslims, praying behind any imam, and avoiding rebellion. These teachings reinforce the earlier ruling on takfir and provide practical guidance for communal life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven principles
The hadith lists seven items from guidance. Read them carefully and number them.
They include rulings on prayer, jihad, and avoiding rebellion.
2
Understand the context of transmission
The hadith is transmitted by forty Tabi'un who attended Badr. Why might this chain be emphasized?
These are early authorities, adding weight to the teaching.
3
Relate to the previous lesson
How does this hadith support the principle that Muslims should not be excommunicated for sins?
The first principle explicitly forbids testifying with disbelief against ahl al-qibla.

Think of a ruler or authority figure you disagree with or even dislike. When you see their shortcomings, does your heart lean towards criticism and distancing from unity? According to this hadith, what is your actual duty—not just regarding rebellion, but for your daily prayers and supplications? How can you change your internal posture tonight in your du'a?
?
You have likely witnessed a fellow Muslim commit a sin that you considered major. In that moment, did your mind immediately label them as 'less of a Muslim' or even question their faith? This hadith commands you to leave hidden matters to Allah. What does that demand of you the next time you see a sin? Be specific: what thought will you replace with trust in Allah's judgment?
?
The hadith instructs you to pray behind every righteous and sinful imam. Is there an imam or leader you avoid because you perceive them as sinful? How does your avoidance harm the unity this hadith commands? What is one concrete step you will take this week to participate in congregational prayer despite such feelings?

Prohibition of Rebellion Against Muslims
Samarqandi prohibits rebellion with the sword against Muslims unjustly.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why rebelling against Muslims with the sword is prohibited and the severe warning from the Prophet about the consequences for both killer and killed.

Core Idea
Rebelling against believers brings mutual ruin.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational ruling from Imam Samarqandi: that a believer must not take up arms against any Muslim unjustly. The author cites a hadith that warns both the aggressor and the defender who intend harm against each other will be in the Fire. This establishes the gravity of internal conflict within the Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic sentence and its translation carefully. Notice that the ruling is presented as the 'seventh question' from earlier discussions.
2
Reflect on the hadith
The Prophet (peace be upon him) says both the killer and the killed (who intentionally fight each other) are in the Fire. Consider what this implies about the severity of rebellion.
This hadith emphasizes mutual responsibility and the danger of factionalism.
3
Understand the scope
The ruling applies when there is no just cause. Ask yourself: what kinds of rebellion are included? The phrase 'unjustly' indicates that legitimate self-defense or fighting oppression may be exceptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة السابعة: وما ذكرنا أنه ينبغي للمؤمن أن لا يخرج على أحد من المسلمين بالسيف بغير حق لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: القاتل والمقتول في النار إذا قصد كل واحد إلى صاحبه. واعلم أن من قتل مؤمنا خطأ وجبت عليه الدية والكفارة، ومن قتل مؤمنا متعمدا لا يكفر، وإن خرج من الدنيا تائبا يغفر له الله، وإن خرج من الدنيا بغير توبة فهو في مشيئة الله تعالى: إن شاء غفر له بفضله، وإن شاء عذبه بعدله على قدر ذنوبه ثم يخرجه الله سبحانه وتعالى من النار ويدخله الجنة. ومن قال أن هذا القاتل يبقى في النار أبدا فهو مبتدع، لأن المؤمن لا يكفر بقتل المؤمن ولا يبقى في النار إلا الكفار.
The seventh question: And what we mentioned is that it is necessary for a believer not to rebel against any of the Muslims with the sword unjustly, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The killer and the killed are in the Fire when each one intended for his companion.' And know that whoever kills a believer by mistake (khata') is obligated to pay blood money (diya) and expiation (kaffara). And whoever kills a believer intentionally (mut'amaddan) does not become an unbeliever (kafir). If he leaves the world repentant (ta'iban), Allah will forgive him. If he leaves the world without repentance, then he is under the will (mashi'a) of Allah Most High: if He wills, He forgives him by His bounty (fadl); if He wills, He punishes him by His justice (adl) according to the measure of his sins, then Allah, glorified and exalted, brings him out of the Fire and admits him to Paradise. And whoever says that this killer remains in the Fire forever is an innovator (mubtadi'), because the believer does not become an unbeliever by killing a believer, and only the unbelievers remain in the Fire forever.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on two issues: rebellion against Muslims and killing a believer. First, the author states that a believer should not take up arms against any Muslim unjustly, citing a hadith that both the killer and the killed who intentionally fight each other will be in the Fire. This underscores the gravity of internal strife. Second, the author differentiates between accidental and intentional killing. Accidental killing requires blood money and expiation. Intentional killing does not render the perpetrator an unbeliever (takfir is prohibited). If the killer repents before death, Allah forgives him. If he dies without repentance, his case is in Allah's will: He may forgive or punish, but ultimately the killer will be taken out of Hell and admitted to Paradise because he is a believer. The author condemns as an innovator anyone who says the killer remains in Hell forever, since only unbelievers abide eternally in Hell.

Key Terms
خروج بالسيف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the hadith cited by Samarqandi say about the combatants in a rebellion?
A) Both the killer and the killed are in the Fire if each intended harm.
B) Only the killer is in the Fire.
C) The killer is forgiven if he repents.
D) The killed is a martyr regardless.

Key Takeaway
Rebelling unjustly against Muslims invites severe punishment from Allah, as warned by the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever harbored such anger or resentment toward a fellow Muslim that you would have wished harm upon them? How does the Prophet's warning that both killer and killed are in the Fire if each intended for the other confront your heart today? What step can you take to release that bitterness before it leads to mutual ruin?
?
The hadith speaks of mutual intent—both parties intending harm. Is there any relationship in your life where you and another Muslim are both holding onto grudges, each waiting for the other to apologize? How can you break that cycle, knowing that both of you are accountable before Allah?
?
Rebellion begins in the heart before the sword. Do you justify any attitude of rebellion—against parents, leaders, or other believers—by thinking you are in the right? Imagine standing before Allah with that intention; would you be confident? What concrete change can you make today to align your heart with this teaching?

Rulings on Killing a Believer
Samarqandi discusses rulings on accidental and intentional killing and refutes eternal punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different rulings for accidental and intentional killing of a believer, and why intentional killing does not render one an unbeliever.

Core Idea
Intentional killing does not expel a believer from faith.

This lesson covers the second major topic from the passage: the legal and theological consequences of killing a believer. Samarqandi distinguishes between accidental and intentional killing, clarifying that intentional killing does not make the perpetrator a disbeliever, and that even if unrepentant, his ultimate fate is Paradise after punishment, not eternal Hell.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic from 'واعلم' to the end. Follow the translation to understand the rulings and the refutation of the innovator's view.
2
Differentiate accidental and intentional killing
Notice that accidental killing requires blood money and expiation, while intentional killing does not incur those worldly penalties in the same way but has a spiritual ruling.
3
Grasp the theological position
Understand that the killer remains a believer and is subject to Allah's will. The author refutes the idea of eternal punishment for such a sinner.
This is a key point against extremists who declare takfir on sinners.

Eighth Issue: Wiping Over Khuffs: Duration and Refutation of the Rafidah
Imam Samarqandi states the duration and permissibility of wiping over khuffs and refutes the Rafidah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the duration of wiping over khuffs for travelers and residents, as well as the prohibition of wiping on the bare foot as a refutation of the Rafidah.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is permitted with set durations; rejecting this is a deviant stance.

In this passage, Imam Samarqandi presents the eighth issue of the creed: the ruling on wiping over khuffs (mash al-khuffayn). He clarifies the time limits for travelers and residents, enumerates those who may perform this act, and explicitly condemns the practice of wiping on the bare foot as the way of the Rafidah. This ruling serves both as a practical legal guidance and a boundary of orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a ruling, its details, a prohibition, and a condemnation.
The passage begins with 'المسألة الثامنة' indicating this is the eighth doctrinal issue.
2
Identify the duration for traveler and resident
The passage gives two durations: three days and nights for the traveler, and one day and night for the resident. Note the counting method: from the time of hadath to the time of hadath.
3
List the categories of people who may wipe
The passage mentions several categories: the highway robber, warriors, the traveler, the sinful, and other Muslims. Notice that even the sinful are included.
This emphasizes that the ruling applies broadly, not only to the pious.
4
Understand the prohibition and its significance
The passage prohibits wiping on the bare foot, calling it the madhhab of the Rafidah and cursing them. This shows the issue is not just legal but also a theological boundary.
The author uses strong language (لعنهم الله) to distance from the Rafidah.
5
Reflect on why this is part of aqidah
Consider why a seemingly fiqhi matter is included in a creedal work. It likely serves to define orthodox practice and repudiate deviant sects.
This connects to the broader purpose of al-Sawad al-Azam: defining the saved sect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثامنة: وما ذكرنا في مسح الخفين فإنه يجوز على المسافر ثلاثة أيام ولياليها من وقت الحدث إلى وقت الحدث وعلى المقيم يوماً وليلة وبراء [؟] حقاقه قاطع الطريق والغزاة والمسافر والفاسق وغيرهم من المسلمين [؟] يمسحون على الخفين ولا يجوز المسح على الرجل العريان لأنه مذهب الروافض لعنهم الله وفي هذا القدر كفاية.
The eighth issue: And what we mentioned about wiping over the khuffs: indeed it is permissible for the traveler three days and their nights from the time of hadath to the time of hadath, and for the resident one day and night, and [??] the highway robber, the warriors, the traveler, the sinful, and other Muslims [??] wipe over the khuffs. And it is not permissible to wipe over the bare foot because it is the madhhab of the Rafidah, may Allah curse them. And in this extent is sufficiency.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage defines the eighth issue: the ruling on wiping over khuffs (mash al-khuffayn). It begins by stating the rule: a traveler may wipe for three days and nights, counting from the time of hadath (ritual impurity) to the next hadath, and a resident (muqim) may wipe for one day and night. The author then lists categories of people for whom wiping is permissible: the highway robber (qati' al-tariq), warriors (ghuzat), travelers, the sinful (fasiq), and other Muslims. The phrase 'وبراء [؟] حقاقه' is obscure but likely refers to those who have certain rights or conditions. The passage then prohibits wiping on a bare foot (al-rajul al-aryan), declaring this to be the madhhab of the Rafidah (a deviant Shi'a sect) and cursing them. The author concludes that this amount of explanation is sufficient.

Key Terms
مسح الخفين
الروافض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Wiping over khuffs is only for pious or special Muslims.
Correction: The passage explicitly includes the sinful (fasiq) and even the highway robber and warriors, showing it is for all Muslims.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on wiping over khuffs for a traveler according to this passage?
A) It is not permissible.
B) It is permissible for three days and nights.
C) It is permissible only for the righteous.
D) It is permissible for one day and night.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is a permissible practice for all Muslims with specific time limits, and rejecting it is associated with the Rafidah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage curses the Rafidah for their practice. In your own life, do you hold on to any practice or belief that you know contradicts the authentic Sunnah, out of stubbornness or sectarianism? What would it take for you to abandon it?
?
The ruling applies to all Muslims, even the sinful. Do you ever judge others as unworthy of Allah's concessions? Have you ever considered that the same mercy that allows the highway robber to wipe over his khuffs might also cover your own shortcomings?
?
The author says 'in this extent is sufficiency.' Are you content with what Allah has prescribed, or do you find yourself adding extra burdens or shortcuts? Examine your heart: are you truly submitting to His limits?

Obedience to the Sultan: Prayer Behind Rulers and Prohibition of Rebellion
Imam Samarqandi asserts the obligation to pray behind any ruler and prohibits rebellion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to obey the sultan, the permissibility of praying behind any ruler, and the prohibition of rebellion based on the Qur'anic command.

Core Idea
Obedience to the sultan is obligatory even if the ruler is unjust; rebellion is forbidden.

This passage from Imam al-Samarqandi addresses the ninth issue concerning the relationship between Muslims and their rulers. It establishes two key points: the obligation to perform congregational prayers behind any amir, and the absolute duty of obedience to the sultan, even if he is unjust. It also warns that disobedience amounts to being a Khariji, a deviant sect. Let's examine the evidence from the Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and translation. Note the main commands and the reasoning provided.
The phrase 'وبراء [؟] حقاقه' is unclear, but the main points are clear.
2
Identify the key rulings
Find the obligations (praying behind any amir, obeying the sultan) and the prohibition (rebelling with sword or disobedience).
3
Understand the reasoning
Why is obedience required even if the ruler is unjust? Because the reward or burden is on him, but obedience remains necessary.
The author links disobedience to being a Khariji.
4
Analyze the Qur'anic proof
The verse 4:59 is cited: 'Obey Allah, obey the Messenger, and those in authority among you.' The author interprets 'those in authority' as the sultans.
Reflect on how this verse supports the obligation.
5
Reflect on the sectarian warning
Why does the author call those who disobey the sultan 'Khariji'? Understand the historical context of the Kharijites who rebelled against legitimate rulers.
This highlights the seriousness of rebellion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة التاسعة: وما ذكرنا أنه يصلى خلف كل أمير صلاة العيدين والجمعة وبراء [؟] حقاقه طاعة السلطان فريضة وإن كان مثقوب الأذنين ولا يجوز الخروج عليه بالسيف ولا بالعصيان له فإن عدل كان الأجر له وإن ظلم كان الوزر عليه ولابد من طاعة السلطان بكل حال لأن من عصى السلطان ولم يعطه فهو خارجي لقوله تعالى {أطيعوا الله وأطيعوا الرسول وأولي الأمر منكم} يعني السلاطين.
The ninth issue: And what we mentioned that one prays behind every amir the prayer of the two Eids and Friday, and [??] obedience to the sultan is an obligation even if he is pierced in the ears. And it is not permissible to rebel against him with the sword nor with disobedience to him. For if he is just, the reward is for him; and if he is unjust, the burden is on him. And obedience to the sultan is necessary in every circumstance, because whoever disobeys the sultan and does not give him (his due) is a Khariji, by the saying of Allah: 'Obey Allah and obey the Messenger and those in authority among you' meaning the sultans.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage defines the ninth issue: the obligation to pray behind any ruler (amir) for the two Eid prayers and Friday prayer, and the duty of obedience to the sultan. The phrase 'وبراء [؟] حقاقه' is unclear, but the main point is that obedience to the sultan is a religious obligation (fard). Even if the ruler has a defect such as 'pierced ears' (possibly a metaphor for being a slave or having a blemish), obedience remains wajib. The author then states that rebellion with the sword or disobedience (al-'isyan) is not allowed. If the ruler is just, he receives the reward; if he is unjust, he bears the burden (wizr). Nonetheless, obedience is required in every circumstance. The author warns that whoever disobeys the sultan and does not give him his due (perhaps allegiance or tax) is a Khariji, a deviant sect that rebels against legitimate rulers. The proof is the Qur'anic verse commanding obedience to Allah, the Messenger, and 'those in authority' (ulu al-amr), which the author interprets as the sultans.

Key Terms
طاعة السلطان
الخارجي
أولي الأمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some Muslims believe it is permissible to rebel against an unjust ruler.
Correction: The passage states that it is not permissible to rebel against the sultan with the sword nor with disobedience, even if he is unjust. The reward or burden is on him, but obedience remains required.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on rebelling against a ruler even if he is unjust?
A) Permissible if the ruler is unjust.
B) Not permissible; obedience is required.
C) Only permissible if the ruler has pierced ears.
D) Permissible only if the ruler is just.

Key Takeaway
Obedience to the sultan is obligatory in all circumstances, and rebellion is forbidden because it leads to being among the Kharijites.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have always believed that rebelling against an unjust ruler is a form of justice. But this lesson calls that belief Kharijism. How will you reconcile your sense of justice with the command to obey even a pierced-eared ruler? Will you trust Allah's wisdom in this command over your own intuition?
?
If you were living under a ruler who is clearly unjust, would you still obey him in non-sinful matters? The passage says obedience is necessary in every circumstance. What is the condition of your heart when you consider that command? Are you willing to submit to it without emotional resistance?
?
The passage says if the ruler is unjust, the burden is on him. This means you can be obedient without bearing his sin. Does this free you from the anxiety of complicity? Or does it challenge your desire to actively fight injustice? Reflect on the difference between obedience and approval.

Refuting the Two Extremes on Faith
Refutation of Jabriyya and Qadariyya on faith being a gift.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why both the Jabriyya and Qadariyya positions on faith are incorrect according to Ahl al-Sunna.

Core Idea
Faith is neither solely from Allah nor solely from the servant—both extremes are wrong.

Imam Samarqandi begins by clarifying the correct stance on faith as a divine gift. He warns against two dangerous extremes: the Jabriyya who deny human responsibility and the Qadariyya who deny Allah's role. This lesson establishes the balanced Sunni position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the two extremes
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author uses the terms 'Jabriyya' and 'Qadariyya' as labels for the two extremes.
2
Identify the mistake of each group
Identify the specific error of the Jabriyya (denying action) and the Qadariyya (denying divine gift). Write them down in your own words.
3
Reflect on why both are problematic
Ask yourself: How does the Sunni position avoid both extremes? The commentary will help you see the balance.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة العاشرة: أما ما ذكرنا أن يرى أن الإيمان عطاء الله تعالى ولا يجوز لأحد أن يقول لا أو من حتى يعطيني الله تعالى الإيمان فإن هذا مذهب الجبرية ولا يجوز أيضاً لأحد أن يقول كله مني وليس فيه عطاء الله تعالى فإن هذا مذهب القدرية. اعلم أن الإيمان عطاء الله تعالى بفضله ورحمته لقوله تعالى {يجتبي إليه من يشاء ويهدي إليه من ينيب} وقوله تعالى {ذلك فضل الله يؤتيه من يشاء} وقوله تعالى {ولو شئنا لآتينا كل نفس هديها} وقوله تعالى {إن ينصركم الله فلا غالب لكم} وقوله تعالى {من يهد الله فهو المهتدي} وقوله تعالى {قل بفضل الله وبرحمته فبذلك فليفرحوا} وقوله تعالى {إنك لا تهدي من أحببت ولكن الله يهدي من يشاء} وقوله تعالى {ما كنت تدري ما الكتاب ولا الإيمان} وقوله {فإن يشأ الله يختم على قلبك ويمحو الله الباطل} وقوله تعالى {بل الله يمن على من يشاء} وقوله تعالى {بل الله يمن عليكم أن هداكم للإيمان إن كنتم صادقين} وقوله {والله يهدي من يشاء إلى صراط مستقيم} وعلى هذا آيات كثيرة. فمن قال أن الإيمان مخلوق أو غير مخلوق فينبغي له أن ينظر لأي شيء يقول. إن الإيمان معرفة بالقلب وإقرار باللسان. فما كان من فعل العبد فهو مخلوق وما كان من صفات الله تعالى فهو غير مخلوق. فإذا قال العبد لا إله إلا الله فقوله تحريك لسانه يقول لا إله إلا الله، ففعل العبد وصفته مخلوق، والله تعالى بجميع صفاته غير مخلوق. وفرق بين قول العبد الذي هو فعله وحركته وبين مقوله الذي هو صفته تعالى، وهو مثل القرآن وقراءته. قراءة القرآن فعل العبد وهو مخلوق، وذلك الذي يقرأ هو كلام الله تعالى غير مخلوق. فالقرآن الذي هو متلو مقروء غير مخلوق. وكذلك أيضاً الإقرار من العبد وهو فعل العبد فهو مخلوق، وتوفيق إقرار العبد من الله تعالى فهو غير مخلوق. ومعرفته من العبد والتعريف من الله تعالى. فما كان من العبد فهو مخلوق وما كان من الله فهو غير مخلوق. والضابط في هذه المسألة أن يقول: إن العبد مع جميع أفعاله مخلوق، والله تعالى بجميع صفاته غير مخلوق. وهذا كفاية.
The tenth issue: As for what we mentioned that he sees that faith is a gift of Allah Most High, and it is not permissible for anyone to say 'No' or 'if only until Allah gives me faith' because this is the madhhab of the Jabriyyah. And it is also not permissible for anyone to say 'it is all from me and there is no gift of Allah in it' because this is the madhhab of the Qadariyyah. Know that faith is a gift of Allah Most High by His bounty and mercy, by His saying: 'He chooses for Himself whom He wills and guides to Himself whoever turns to Him,' and His saying: 'That is the bounty of Allah which He gives to whom He wills,' and His saying: 'And if We willed, We would have given every soul its guidance,' and His saying: 'If Allah helps you, none can overcome you,' and His saying: 'Whom Allah guides, he is the guided one,' and His saying: 'Say: In the bounty of Allah and His mercy, in that let them rejoice,' and His saying: 'Indeed, you do not guide whom you love, but Allah guides whom He wills,' and His saying: 'You did not know what the Book is nor faith,' and His saying: 'Then if Allah wills, He will seal your heart and Allah will abolish falsehood,' and His saying: 'Rather, Allah bestows favor upon whom He wills,' and His saying: 'Rather, Allah bestows favor upon you that He guided you to faith, if you should be truthful,' and His saying: 'And Allah guides whom He wills to a straight path.' And on this there are many verses. So whoever says that faith is created or not created, he should look to what he is saying. Faith is knowledge in the heart and affirmation with the tongue. So what is from the act of the servant is created, and what is from the attributes of Allah Most High is uncreated. So when the servant says 'There is no god but Allah,' his statement is the movement of his tongue saying 'There is no god but Allah' — thus the act of the servant and his attribute are created, and Allah Most High with all His attributes is uncreated. And there is a difference between the statement of the servant, which is his act and movement, and His Statement, which is His attribute. And it is like the Qur'an and its recitation: the recitation of the Qur'an is the act of the servant and is created, and that which is recited is the speech of Allah Most High, uncreated. So the Qur'an which is recited and read is uncreated. Likewise, the affirmation from the servant is his act, so it is created, while the success of the servant's affirmation from Allah Most High is uncreated. And his knowledge from the servant and the teaching from Allah Most High. So whatever is from the servant is created, and whatever is from Allah is uncreated. And the rule in this issue is to say: The servant with all his actions is created, and Allah Most High with all His attributes is uncreated. And this is sufficient.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage defines the tenth issue: the nature of faith (iman) and its relationship to divine gift and human action. It is a long continuous argument. The author begins by refuting two extremes: the Jabriyyah (fatalists) who negate human responsibility by saying 'unless Allah gives me faith I cannot act', and the Qadariyyah (free-will proponents) who say faith is entirely from themselves with no gift from Allah. Both are rejected. Then, starting with 'اعلم' (know), the author establishes that faith is a gift from Allah by His grace and mercy, citing many Qur'anic verses. The verses emphasize that guidance is from Allah alone. After the proof from revelation, the author addresses the question: is faith created (makhluq) or uncreated (ghayr makhluq)? He says one must consider what faith is: it is knowledge in the heart (ma'rifa bil-qalb) and affirmation with the tongue (iqrar bil-lisan). The acts of the servant (like uttering the shahada, moving the tongue) are created, because they are the servant's actions and attributes. The attributes of Allah (like His giving of faith, His speech) are uncreated. The author gives the example of the shahada: the servant's utterance is his act and attribute, thus created; but the meaning (the word of tawhid) as an attribute of Allah is uncreated. He then compares this to the Qur'an: the recitation (qira'a) is the act of the servant, created; the recited Qur'an (al-Qur'an al-matluww al-maqru') is the speech of Allah, uncreated. Similarly, the servant's affirmation (iqrar) is his act, created; the divine tawfiq (success) enabling that affirmation is from Allah, uncreated. The servant's knowledge (ma'rifa) is his act, but the teaching (ta'rif) from Allah is uncreated. The summary rule (al-dabit) is: the servant with all his actions is created; Allah with all His attributes is uncreated. The author ends by saying this is sufficient.

Key Terms
الجبرية
القدرية
عطاء الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if faith is from Allah, humans have no role, or if it's from humans, Allah has no role.
Correction: The Sunni position affirms both: faith is a gift from Allah and an act of the servant.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group says 'it is all from me'?
A) Jabriyya
B) Qadariyya
C) Ahl al-Sunna
D) Murji'a

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna rejects both extreme determinism and extreme free will—faith is Allah's gift that the servant receives through action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you struggle to obey a command, do you ever find yourself thinking, 'I can't do it until Allah gives me the faith'? In light of this lesson, how is that excuse actually a form of Jabriyya? What is one step you will take today to actively seek Allah's gift while taking responsibility for your actions?
?
Do you ever feel proud of your good deeds as if they are entirely your own doing, forgetting that even the ability to act is a gift from Allah? How does this passage warn against that Qadariyya mindset? What can you do right now to express gratitude for that gift?
?
Think of an area of your faith where you lean too far toward either extreme—either blaming Allah for your lack of faith or taking full credit for your faith. Which extreme is your tendency, and how will you correct it today by embracing the balanced teaching of this passage?

Qur'anic Proof that Faith is a Gift
Qur'anic verses establishing faith as Allah's gift.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extensive Qur'anic evidence that faith is a gift from Allah by His grace and mercy.

Core Idea
Faith is purely a gift from Allah, as shown by numerous Qur'anic verses.

Imam Samarqandi provides a cascade of Qur'anic verses to cement the principle that faith is a divine gift. These verses cover guidance, favor, and the inability of humans to guide themselves. This lesson gathers the scriptural foundation for the Sunni position.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of verses
Read the Arabic passage with the verses. Notice the diversity of the verses cited. Then read the translation.
Try to identify common themes among the verses.
2
Notice the repeated themes
Pay attention to phrases like 'whom He wills' and 'guidance'. What do they tell us about who gives faith?
3
Summarize the key message
In your own words, summarize the main point that the author is proving with these verses.
This consolidates the learning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The Prophet (PBUH) could not guide even his beloved uncle; guidance is entirely Allah's. When you see a loved one distant from Islam, do you despair or rely on your own efforts? Will you from now on combine sincere dua with action, trusting that Allah alone grants guidance?

Faith and Disbelief

Created and Uncreated in Faith: The Sunni Distinction
Distinction between created and uncreated aspects of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how to distinguish between created and uncreated aspects of faith based on the servant's act versus Allah's attribute.

Core Idea
The servant's acts are created; Allah's attributes are uncreated—faith involves both.

Having established that faith is a gift, Imam Samarqandi addresses a critical question: is faith created or uncreated? He answers by defining faith as knowledge and affirmation, then distinguishing between the servant's action and Allah's attribute. He uses the analogy of the Qur'an and its recitation to clarify, and concludes with a comprehensive rule.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage defining faith and the distinction
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the definition of faith and the principle 'what is from the servant's act is created; what is from Allah's attribute is uncreated'.
2
Understand the example of the shahada
The author gives the example of saying 'There is no god but Allah'. Distinguish between the tongue's movement (act of servant, created) and the meaning (attribute of Allah, uncreated).
This is a concrete application of the principle.
3
Reflect on the Qur'an analogy
The analogy between the Qur'an and its recitation is crucial. Understand why recitation is created and the recited Qur'an is uncreated.
This helps in understanding the broader issue of the createdness of the Qur'an.
4
Memorize the final rule
The last sentence ('The servant with all his actions is created, and Allah with all His attributes is uncreated') is the concise summary. Commit it to memory.
This rule resolves the confusion about createdness.

Know that faith is a gift of Allah Most High by His bounty and mercy, by His saying: 'He chooses for Himself whom He wills and guides to Himself whoever turns to Him,' and His saying: 'That is the bounty of Allah which He gives to whom He wills,' and His saying: 'And if We willed, We would have given every soul its guidance,' and His saying: 'If Allah helps you, none can overcome you,' and His saying: 'Whom Allah guides, he is the guided one,' and His saying: 'Say: In the bounty of Allah and His mercy, in that let them rejoice,' and His saying: 'Indeed, you do not guide whom you love, but Allah guides whom He wills,' and His saying: 'You did not know what the Book is nor faith,' and His saying: 'Then if Allah wills, He will seal your heart and Allah will abolish falsehood,' and His saying: 'Rather, Allah bestows favor upon whom He wills,' and His saying: 'Rather, Allah bestows favor upon you that He guided you to faith, if you should be truthful,' and His saying: 'And Allah guides whom He wills to a straight path.' And on this there are many verses. So whoever says that faith is created or not created, he should look to what he is saying. Faith is knowledge in the heart and affirmation with the tongue. So what is from the act of the servant is created, and what is from the attributes of Allah Most High is uncreated. So when the servant says 'There is no god but Allah,' his statement is the movement of his tongue saying 'There is no god but Allah' — thus the act of the servant and his attribute are created, and Allah Most High with all His attributes is uncreated. And there is a difference between the statement of the servant, which is his act and movement, and His Statement, which is His attribute. And it is like the Qur'an and its recitation: the recitation of the Qur'an is the act of the servant and is created, and that which is recited is the speech of Allah Most High, uncreated. So the Qur'an which is recited and read is uncreated. Likewise, the affirmation from the servant is his act, so it is created, while the success of the servant's affirmation from Allah Most High is uncreated. And his knowledge from the servant and the teaching from Allah Most High. So whatever is from the servant is created, and whatever is from Allah is uncreated. And the rule in this issue is to say: The servant with all his actions is created, and Allah Most High with all His attributes is uncreated. And this is sufficient.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage defines the tenth issue: the nature of faith (iman) and its relationship to divine gift and human action. It is a long continuous argument. The author begins by refuting two extremes: the Jabriyyah (fatalists) who negate human responsibility by saying 'unless Allah gives me faith I cannot act', and the Qadariyyah (free-will proponents) who say faith is entirely from themselves with no gift from Allah. Both are rejected. Then, starting with 'اعلم' (know), the author establishes that faith is a gift from Allah by His grace and mercy, citing many Qur'anic verses. The verses emphasize that guidance is from Allah alone. After the proof from revelation, the author addresses the question: is faith created (makhluq) or uncreated (ghayr makhluq)? He says one must consider what faith is: it is knowledge in the heart (ma'rifa bil-qalb) and affirmation with the tongue (iqrar bil-lisan). The acts of the servant (like uttering the shahada, moving the tongue) are created, because they are the servant's actions and attributes. The attributes of Allah (like His giving of faith, His speech) are uncreated. The author gives the example of the shahada: the servant's utterance is his act and attribute, thus created; but the meaning (the word of tawhid) as an attribute of Allah is uncreated. He then compares this to the Qur'an: the recitation (qira'a) is the act of the servant, created; the recited Qur'an (al-Qur'an al-matluww al-maqru') is the speech of Allah, uncreated. Similarly, the servant's affirmation (iqrar) is his act, created; the divine tawfiq (success) enabling that affirmation is from Allah, uncreated. The servant's knowledge (ma'rifa) is his act, but the teaching (ta'rif) from Allah is uncreated. The summary rule (al-dabit) is: the servant with all his actions is created; Allah with all His attributes is uncreated. The author ends by saying this is sufficient.

Key Terms
مخلوق
غير مخلوق
فعل العبد
صفات الله
كلام الله
قراءة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that faith is entirely created or entirely uncreated, without distinction.
Correction: Faith has two aspects: the servant's acts (created) and Allah's attributes (uncreated).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of the servant's affirmation (iqrar)?
A) Uncreated because it is from Allah
B) Created because it is an act of the servant
C) Both created and uncreated
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The servant's actions, including his utterance and affirmation of faith, are created, while Allah's attributes, including His giving of faith and His speech, are uncreated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'La ilaha illa Allah' today, will you pause to realize that your tongue's movement is created, but the meaning you affirm is Allah's uncreated speech? How does this awareness change your reverence in that moment?
?
Your ability to say the shahada is a gift of tawfiq from Allah, which is uncreated. Have you ever sincerely thanked Allah for granting you this affirmation? Will you make it a daily practice to express gratitude for His enabling you to utter the words of faith?
?
If your faith includes both your own created effort and Allah's uncreated grace, can you ever boast about your iman? Take a moment to ask yourself: Do I sometimes feel proud of my faith as if it were my own achievement? How can I humble myself and acknowledge that every good act is from Allah?

Actions of Servants Are Created
Imam Samarqandi affirms that all human actions are created by Allah, refuting those who deny it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all human actions are created by Allah based on Qur'anic proofs, and that denying this is a serious innovation.

Core Idea
All human actions are created by Allah; none are eternal.

In this passage, Imam Samarqandi presents a foundational creedal point: the createdness of human actions. He clearly distinguishes between Allah's attributes (uncreated) and human deeds (created), and supports his claim with three clear Qur'anic verses. This lesson will help you grasp the reasoning and its importance for correct belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get a feel for its flow. Then read the literal translation. Notice the concise but powerful style.
2
Identify the main claim
Locate the central statement: 'the actions of the servants are created.' Then notice the contrast with Allah's attributes being uncreated.
3
Examine the three Qur'anic proofs
The author quotes three verses. Find each one and consider how each supports the claim. Reflect on why the third verse about Allah's power is especially strong.
The verses are: 37:96, 13:16, and a general verse about divine power (e.g., 2:20).
4
Understand the warning
Read the consequence: whoever denies this is an innovator (mubtadi'). Consider why this issue is so serious in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الحادية عشرة: وما ذكرنا من أنه ينبغي له أن يعلم أن أفعال العباد مخلوقة، فالله تعالى بجميع أفعاله وصفاته غير مخلوق، لأن أفعال العباد لم تكن قديمة بل الله خلقها. ويعلم أن الصلاة والزكاة والصيام والحج وجميع ما يفعله العبد فهو مخلوق لقوله تعالى {والله خلقكم وما تعملون} وقوله تعالى {الله خالق كل شيء} وقوله {والله على كل شيء قدير}. ومن لم يقل أفعال العباد مخلوقة فهو مبتدع. وهذه الحجة كفاية للعاقل.
The eleventh issue: And what we mentioned that it is necessary for him to know that the actions of the servants are created. So Allah Most High with all His actions and attributes is uncreated, because the actions of the servants are not eternal, rather Allah created them. And he knows that prayer, zakat, fasting, hajj, and all that the servant does are created by the saying of Allah: 'And Allah created you and what you do,' and His saying: 'Allah is the Creator of everything,' and His saying: 'And Allah is over all things competent.' And whoever does not say that the actions of the servants are created is an innovator. And this proof is sufficient for the intelligent.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage defines the eleventh issue: the actions of human servants are created (makhluqa). It begins by asserting that the servant's actions are created, while Allah with all His actions and attributes is uncreated. The reasoning: human actions are not eternal (qadima); rather, Allah creates them. The author specifically mentions acts of worship (prayer, zakat, fasting, hajj) and general actions, stating they are created. He provides three Qur'anic proofs: 'And Allah created you and what you do' (37:96), 'Allah is the Creator of everything' (13:16), and 'Allah is over all things competent' (2:20 etc.). Those who deny that human actions are created are labeled as innovators (mubtadi'). The author concludes that this proof is sufficient for the intelligent person.

?
