?
If denying that actions are created is a serious innovation, search your own heart: do you ever feel that your good deeds originate purely from your own will and effort, independent of Allah’s creation? How can you train yourself to attribute every success in worship back to Him?
?
This passage declares that the proof is sufficient for the intelligent. Are you among those who accept this truth with certainty, or do you harbor doubts? What step will you take today to internalize that your very ability to act is a gift from Allah, not a product of your own power?

The Intellect of Believers and Disbelievers Are Not Equal
Samarqandi asserts inequality of intellect between believers and disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Imam al-Samarqandi, the intellect of prophets and believers is fundamentally superior to that of disbelievers.

Core Idea
Faith grants a higher intellect.

This lesson presents a concise but profound assertion from Imam al-Samarqandi. Although the full argument is not preserved, the claim itself is clear: the intellect of believers is not equal to that of disbelievers. Let's examine this statement and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source once, then its literal translation. Notice the formal opening 'The thirty-fourth question'.
The passage is incomplete; only the opening sentence survives.
2
Identify key terms
Note the terms 'عقل' (intellect), 'الأنبياء' (prophets), 'المؤمنين' (believers), 'الكفار' (disbelievers). These are the central actors in the claim.
3
Understand the assertion
The author states that it is incumbent to know that the intellect of these groups is not equal. This is a doctrinal position, not a descriptive observation.
The text does not provide reasons, only the claim.
4
Reflect on theological significance
Consider why this inequality matters: it implies that faith itself transforms or elevates the intellect. This has implications for how we view knowledge and guidance.
This reflection stays within the bounds of the passage's claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة الرابعة والثلاثون: وما قلنا إنه ينبغي له أن يعلم أنه لا يكون عقل الأنبياء والمؤمنين وعقل الكفار مستويين. ) ولا يكون (
The thirty-fourth question: And we say that it is incumbent upon him to know that the intellect of the prophets and the believers and the intellect of the disbelievers are not equal. (And it is not...)
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage introduces the thirty-fourth question, which asserts an inequality between the intellect ('aql) of the prophets and believers and that of the disbelievers. The text is incomplete, but the opening statement clearly sets forth the claim that these intellects are not equal. The author likely intended to provide proofs or explanations, but only the initial declaration is present in the OCR. The statement itself indicates a theological position that faith elevates one's intellectual capacity or that the intellect of a believer is qualitatively superior due to guidance from God. The incomplete closing 'ولا يكون' suggests a continuation that was not captured.

Five Types of People and Their Final Abode
Samarqandi classifies people into five types and states their fate based on faith and repentance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five categories of people in this world according to Samarqandi and how their faith, repentance, and sin determine their eternal destiny.

Core Idea
Your final destination depends on faith, repentance, and the will of Allah.

Samarqandi presents a crucial classification of people based on their spiritual state at death. This classification helps us understand the nuanced Islamic view of salvation: not all sinners are equal, and repentance transforms one's fate. The passage also provides scriptural evidence from the Quran and hadith, particularly regarding intercession for major sinners.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the five types
Carefully read the Arabic and translation. List the five categories of people Samarqandi mentions. Notice the key terms for each.
The fifth category might be tricky: 'believing sinner who does not persist in repentance' means someone who sins but does not repent before death.
2
Understand the three possible fates
Samarqandi describes three outcomes: eternal Paradise, eternal Hell, or a temporary punishment followed by Paradise. Link each category to its fate.
The third outcome (under Allah's will) applies only to believers who die in major sins without repentance.
3
Analyze the scriptural evidence
Read the Quranic verses (4:48, 15:44) and the hadith about the seven gates. Understand how they support the ruling on major sinners and intercession.
The hadith shows that intercession is specifically for sinful Muslims who die unrepentant.
4
Reflect on the middle position
Contrast this view with extremes: that all Muslims go directly to Paradise or that any sin leads to eternal Hell. Samarqandi affirms Allah's justice and mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما قلنا انه ينبغي له ان يعلم ان الخلق في الدنيا على خمسة اوجه وهم مشرك ومنافق ومطبع[؟] بغير ذنب ومذنب مصر على التوبة ومؤمن مذنب غير مصر على التوبة اعلم ان من خرج من الدنيا مشركا منافقا يدخل النار ويخلد فيها ومن خرج من الدنيا بغير ذنب او خرج مع التوبة يدخل الجنة ويخالد فيها ومن عمل الكبائر وخرج من الدنيا بغير توبة فهو فى مشيئة الله تعالى ان شاء غفر له بفضله وان شاء عذبه بعدله بقدر ذنوبه ثم يدخله الجنة بفضله وما قلناه صحيح فى الكتاب والخبر لقوله تعالى ان الله لا يغفر ان يشرك به ويغفر مادون ذلك لمن يشاء وقوله تعالى لها سبعة أبواب لكل باب منهم جزء مقسوم ( قال ) رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قلت ياجبريل لمن هذا الباب الواحد فقال للمذنبين من امتك فبكى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ودخل منزله ولم يخرج سبعة ايام الا للصلاة ولم يكلم احدا حتى وعده الله الشفاعة وقال ان للنار سبعة ابواب باب منها لامتك من اصحاب الكبائر الذين خرجوا من الدنيا بغير توبة فيعذبهم الله على قدر ذنوبهم ثم يخرجون منها ويدخلون الجنة بفضله وببركة الايمان بفضلك وبشفاعتك وهذا كفاية للعاقل
And what we said: it is fitting for him to know that the creation in the world are of five types: polytheist, hypocrite, one purified without sin, one who persists in repentance despite sin, and a believing sinner who does not persist in repentance. Know that whoever leaves the world as a polytheist or hypocrite enters the Fire and abides therein forever. Whoever leaves the world without sin or leaves with repentance enters Paradise and abides therein forever. And whoever commits major sins and leaves the world without repentance is under the will of Allah Almighty: if He wills, He forgives him by His bounty; if He wills, He punishes him by His justice to the extent of his sins, then admits him to Paradise by His bounty. What we have said is confirmed in the Book and the Sunnah, for Allah Almighty says: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive association with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' (4:48). And He says: 'It has seven gates; for every gate is a designated portion' (15:44). The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'I said, O Jibril, for whom is this single gate?' He said: 'For the sinners among your ummah.' So the Prophet (ﷺ) wept and entered his house, not leaving for seven days except for prayer, and did not speak to anyone until Allah promised him intercession and said: 'Indeed, there are seven gates of Hell; one of them is for your ummah among the people of major sins who left the world without repentance. Allah will punish them to the extent of their sins, then they will come out of it and enter Paradise by His bounty, by the blessing of faith, by your merit, and by your intercession.' And this is sufficient for the intelligent.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a classification and theological ruling on the final destiny of five categories of people. The author begins by stating that people in this world are of five types: polytheist, hypocrite, one who leaves without sin (i.e., perfectly obedient or a child), a sinner who persists in repentance (so dies repentant), and a believing sinner who does not repent before death. He then explains their outcomes: polytheists and hypocrites are eternally in Hell. Those who die sinless or repentant enter Paradise eternally. Those who die in major sins without repentance are under Allah's will—either forgiven directly by grace or punished justly according to their sins, then ultimately admitted to Paradise by grace. He supports this with Qur'anic verses (4:48, 15:44) and a hadith about the seven gates of Hell, where one gate is specifically for sinners of the Prophet's ummah who die unrepentant; they will be punished then released through intercession. The author concludes that this is sufficient for the intelligent person.

Key Terms
مشرك
منافق
مطبع
مذنب
توبة
مشيئة
شفاعة
خلود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think all Muslims who sin will never be punished; others think they will be eternally punished.
Correction: This passage clarifies the intermediate position of Ahl al-Sunnah: believers who die in major sins without repentance are under Allah's will—He may punish temporarily then admit to Paradise, or forgive directly.

Checkpoint
According to Samarqandi, what is the fate of a believer who dies committing major sins without repentance?
A) He is eternally in Hell.
B) He is under Allah's will; He may forgive or punish temporarily then admit to Paradise.
C) He definitely enters Paradise without any punishment.
D) He is in a state of suspension forever.

Key Takeaway
A Muslim who dies in major sins without repentance is not necessarily eternally doomed; he is subject to Allah's will and may ultimately enter Paradise through mercy and intercession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading this lesson, consider your own life: which of the five categories do you most fear you belong to right now? If you are a believing sinner who has not repented from major sins, are you genuinely striving to repent, or are you complacent, assuming Allah will forgive you anyway?
?
The Prophet wept when he learned of the gate of Hell for his sinful ummah. Does your heart weep over your own sins? If not, what does that say about your awareness of Allah's justice and your need for His mercy?
?
This lesson teaches that even those punished in Hell for major sins will ultimately be brought out by Allah's bounty and the Prophet's intercession. How does this balance of fear and hope change the way you view your daily sins? Will you continue in sin hoping for intercession, or will it drive you to repent more sincerely?

The Three States and the Reality of Faith
Samarqandi defines the three human states and asserts the reality of iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that iman is a real state (haqiqah) and that a person is either a real believer, a real disbeliever, or a real hypocrite, and that major sins do not make iman metaphorical.

Core Idea
Iman is real; sin does not turn it into metaphor.

Samarqandi begins by establishing a fundamental categorization: every person falls into one of three real states. This sets the stage for his argument that iman is not diminished by sins, and that claiming otherwise is innovation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three states
Read the first part and note the three exclusive categories: believer, disbeliever, hypocrite. They are real, not metaphorical.
2
Understand the consequence
If someone does not have real iman, they have real kufr. So a sinner's iman is still real.
3
See the innovation
Anyone who says the sinner's iman is metaphorical is an innovator (mubtadi'). This is the key point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الأربعون: وما ذكرنا أنه ينبغي له أن يعلم أن الإيمان هو بالحقيقة لا بالمجاز، لأن الرجل لا يكون خارجا عن أحد الأحوال الثلاثة: إما أن يكون مؤمنا أو كافرا أو منافقا. فمن لم يكن له الإيمان بالحقيقة كان له الكفر بالحقيقة. فمن زنى أو قتل مسلما بغير حق أو شرب الخمر أو عمل باللواطة أو أخذ مال المسلم أو لم يصل أو ما أشبه ذلك، كان إيمانه صحيحا وهو مؤمن حقيقة. ومن قال إيمانه بالمجاز لا بالحقيقة فهو مبتدع. وهذا القائل لا يخرج من الحالين: إما أن يكفر المؤمن بالذنوب أو يعد الطاعة من الإيمان. فإن كان يعد الطاعة من الإيمان فهو مبتدع، وإن كان يكفر المؤمن بالذنوب ويقول الإيمان بالمجاز فقل له: لو كان الكافر صلى وصام ولم يزن ولم يسفك الدم وترك جميع المعاصي ولكنه لا يؤمن فيجب أن يقول كفره مجاز. فكما أن الكافر لا يخرج بأعمال الخير من الكفر بالحقيقة، فكذلك المؤمن لا يخرج من الإيمان الحقيقي بالذنوب والمعاصي. لأن الله تعالى سمى أهل المعاصي باسم الإيمان فقال: "توبوا إلى الله جميعا أيها المؤمنون" الآية. فإن قال: سَمَّاهُم الله تعالى بالمجاز فقد كفر، لأن المجاز لا يكون إلا من لا يعلم أنه مؤمن أو غير مؤمن، والله تعالى عالم بأن هذا المذنب بالحقيقة. فمن هذا قال: "توبوا إلى الله جميعا أيها المؤمنون" وما قال: "يا أيها الكافرون توبوا". والعبد لا يخلو من أحد الأحوال الثلاثة: إما أن يكون مؤمنا بالحقيقة أو كافرا بالحقيقة أو منافقا بالحقيقة.
The fortieth issue: And what we have mentioned: It is necessary for him to know that iman (faith) is in reality (haqiqah), not metaphorically (majaz). Because a person is not outside one of three states: either he is a believer, or a disbeliever, or a hypocrite. Whoever does not have iman in reality, has disbelief (kufr) in reality. So whoever commits zinā (adultery), or kills a Muslim unjustly, or drinks wine, or commits sodomy, or takes the property of a Muslim, or does not pray, or the like, his iman is sound and he is a believer in reality. Whoever says his iman is metaphorical, not real, is an innovator (mubtadi'). This speaker cannot escape one of two states: either he declares the believer a disbeliever due to sins, or he considers obedience as part of iman. If he considers obedience as part of iman, he is an innovator. And if he declares the believer a disbeliever due to sins and says iman is metaphorical, then say to him: If a disbeliever prays, fasts, does not commit zinā, does not shed blood, and abandons all sins, but does not believe, then he would have to say that his disbelief is metaphorical? Just as the disbeliever does not leave real disbelief by doing good deeds, so too the believer does not leave real iman by sins and disobedience. Because Allah called the people of sins by the name of iman: 'Turn to Allah altogether, O believers'. If he says: Allah called them metaphorically, then he has disbelieved, because metaphor (majaz) is only used by one who does not know whether he is a believer or not, and Allah knows that this sinner is in reality. For this reason He said 'O believers' and did not say 'O disbelievers, repent'. A servant is not free from one of three states: either he is a believer in reality, or a disbeliever in reality, or a hypocrite in reality.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof that iman is a real state (haqiqah) not merely metaphorical. The author begins by categorizing people into three exclusive states: believer, disbeliever, or hypocrite. If someone does not have real iman, they have real kufr. Therefore, a person who commits major sins like murder, adultery, drinking wine, etc., still has sound iman and is a real believer. Those who claim such a person's iman is metaphorical are innovators. The author then shows that such a position leads to one of two errors: either they make obedience a part of iman (which is innovation) or they declare believers disbelievers due to sins. The author refutes the latter by analogy: just as a disbeliever who does good deeds remains a real disbeliever, a believer who sins remains a real believer. He then cites the Quranic verse where Allah addresses sinners as 'O believers', commanding them to repent. If one claims this is metaphorical, they commit kufr because metaphor is used when the speaker is ignorant of the true state, but Allah knows the sinner's true state. Therefore, iman is real and not lost by sins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Major sins make a person a metaphorical believer or a disbeliever.
Correction: Sins do not change the reality of iman; a sinner remains a real believer.

Checkpoint
According to Samarqandi, how many real states can a person be in?
A) Two: believer or disbeliever
B) Three: believer, disbeliever, or hypocrite
C) Four: believer, disbeliever, hypocrite, or sinner
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Iman is a real state (haqiqah) and remains real even when a person commits major sins.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think honestly: when you fall into a major sin, do you feel like your iman is gone or that you are no longer a real believer? How does this passage force you to redefine your self-image and your relationship with Allah?
?
If iman remains real even after repeated sins, what does that demand of you regarding hope in Allah's mercy? Will you let this truth drive you to sincere repentance, or will you use it to justify complacency?
?
Do you secretly look down on believers who commit public sins, considering them less Muslim? How does this passage shatter that judgment and call you to see them as fellow mu'minun who need your brotherly support?

Refuting the Metaphorical View of Faith
Samarqandi refutes the metaphorical view through a dichotomy, an analogy, and a Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two errors of the metaphorical view and how the Quran proves iman is real for sinners.

Core Idea
If iman were metaphorical for sinners, then kufr would be metaphorical for pious disbelievers.

Samarqandi now dismantles the position that a sinner's iman is metaphorical. He shows that this view leads to either considering obedience part of iman or declaring believers disbelievers. Using a powerful analogy and a Quranic verse, he demonstrates the absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Examine the two options
The metaphorical view leads to one of two errors: either obedience is part of iman (innovation) or believers become disbelievers.
2
Understand the analogy
Just as good deeds do not make a disbeliever's kufr metaphorical, sins do not make a believer's iman metaphorical.
This is the core logical argument.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
Allah addresses sinners as 'O believers', commanding them to repent. If this were metaphorical, it would imply Allah is ignorant, which is impossible.
4
Conclude
The servant is always one of three real states; iman is never metaphorical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الأربعون: وما ذكرنا أنه ينبغي له أن يعلم أن الإيمان هو بالحقيقة لا بالمجاز، لأن الرجل لا يكون خارجا عن أحد الأحوال الثلاثة: إما أن يكون مؤمنا أو كافرا أو منافقا. فمن لم يكن له الإيمان بالحقيقة كان له الكفر بالحقيقة. فمن زنى أو قتل مسلما بغير حق أو شرب الخمر أو عمل باللواطة أو أخذ مال المسلم أو لم يصل أو ما أشبه ذلك، كان إيمانه صحيحا وهو مؤمن حقيقة. ومن قال إيمانه بالمجاز لا بالحقيقة فهو مبتدع. وهذا القائل لا يخرج من الحالين: إما أن يكفر المؤمن بالذنوب أو يعد الطاعة من الإيمان. فإن كان يعد الطاعة من الإيمان فهو مبتدع، وإن كان يكفر المؤمن بالذنوب ويقول الإيمان بالمجاز فقل له: لو كان الكافر صلى وصام ولم يزن ولم يسفك الدم وترك جميع المعاصي ولكنه لا يؤمن فيجب أن يقول كفره مجاز. فكما أن الكافر لا يخرج بأعمال الخير من الكفر بالحقيقة، فكذلك المؤمن لا يخرج من الإيمان الحقيقي بالذنوب والمعاصي. لأن الله تعالى سمى أهل المعاصي باسم الإيمان فقال: "توبوا إلى الله جميعا أيها المؤمنون" الآية. فإن قال: سَمَّاهُم الله تعالى بالمجاز فقد كفر، لأن المجاز لا يكون إلا من لا يعلم أنه مؤمن أو غير مؤمن، والله تعالى عالم بأن هذا المذنب بالحقيقة. فمن هذا قال: "توبوا إلى الله جميعا أيها المؤمنون" وما قال: "يا أيها الكافرون توبوا". والعبد لا يخلو من أحد الأحوال الثلاثة: إما أن يكون مؤمنا بالحقيقة أو كافرا بالحقيقة أو منافقا بالحقيقة.
The fortieth issue: And what we have mentioned: It is necessary for him to know that iman (faith) is in reality (haqiqah), not metaphorically (majaz). Because a person is not outside one of three states: either he is a believer, or a disbeliever, or a hypocrite. Whoever does not have iman in reality, has disbelief (kufr) in reality. So whoever commits zinā (adultery), or kills a Muslim unjustly, or drinks wine, or commits sodomy, or takes the property of a Muslim, or does not pray, or the like, his iman is sound and he is a believer in reality. Whoever says his iman is metaphorical, not real, is an innovator (mubtadi'). This speaker cannot escape one of two states: either he declares the believer a disbeliever due to sins, or he considers obedience as part of iman. If he considers obedience as part of iman, he is an innovator. And if he declares the believer a disbeliever due to sins and says iman is metaphorical, then say to him: If a disbeliever prays, fasts, does not commit zinā, does not shed blood, and abandons all sins, but does not believe, then he would have to say that his disbelief is metaphorical? Just as the disbeliever does not leave real disbelief by doing good deeds, so too the believer does not leave real iman by sins and disobedience. Because Allah called the people of sins by the name of iman: 'Turn to Allah altogether, O believers'. If he says: Allah called them metaphorically, then he has disbelieved, because metaphor (majaz) is only used by one who does not know whether he is a believer or not, and Allah knows that this sinner is in reality. For this reason He said 'O believers' and did not say 'O disbelievers, repent'. A servant is not free from one of three states: either he is a believer in reality, or a disbeliever in reality, or a hypocrite in reality.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof that iman is a real state (haqiqah) not merely metaphorical. The author begins by categorizing people into three exclusive states: believer, disbeliever, or hypocrite. If someone does not have real iman, they have real kufr. Therefore, a person who commits major sins like murder, adultery, drinking wine, etc., still has sound iman and is a real believer. Those who claim such a person's iman is metaphorical are innovators. The author then shows that such a position leads to one of two errors: either they make obedience a part of iman (which is innovation) or they declare believers disbelievers due to sins. The author refutes the latter by analogy: just as a disbeliever who does good deeds remains a real disbeliever, a believer who sins remains a real believer. He then cites the Quranic verse where Allah addresses sinners as 'O believers', commanding them to repent. If one claims this is metaphorical, they commit kufr because metaphor is used when the speaker is ignorant of the true state, but Allah knows the sinner's true state. Therefore, iman is real and not lost by sins.

Iman is Real: The Three States
Establishes the three human states and asserts iman is real despite sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the tripartite division of humans into believer, disbeliever, and hypocrite, and why iman remains real even for those who commit major sins.

Core Idea
Iman is real, not metaphorical; sinners remain true believers.

Before we can discuss the nature of iman, we must recognize that every person falls into one of three categories. Imam Samarqandi begins by establishing this foundational division and then directly addresses the question: can a believer who sins still be called a true believer? The following passage lays out the answer clearly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage once
Read the Arabic passage slowly, then read the translation. Notice the opening statement about the three states.
The passage begins with a strong claim: iman is real, not metaphorical.
2
Identify the three states
The author lists three states: believer, disbeliever, hypocrite. Understand why these three exhaust all possibilities.
A person is either a believer, a disbeliever, or a hypocrite.
3
Note the list of sins
The author gives examples of major sins (adultery, murder, etc.) and asserts that committing them does not negate iman.
Sins do not remove the reality of iman.
4
Recognize the innovator claim
Whoever says the sinner's iman is metaphorical is called an innovator. This sets up the refutation in the next lesson.
The passage ends with a clear verdict: that view is innovation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة الاربعون وما ذكرنا أنه ينبغي له أن يعلم أن الإيمان هو بالحقيقة لا بالمجاز، لأن الرجل لا يكون خارجا عن أحد الأحوال الثلاثة: أما أن يكون مؤمنا أو كافرا أو منافقا. فمن لم يكن له الإيمان بالحقيقة كان له الكفر بالحقيقة. فمن زنى أو قتل مسلما بغير حق أو شرب الخمر أو عمل باللواطة أو أخذ مال المسلم أو لم يصل أو ما أشبه ذلك كان إيمانه صحيحا وهو مؤمن حقيقة. ومن قال إيمانه بالمجاز لا بالحقيقة فهو مبتدع. وهذا القائل لا يخرج من الحالين: أما أن يكفر المؤمن بالذنوب أو يعد الطاعة من الإيمان. فان كان يعد الطاعة من الإيمان فهو مبتدع، وان كان يكفر المؤمن بالذنوب ويقول الإيمان بالمجاز فقل له: لو كان الكافر صلى وصام ولم يزن ولم يسفك الدم وترك جميع المعاصي ولكنه لا يؤمن فيجب أن يقول كفره مجاز. فكما أن الكافر لا يخرج بأعمال الخير من الكفر بالحقيقة، فكذلك المؤمن لا يخرج من الإيمان الحقيقي بالذنوب والمعاصي. لأن الله تعالى سمى أهل المعاصي باسم الإيمان فقال: "توبوا إلى الله جميعا أيها المؤمنون" الآية. فان قال سماهم الله تعالى بالمجاز فقد كفر، لأن المجاز لا يكون إلا ممن لا يعلم أنه مؤمن أو غير مؤمن، والله تعالى عالم بأن هذا المذنب بالحقيقة. فمن هذا قال "توبوا إلى الله جميعا أيها المؤمنون" وما قال "يا أيها الكافرون توبوا". والعبد لا يخلو من أحد الأحوال الثلاثة: أما أن يكون مؤمنا بالحقيقة أو كافرا بالحقيقة أو منافقا بالحقيقة. فان كان المؤمن قدرا تكب المعاصي ثم تاب غفر الله له، وان كان مات بغير توبة فهو في مشيئة الله تعالى: إن شاء عذبه بعدله وإن شاء غفر له بفضله. والمنافق أشر من الكافر. فمن قال في الإيمان غير ما قلنا فهو مبتدع. وهذا كفاية للعاقل والله تعالى أعلم.
The fortieth question: And what we mentioned: That he should know that iman is in reality (bi-l-haqiqa), not metaphorically (bi-l-majaz), because a person does not fall outside one of three states: either he is a believer, a disbeliever, or a hypocrite. Whoever does not have iman in reality has disbelief in reality. So whoever commits adultery, kills a Muslim unjustly, drinks wine, practices sodomy, takes a Muslim's property, does not pray, or similar, his iman is sound and he is a believer in reality. Whoever says his iman is metaphorical, not real, is an innovator. This speaker does not escape one of two states: either he declares the believer a disbeliever due to sins, or he regards obedience as part of iman. If he regards obedience as part of iman, he is an innovator; if he declares the believer a disbeliever due to sins and says iman is metaphorical, then say to him: If a disbeliever prays, fasts, does not commit adultery, does not shed blood, and abandons all sins, but he does not believe, then he must say that his disbelief is metaphorical. Just as the disbeliever does not exit from real disbelief by good deeds, likewise the believer does not exit from real iman by sins and disobedience. Because Allah Most High called the people of sins by the name of iman, saying: 'Repent to Allah all of you, O believers' (Quran 24:31). If he says Allah called them metaphorically, he has disbelieved, because metaphor is only from one who does not know whether he is a believer or not, and Allah Most High knows truly that this sinner is a sinner in reality. Therefore He said: 'Repent to Allah all of you, O believers' and did not say 'O disbelievers, repent'. And the servant does not escape one of three states: either he is a believer in reality, a disbeliever in reality, or a hypocrite in reality. If the believer commits sins then repents, Allah forgives him; if he dies without repentance, he is under Allah's will: if He wills, He punishes him by His justice, and if He wills, He forgives him by His bounty. The hypocrite is worse than the disbeliever. Whoever says about iman other than what we said is an innovator. And this is sufficient for the intelligent person, and Allah Most High knows best.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition on the nature of iman (faith), arguing that it is real (haqiqa) and not metaphorical (majaz). The author presents a tripartite classification of humans: believer, disbeliever, hypocrite. He asserts that if a person does not have iman in reality, then he has disbelief in reality. Sins do not negate the reality of iman; a sinner remains a true believer. The author then identifies two erroneous positions of those who say iman is metaphorical: either they consider major sins as removing iman (making the believer a disbeliever) or they include acts of obedience as part of iman. Both are rejected. To refute the claim that iman is metaphorical for sinners, the author uses a parallel argument: if a disbeliever performs good deeds, we do not say his disbelief becomes metaphorical; similarly, sins do not make a believer's iman metaphorical. He then cites the Quranic verse calling sinners 'believers' (24:31) and argues that if Allah called them metaphorically, that would imply ignorance, which is impossible for Allah. The passage concludes that the fate of a sinner who dies without repentance is in Allah's will—He may punish or forgive. The hypocrite is worse than a disbeliever. Anyone who opposes this teaching is an innovator.

حقيقة
مجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Committing major sins completely removes iman, making the person a disbeliever.
Correction: The passage affirms that even one who commits such sins is a true believer, and his iman remains sound.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, a Muslim who commits murder or adultery is considered:
A) A disbeliever in reality
B) A believer metaphorically
C) A believer in reality
D) A hypocrite

Key Takeaway
Every person is either a true believer or a true disbeliever, and major sins do not make a believer's iman metaphorical.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that your iman remains real even if you commit major sins. Does this truth comfort you into continuing in sin, or does it drive you to repent out of gratitude? What is your heart's response right now?
?
If iman is truly real and not metaphorical, then your identity as a believer is secure. But are you living as if that identity demands nothing from you? Examine your life: where are you treating your iman as if it were merely metaphorical by neglecting its requirements?
?
The passage says whoever says a sinner's iman is metaphorical is an innovator. Have you ever secretly doubted the iman of a fellow Muslim who committed a sin you find severe? How does this passage challenge your judgment of others?

Refuting the Metaphorical View: Arguments and Proof
Refutes the metaphorical view using logical parallel and Quranic verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed refutation of those who claim iman is metaphorical, including the parallel argument from a disbeliever's good deeds and the Quranic verse calling sinners 'believers'.

Core Idea
Allah Himself calls sinners 'O believers,' proving their iman is real.

Having established that iman is real even for sinners, Imam Samarqandi now refutes the innovators who insist it is metaphorical. He exposes their two possible positions, destroys them with a powerful parallel argument, and seals the case with a direct Quranic verse. This passage consolidates the doctrine with both reason and revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the second passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the structure: two erroneous positions, then a parallel argument, then a verse.
The passage is more argumentative than the first.
2
Identify the two positions of the innovator
The author says the innovator either declares believers disbelievers due to sins, or includes obedience in iman. Both are wrong.
The innovator cannot escape these two errors.
3
Understand the parallel argument
If a disbeliever does good deeds, we don't say his disbelief becomes metaphorical. Similarly, sins don't make iman metaphorical.
This is a logical reductio ad absurdum.
4
Analyze the Quranic proof
Allah addresses sinners as 'O believers' (24:31). If this were metaphorical, it would imply ignorance—impossible for Allah.
The verse is a decisive textual proof.
5
Note the final rulings
The passage concludes with the fate of sinners (under Allah's will) and the statement that the hypocrite is worse than the disbeliever.
This completes the doctrine.

Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition on the nature of iman (faith), arguing that it is real (haqiqa) and not metaphorical (majaz). The author presents a tripartite classification of humans: believer, disbeliever, hypocrite. He asserts that if a person does not have iman in reality, then he has disbelief in reality. Sins do not negate the reality of iman; a sinner remains a true believer. The author then identifies two erroneous positions of those who say iman is metaphorical: either they consider major sins as removing iman (making the believer a disbeliever) or they include acts of obedience as part of iman. Both are rejected. To refute the claim that iman is metaphorical for sinners, the author uses a parallel argument: if a disbeliever performs good deeds, we do not say his disbelief becomes metaphorical; similarly, sins do not make a believer's iman metaphorical. He then cites the Quranic verse calling sinners 'believers' (24:31) and argues that if Allah called them metaphorically, that would imply ignorance, which is impossible for Allah. The passage concludes that the fate of a sinner who dies without repentance is in Allah's will—He may punish or forgive. The hypocrite is worse than a disbeliever. Anyone who opposes this teaching is an innovator.

Key Terms
إيمان
مجاز
مؤمن
كافر
منافق
ذنب
طاعة
مشيئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic address 'O believers' to sinners is metaphorical, not real.
Correction: The passage argues that if it were metaphorical, Allah would be ignorant of their true state—impossible. Therefore, their iman is real.

Checkpoint
What is the parallel argument used in this passage?
A) A believer's good deeds make his iman metaphorical
B) A disbeliever's good deeds do not make his disbelief metaphorical
C) A hypocrite is worse than a disbeliever
D) Repentance removes all sins

Key Takeaway
Allah calls sinners 'believers' in the Quran, proving their iman is real, and any claim of metaphor is refuted by logic and revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you knew a fellow Muslim had fallen into a major sin, would you be quick to view them as less of a believer? How can the logical parallel (disbeliever with good deeds remains disbeliever) and the Quranic address reshape your view of them and your own responsibility?
?

Definition of Iman: Heart and Tongue
Samarqandi defines iman as knowledge in the heart and confession on the tongue, with an exception for the mute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the essential components of iman according to Imam al-Samarqandi: knowledge in the heart and confession on the tongue, and the rulings for those who lack one component.

Core Idea
True iman requires both heart knowledge and tongue confession; lacking either makes one a hypocrite or disbeliever.

Imam al-Samarqandi begins by grounding the definition of iman in its two essential pillars: the heart and the tongue. He then clarifies exceptions and consequences for those who fall short, distinguishing believers from hypocrites and disbelievers. This passage gives a clear, practical criterion for assessing faith in both inner conviction and outward expression.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source once, then its translation. Note how the author defines iman and the exceptions he mentions.
Pay attention to the terms 'ma'rifa' (knowledge) and 'iqrar' (confession).
2
Identify the two components of iman
Find where the text states that iman is 'knowledge in the heart' and 'confession on the tongue'. Notice the exception for the mute.
The tongue does not benefit without the heart.
3
Understand the three categories of people
The passage distinguishes three groups: believers (both heart and tongue), hypocrites (tongue only), and disbelievers (heart only without tongue). List each and their outcomes.
This is a key doctrinal point.
4
Reflect on the sufficiency of the definition
The author concludes that this explanation of iman as confession by tongue and affirmation by heart is sufficient for the intelligent. Consider why this clarity matters.
5
Test your understanding with the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to ensure you can identify the status of someone who knows in the heart but does not confess with the tongue.
The answer is directly from the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة الثالثة والاربعون
وما قلنا انه ينبغي للمؤمن ان يعلم ان الايمان على الجارحتين على القلب واللسان الامن كان له عذر بان كان الكن ولا ينفع بغير قلب في حال والايمان هو معرفة الله تعالى بوحدانيته بالقلب والاقرار باللسان بوخدانيته لانه واحد ليس شيء وهو السميع البصير فهذا هوراس الايمان فمن اقربا باللسان ولم يقر بالقلب فهو منافق ومن عرف الله تعالى بالقلب ولم يقر باللسان فهو كافر باله ( واعلم) ان الایمان اقرار باللسان وتصديق بالقلب وهذا كفاية للعاقل
Issue forty-three: And we said that it is befitting for the believer to know that iman is upon the two limbs: the heart and the tongue, except for one who has an excuse such as being mute, and it (the tongue) does not benefit without the heart in any case. And iman is knowledge of Allah Almighty in His oneness by the heart and confession by the tongue of His oneness, because He is One, there is nothing like Him, and He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing. So this is the head of iman. So whoever confesses by the tongue but does not affirm in the heart is a hypocrite. And whoever knows Allah Almighty in the heart but does not confess by the tongue is a disbeliever in Him. (And know) that iman is confession by the tongue and affirmation (tasdiq) by the heart. And this is sufficient for the intelligent.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage defines iman (faith) in terms of its essential components. The author states that iman is connected to two bodily organs: the heart and the tongue, except for someone with a valid excuse like muteness, where the tongue is not required. Iman is defined as knowledge (معرفة) of Allah's oneness in the heart and verbal confession (إقرار) by the tongue of that oneness. This is called the 'head of iman' (رأس الإيمان). The passage distinguishes three categories: one who confesses with the tongue but does not affirm in the heart is a hypocrite (منافق); one who knows in the heart but does not confess with the tongue is a disbeliever (كافر); only combined confession and affirmation constitute true iman. The author reiterates that iman is confession by the tongue and affirmation (تصديق) by the heart, which suffices for the intelligent.

Misconception: Some think that mere verbal confession (shahada) without inner conviction is sufficient for iman.
Correction: The text requires both knowledge in the heart and confession with the tongue; tongue alone makes one a hypocrite.

Checkpoint

B) He is a hypocrite.

Key Takeaway

Correct Belief about Iman: Refutation of Erroneous Views
Samarqandi refutes sectarian positions on iman and affirms the correct Ahl al-Sunnah view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various deviant definitions of iman refuted by Imam al-Samarqandi and the correct Ahl al-Sunnah position that iman is affirmation by the tongue and belief in the heart.

Core Idea
Iman is affirmation by tongue and belief in heart; all other definitions are misguided.

This passage presents a series of refutations of sectarian positions on the nature of iman. Imam al-Samarqandi systematically identifies each erroneous view, labeling its proponents, and then declares them all misguided. He concludes with the correct view that defines iman as both verbal affirmation and heartfelt belief.

Guided Path
1
Identify the erroneous positions
Read through the passage and note each erroneous definition of iman. Look for the pattern: each is attributed to a specific group (Jahmi, Karrami, Murji'a, etc.).
There are six distinct erroneous positions listed.
2
Understand the labels
Familiarize yourself with the names: Jahmi (followers of Jahm bin Safwan), Karrami (followers of Muhammad bin Karram), Murji'a (those who postpone judgment), and others. Each label indicates a specific theological error.
The labels are used as shorthand for their respective doctrines.
3
Notice the pattern
Observe that each error either omits a component of iman or misplaces it. For example, the Jahmi omits the tongue, the Karrami omits the heart, and the Murji'a omits inner knowledge.
The correct definition includes both tongue and heart.
4
Why adding action is innovation
Samarqandi states that whoever says iman includes action with the limbs is a mubtadi' (innovator). Reflect on why this view is considered extreme, as it makes salvation conditional on external deeds.
This does not mean deeds are unimportant, but they are not part of the definition of iman.
5
Learn the correct definition
The passage concludes with the correct view: iman is affirmation by the tongue (iqrar) and belief in the heart (tasdiq). This is the position of Ahl al-Sunnah.
Samarqandi says this is sufficient for the intelligent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة الرابعة والاربعون: وما قلنا انه ينبغي له ان يعلم ان من عرف الله تعالى بالقلب ولم يعرفه باللسان فهو كافر ومن أقر باللسان ولم يعرفه بالقلب فهو منافق ومن قال ان الايمان على القلب دون اللسان فهو جهمي ومن قال ان الايمان على اللسان دون القلب فهو كرامي ومن قال ان الايمان قول باللسان بغير معرفة بالقلب فهو من المرجئة ومن قال ان الايمان هو معرفة بالقلب بغير اقرار باللسان وتصديق بالقلب فهو كاهل الكتاب يعرفونه ولا يقرون به ولا يصدقونه ومن قال ان الايمان هو اقرار باللسان ومعرفة بالقلب وعمل بالجوارح فهو مبتدع ومن قال ان الايمان هو معرفة بالقلب بغير اقرار باللسان وتصديق بالقلب فهو جهمي وهؤلاء كلهم ضالون والصواب في ذلك ان يعلم ان الايمان هو اقرار باللسان وتصديق بالقلب وهذا كفاية للعاقل والله اعلم بالصواب
The forty-fourth question: And we said that it is necessary for him to know that whoever knows Allah, the Exalted, in the heart but does not know Him with the tongue is a disbeliever, and whoever affirms with the tongue but does not know Him in the heart is a hypocrite. And whoever says that iman is upon the heart without the tongue is a Jahmi. And whoever says that iman is upon the tongue without the heart is a Karrami. And whoever says that iman is speech with the tongue without knowledge in the heart is of the Murji'a. And whoever says that iman is knowledge in the heart without affirmation by the tongue and belief in the heart is like the People of the Book: they know him but do not affirm him and do not believe him. And whoever says that iman is affirmation by the tongue, knowledge in the heart, and action with the limbs is a mubtadi' (innovator). And whoever says that iman is knowledge in the heart without affirmation by the tongue and belief in the heart is a Jahmi. All of these are misguided. And the correct in that is to know that iman is affirmation by the tongue and belief in the heart. And this is sufficient for the intelligent. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (radd) of various sectarian positions on the definition of iman. Imam al-Samarqandi lists erroneous views: 1) The Jahmi position: iman is only in the heart, not requiring the tongue. 2) The Karrami position: iman is only on the tongue, not the heart. 3) The Murji'a position: iman is mere speech without inner knowledge. 4) The view imitating the People of the Book: they know the truth but do not affirm or believe. 5) The view that adds action to the components of iman (this is a bid'a according to Samarqandi, though some later scholars differed). 6) Another Jahmi view (repeated for emphasis). He declares all these groups as misguided (dallun). Then he states the correct (sawab) view: iman is affirmation by the tongue and tasdiq (belief) in the heart. This is the Ahl al-Sunnah position. He concludes by saying this suffices for the intelligent.

Key Terms
جهمي
كرامي
مرجئة
مبتدع
ضالون
إيمان
إقرار
تصديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that including action in the definition of iman is correct and necessary.
Correction: Samarqandi explicitly labels the view that iman includes action as innovation (bid'a). The correct definition comprises only tongue affirmation and heart belief.

Checkpoint
According to Samarqandi, which group says that iman is only on the tongue without the heart?
A) Jahmi
B) Karrami
C) Murji'a
D) People of the Book

Key Takeaway
Iman is defined as affirmation by the tongue and heartfelt belief, and any deviation from this is misguidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
You are surrounded by people who may claim faith but lack inner conviction, or who have inner conviction but never express it. Which person are you? Take a moment to examine your own heart and tongue—do they match as this lesson demands? What will you change today to ensure your iman is genuine?

The Obligation of Kasb and Its Rulings
Samarqandi establishes the obligation of kasb and warns against denial and misattribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that kasb (earning) is an obligation at certain times, and that denying its obligation or attributing provision to earning constitutes disbelief or polytheism.

Core Idea
Kasb is obligatory at times; denying it is disbelief, and seeing provision from it is polytheism.

Imam al-Samarqandi addresses the necessity of earning a livelihood. He clarifies that while earning can be obligatory in specific circumstances, it must be understood correctly to avoid falling into disbelief. This passage defines the boundaries of belief regarding kasb.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim about kasb's obligation
Read the Arabic passage once. Notice that Samarqandi states 'kasb is obligatory in some times' and then provides evidence.
The evidence includes the verse to Maryam and the phrase 'made the day a means of livelihood'.
2
Contrast the rulings: concession vs. innovation
The passage says abandoning kasb is a concession (rukhsa) but denying it is innovation (bid'a). Understand the difference.
Denying the obligation leads to disbelief, as stated clearly.
3
Understand the extreme warning against attributing provision to earning
Whoever sees provision (rizq) from earning itself has disbelieved and is called a polytheist. This is a strong rejection of causal attribution.
This connects to the broader Islamic doctrine that provision is from Allah alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة السابعة والاربعون: وما قلنا انه ينبغي له ان يعلم ان الكسب يفترض فى بعض الاوقات لان الله تعالى اومي الى مريم وقال وهزي اليك بجذع النخلة وجعل النهار معاشا وأعلم ان ترك الكسب رخصة وانكار الكسب بدعة فمن انكره فهو كافر ومن رأى الرزق من الكسب فقد كفر ويسمى مشركا وينبغي ان يكون الكسب تحت اليقين والتوكل على اليقين تمنى لم يكن الكسب تحت اليقين كان كفرا لانه تعالى قال الله الذي خلقكم ثم رزقكم ثم يمينكم ثم يحيكم واعلم ان المكسب لا يزيد في الرزق ولا ينقص رزق من ترك الكسب وان الله تعالى لا ينقص من رزق المى لاسائنه ولا يزيد فى رزق المحسن لاحسانه لان الله تعالى قال وقدر فيها اقواتها في اربعة ايام سواء للسائلين وقال تعالى فورب السماء والأرض الآية حدثنا الثقات بإسنادهم عن ابن عباس عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال من لم ير الكسب فريضة على نفسه بمنزلة الصلاة والصوم فهو مبتدع قيل لابن عباس اي الكسب افضل
The forty-seventh question: And we said that it is necessary for him to know that earning (kasb) is obligatory in some times, because Allah, the Exalted, gestured to Maryam and said: 'And shake the trunk of the palm tree towards you' (Q 19:25), and made the day a means of livelihood (ma'ash). And know that abandoning earning is a concession (rukhsa), and denying earning is innovation (bid'a). So whoever denies it is a disbeliever. And whoever sees provision (rizq) from earning has disbelieved and is called a polytheist (mushrik). And it is necessary that earning be under certainty (yaqin) and trust (tawakkul). If earning is not under certainty, it is disbelief, because He, the Exalted, said: 'Allah is the One who created you, then provided for you, then will cause you to die, then will bring you to life' (Q 30:40). And know that earning does not increase provision, nor does it decrease provision from one who abandons earning. And Allah, the Exalted, does not decrease the provision of the wrongdoer for his wrongdoing, nor does He increase the provision of the good-doer for his good deeds, because Allah, the Exalted, said: 'And He determined therein their sustenance in four days, equal for those who ask' (Q 41:10). And He, the Exalted, said: 'So by the Lord of the heaven and the earth...' (Q 51:23). Trustworthy narrators narrated to us with their chain from Ibn 'Abbas from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Whoever does not consider earning a duty upon himself like prayer and fasting is an innovator.' Ibn 'Abbas was asked: 'Which earning is best?'
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal instruction on kasb (earning a livelihood). Imam al-Samarqandi states that it is necessary to know that kasb is obligatory (yufrad) at certain times. He provides evidence: Allah commanded Maryam to shake the palm tree (Q 19:25) and made the day for livelihood (Q 78:11). Abandoning kasb is a rukhsa (concession), but outright denial of its obligation is bid'a. He then warns: whoever denies kasb is a kafir; whoever believes that rizq (provision) comes from kasb itself (rather than from Allah) has committed kufr and is called a mushrik. He emphasizes that kasb must be accompanied by yaqin (certainty) and tawakkul (trust in Allah); if kasb is not under certainty, it becomes kufr. He supports this with a Quranic verse (Q 30:40) that links creation, provision, death, and resurrection to Allah alone. He further states that kasb does not increase or decrease predetermined rizq, nor does Allah change provision based on deeds. He cites Q 41:10 and Q 51:23 (the latter might be 'In the heaven is your provision' etc.). Then he narrates a hadith through Ibn 'Abbas that whoever does not consider kasb a duty like prayer and fasting is a mubtadi'. The passage ends with an incomplete question: 'Which earning is best?' This lesson covers the content up to the end of the window.

كسب
رخصة
بدعة
رزق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that earning guarantees provision or that provision comes from earning.
Correction: The passage states that whoever sees provision from earning has disbelieved and is called a polytheist; provision is from Allah alone.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of one who denies the obligation of kasb?
A) He is excused as long as he trusts Allah
B) He is an innovator and a disbeliever
C) He is merely mistaken
D) He is a hypocrite

Key Takeaway
Kasb can be obligatory, and denying its obligation or attributing provision to earning leads to disbelief or polytheism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Kasb under Certainty and Trust, Provision from Allah Alone
Samarqandi links kasb to tawakkul and refutes the idea that earning changes provision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that earning must be accompanied by certainty and trust in Allah, and that earning does not increase provision, as supported by Quranic verses and a hadith.

Core Idea
Earning is valid only with trust; provision is from Allah alone, not increased by effort.

After establishing the obligation of kasb, Imam al-Samarqandi now clarifies its proper spiritual context. Earning must be grounded in certainty (yaqin) and trust (tawakkul), otherwise it risks becoming disbelief. He also addresses a common misconception that earning increases provision, and cites a hadith emphasizing the duty of earning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the condition: earning under certainty and trust
The passage states that kasb must be under yaqin and tawakkul. If not, it is disbelief, supported by Quran 30:40.
Realize that action without reliance on Allah can become problematic.
2
Grasp that earning does not affect provision
Samarqandi asserts that kasb does not increase or decrease rizq; Allah's decree is fixed. Evidence from Quran 41:10 and 51:23.
This counters the notion that effort directly causes more provision.
3
Read the hadith about considering kasb a duty
The Prophet said whoever does not consider earning a duty like prayer and fasting is an innovator. This reinforces the seriousness of earning.
The passage ends with an incomplete question about the best earning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The forty-seventh question: And we said that it is necessary for him to know that earning (kasb) is obligatory in some times, because Allah, the Exalted, gestured to Maryam and said: 'And shake the trunk of the palm tree towards you' (Q 19:25), and made the day a means of livelihood (ma'ash). And know that abandoning earning is a concession (rukhsa), and denying earning is innovation (bid'a). So whoever denies it is a disbeliever. And whoever sees provision (rizq) from earning has disbelieved and is called a polytheist (mushrik). And it is necessary that earning be under certainty (yaqin) and trust (tawakkul). If earning is not under certainty, it is disbelief, because He, the Exalted, said: 'Allah is the One who created you, then provided for you, then will cause you to die, then will bring you to life' (Q 30:40). And know that earning does not increase provision, nor does it decrease provision from one who abandons earning. And Allah, the Exalted, does not decrease the provision of the wrongdoer for his wrongdoing, nor does He increase the provision of the good-doer for his good deeds, because Allah, the Exalted, said: 'And He determined therein their sustenance in four days, equal for those who ask' (Q 41:10). And He, the Exalted, said: 'So by the Lord of the heaven and the earth...' (Q 51:23). Trustworthy narrators narrated to us with their chain from Ibn 'Abbas from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, that he said: 'Whoever does not consider earning a duty upon himself like prayer and fasting is an innovator.' Ibn 'Abbas was asked: 'Which earning is best?'
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal instruction on kasb (earning a livelihood). Imam al-Samarqandi states that it is necessary to know that kasb is obligatory (yufrad) at certain times. He provides evidence: Allah commanded Maryam to shake the palm tree (Q 19:25) and made the day for livelihood (Q 78:11). Abandoning kasb is a rukhsa (concession), but outright denial of its obligation is bid'a. He then warns: whoever denies kasb is a kafir; whoever believes that rizq (provision) comes from kasb itself (rather than from Allah) has committed kufr and is called a mushrik. He emphasizes that kasb must be accompanied by yaqin (certainty) and tawakkul (trust in Allah); if kasb is not under certainty, it becomes kufr. He supports this with a Quranic verse (Q 30:40) that links creation, provision, death, and resurrection to Allah alone. He further states that kasb does not increase or decrease predetermined rizq, nor does Allah change provision based on deeds. He cites Q 41:10 and Q 51:23 (the latter might be 'In the heaven is your provision' etc.). Then he narrates a hadith through Ibn 'Abbas that whoever does not consider kasb a duty like prayer and fasting is a mubtadi'. The passage ends with an incomplete question: 'Which earning is best?' This lesson covers the content up to the end of the window.

Key Terms
يقين
توكل
رزق
فريضة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that working harder will increase their provision.
Correction: The passage clearly states that earning does not increase or decrease provision; rizq is predestined by Allah.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say about one who does not consider kasb a duty like prayer and fasting?
A) He is a disbeliever
B) He is an innovator
C) He is excused if he trusts Allah
D) He is a hypocrite

Key Takeaway
Earning must be coupled with trust in Allah, and it does not alter the provision Allah has decreed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you work to earn a living, do you honestly check your heart: is your earning under certainty (yaqin) that provision comes only from Allah, or do you feel anxious that your effort determines your sustenance? What would it take for you to truly believe that your income does not depend on your work but on Allah's decree?
?
The passage equates earning without certainty to disbelief. Is there any area of your earning—salary, business, side hustles—where you secretly believe that your success is your own doing and not entirely from Allah? How can you cultivate tawakkul in that sphere starting today?
?
You may know that provision is fixed, but do you actually live without worry about provision? If you lost your job tomorrow, would your trust in Allah remain intact, or would you panic? What concrete step can you take this week to strengthen your reliance on Allah rather than your savings or skills?

The Equality of Iman Among All Believers
Imam Samarqandi states the equality of iman across all believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Imam Samarqandi, the iman of all believers—righteous or sinful, angel or human—is essentially identical, and that denying this equality constitutes innovation.

Core Idea
The iman of every believer is identical in essence, regardless of deeds.

Imam Samarqandi tackles a crucial question: Does sin diminish one's faith? In this passage, he asserts unequivocally that the iman of the righteous and the sinner is equal, and he supports this with a Quranic verse that groups angels and believers together in the same testimony of tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to grasp the main claim.
Pay attention to the key terms: المحسن (righteous) and المسيء (evil-doer).
2
Identify the claim and refutation
Notice that Imam Samarqandi first states the equality of iman between the righteous and the evil-doer. Then he explicitly rejects the opposite view, calling it a lie and innovation.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
Look at the verse he cites (3:18). Reflect on how it links Allah, angels, and the people of knowledge (believers) in the same testimony. Why does this prove equality of iman?
The verse implies that the angels and believers share the same act of witnessing, which indicates their iman is the same.
4
Consider the broader implication
Ask yourself: If iman is equal, what differentiates believers? The answer lies in deeds and piety, not the essence of faith itself.
This lesson helps avoid the error of rejecting sinners as true believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وماقلنا انه ينبغي له ان يعلم ان ايتمان المحسن والمسئء سواء و ايمان جبریل و میکائیل وسائر الملائكة وايمان جميع الأنبياء والرسل وايماننا سواء فمن قال ان ايمان المي اقل من ايمان المحسن فقد كذب وهو مبتدع لان الله تعالى قال شهد الله انه لا اله الاهو والملائكة وأولوا العلم قائما بالقسط اراد به المؤمنين فمن قال ان الملائكة قالت هذا القول اكثر مما قال الله تعالى اواقل فهو مبتدع
And what we said: that he should know that the iman of the righteous (muhsin) and the evil-doer (musi') is equal; and the iman of Jibril, Mika'il, and the rest of the angels, and the iman of all the prophets and messengers, and our iman are equal. So whoever says that the iman of the evil-doer is less than the iman of the righteous has lied and is an innovator. Because Allah the Exalted said: 'Allah bears witness that there is no god but He, and the angels and the people of knowledge, standing in justice' (3:18). He intended thereby the believers. So whoever says that the angels said this statement more than what Allah said or less is an innovator.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage addresses the equality of iman (faith) among all believers regardless of their deeds. The Imam asserts that the iman of the righteous (muhsin, the one who does good) and the evil-doer (musi', the one who sins) is equal. This means the core belief (tasdiq) is identical. He extends this to include the iman of angels (Jibril, Mika'il, and all angels) and all prophets and messengers, and the iman of ordinary believers—all are equal. Whoever claims that the evil-doer's iman is less than the righteous person's has lied and is an innovator (mubtadi'). The proof is from Quran 3:18, where Allah, the angels, and the people of knowledge (ulul 'ilm) testify to tawhid. The 'people of knowledge' here are the believers. The angels and believers are joined in the same testimony, implying their iman is equal. If one were to claim that the angels' testimony is greater or lesser than what Allah said, that would be innovation. The point is that iman (the act of believing) is essentially the same in all believers; differences in action or knowledge affect piety but not the reality of iman itself.

Key Terms
المحسن
المسيء
جبریل
میکائیل
الملائكة
أولوا العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that iman increases and decreases with deeds, so the righteous have more iman than sinners.
Correction: Imam Samarqandi states that the iman of the righteous and the sinner is equal. Differences in deeds affect one's degree of piety (taqwa) but not the essence of faith (iman).

Checkpoint
According to Imam Samarqandi, what is the relationship between the iman of the righteous and the evil-doer?
A) The righteous have more iman than the evil-doer.
B) The evil-doer's iman is less because of sins.
C) Their iman is equal in essence.
D) The evil-doer has no iman if he sins.

Key Takeaway
The iman of every believer—whether righteous or sinful, angel or human—is identical in essence, and denying this is innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to have iman, but do you truly believe that your iman is identical to that of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him)? How does this affect your view of your own shortcomings and your hope in Allah's mercy?
?
When you see a Muslim committing major sins, do you consider their iman less than yours? What does this lesson demand you change in your heart towards them?
?
The angels bear witness to tawhid alongside you. Are you conscious that your testimony of 'La ilaha illa Allah' is the same as Jibril's? Does this elevate the weight you give to your own shahada?

Iman is Distinct from Action
Samarqandi argues that iman is separate from action using multiple proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Islamic theology distinguishes faith (iman) from actions, based on the arguments presented by Imam al-Samarqandi.

Core Idea
Faith is constant; actions are conditional. They are not the same.

This lesson examines a key issue in Islamic theology: is iman (faith) identical to action, or are they distinct? Imam al-Samarqandi presents several compelling proofs to separate the two. By working through his arguments, you will grasp an essential principle of Ahl al-Sunna belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get an overview of the argument. Notice the strong thesis statement at the beginning.
The passage is titled 'The forty-eighth issue', indicating it is a distinct topic.
2
Identify the thesis
Find the sentence where Samarqandi states that iman is other than action and action is other than iman. This is the central claim.
He also says not every obedience is iman, just as not every sin is kufr.
3
Examine the first proof
Read the proof based on the prophets: despite different laws, their iman was one. This shows iman is separate from their varied actions.
If iman were tied to action, prophets would have different degrees of iman, which is impossible.
4
Examine the remaining proofs
Work through the proofs about time, place, purity, and the afterlife. Each shows that iman is continuously valid while actions have conditions.
Examples: prayer before time is invalid, fasting before Ramadan is invalid, iman on a garbage heap is valid, prayer is not.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider the final statement: believers in Paradise have iman without action. This clinches the argument that iman and action are distinct.
Samarqandi ends with 'This is sufficient for what we said. And Allah knows best.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة الثامنة والاربعون وما قلنا انه ينبني له ان يعلم ان الايمان سوى العمل والعمل سوى الايمان وليس كل طاعة ايمانا كما ان الكفر معصية وليس كل معصية كفرا فان لكل نبي شرعة ومنهاجا يعني كان لكل في شريعة وامن سوى ما كان للآخر لان ايمان أحدهم سوى ايمان الاخر فلما كان ايمان الانبياء واحدا وشرائعهم مختلفة علم ان الايمان يباين العمل لانه لا يجوزان يكون لاحدهم ايمان كثير وللاخر قليل واما الدلائل فظاهرة ألا ترى ان الايمان على الدوام والعمل ليس على الدوام لان الرجل اذا صلى قبل وقت الصلاة فان الصلاة لا تجوز وكذلك اذا صام قبل شهر رمضان فانه لا يجوز صومه عن رمضان ولو كان كافرا و عمل جميع الخيرات والطاعات قبل ان يؤمن لا يصير مؤمنا لان الايمان قبل العمل والايمان على الدوام والعمل بالاوقات ومن جهة اخرى لو ان الكافر آمن على رأس المزبلة يجوز ايمانه واذا صلى على المزبلة فانه لا يجوز فلو كان العمل من الايمان لما جاز بعضه على النجاسة وبعضه لا يجوز وايضا لو ان امراة حائضا او رجلا جنبا آمن يجوز ايمانه وان صلى على مثل هذه الحالة لا تجوز صلاته ألا ترى ان المؤمنين يكونون في الجنة مؤمنين بغير عمل فقد ظهر ان الايمان يباين العمل وهذا كفاية لما قل والله اعلم
The forty-eighth issue: And we said that he should know that faith (al-iman) is other than action (al-`amal) and action is other than faith, and not every obedience is faith just as disbelief (al-kufr) is disobedience but not every disobedience is disbelief. For every prophet had a law and a way, meaning each had a law and security other than what was for the other, because the faith of one of them is other than the faith of the other. So when the faith of the prophets is one and their laws are different, it is known that faith is distinct from action, because it is not possible that one of them has much faith and another has little. As for the proofs, they are apparent: Do you not see that faith is continuous while action is not continuous? For if a man prays before the time of prayer, the prayer is not valid; similarly, if he fasts before the month of Ramadan, his fast is not valid for Ramadan. And if a disbeliever performs all good deeds and acts of obedience before he believes, he does not become a believer because faith precedes action. Faith is continuous, while action is tied to times. From another angle: if a disbeliever believes on top of a garbage heap, his faith is valid, but if he prays on a garbage heap, it is not valid. So if action were part of faith, some of it would be permissible on impurity and some would not. Also, if a menstruating woman or a man in a state of janabah believes, his faith is valid, but if he prays in such a state, his prayer is not valid. Do you not see that the believers will be in Paradise as believers without action? So it has become clear that faith is distinct from action. This is sufficient for what we said. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage presents an argument that faith (iman) and action (amal) are distinct entities. The author begins by stating the thesis: iman is other than amal, and amal is other than iman. He supports this by noting that not every act of obedience is iman, just as not every sin is kufr. He then gives a first proof based on the prophets: although each prophet had a different law (shari`ah) and a different level of security (amn?), their iman was one and the same, so iman cannot be the same as their varying laws and actions. Next, he offers several analogies to show that iman is continuous and timeless, while actions are conditional on time, place, and ritual purity. For example, prayer before its time is invalid, fasting before Ramadan is invalid, and actions performed before iman do not make one a believer. He also notes that iman is valid even on impure ground, whereas prayer is not. Finally, he points out that in Paradise, believers will be without actions, yet they remain believers. Thus iman is separate from action.

Key Terms
الإيمان (al-iman)
العمل (al-`amal)
الطاعة (al-ta`ah)
المعصية (al-ma`siah)
الشرعة (al-shir`ah)
المنهاج (al-minhaj)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Iman and action are identical; performing actions is faith itself.
Correction: The passage shows that iman is continuous and valid even without actions, while actions are conditional on time, place, and purity. Therefore, iman is distinct from action.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what aspect of iman distinguishes it from action?
A) Iman can increase and decrease
B) Iman is continuous while actions are tied to specific times and conditions
C) Iman is only valid after performing actions
D) Iman is the same as obedience

Key Takeaway
Iman is a constant state of belief in the heart, while actions are outward expressions that are bound by specific conditions; they are not the same.

The Equality of Iman Between Righteous and Wrongdoer
Samarqandi states the equality of iman and refutes the idea of lesser iman for wrongdoers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the essence of iman (faith) is identical for every believer, whether righteous or sinful, based on Quranic evidence and logical reasoning.

Core Idea
Iman is one; actions do not affect its essence.

Imam Samarqandi begins by asserting a fundamental principle of Sunni theology: the faith of the righteous and the wrongdoer is equal, as is the faith of angels, prophets, and ordinary believers. This lesson examines the first part of his argument, including the Quranic proof and the refutation of those who claim degrees in iman.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to get the gist.
Notice the strong opening assertion.
2
Identify the thesis and Quranic evidence
Find the central claim that iman of al-muhsin and al-musi' are equal. Then locate the verse (3:18) and see how it is used.
The verse is cited as proof.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Samarqandi concludes that faith is one. Ask yourself: why does he say the difference lies in actions, not iman?
This sets up the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة التاسعة والاربعون وما قلنا انه ينبغي له ان يعلم ان ايمان المحسن والمسيء سواء وايمان جبريل وميكائيل وسائر الملائكة وايمان جميع الانبياء والرسل وايماننا سواء فمن قال ان ايمان المسيء اقل من ايمان المحسن فقد كذب وهو مبتدع لان الله تعالى قال شهد الله انه لا اله الا هو والملائكة وأولوا العلم قائما بالقسط اراد به المؤمنين فمن قال ان الملائكة قالت هذا القول اكثر مما قال الله تعالى او اقل فهو مبتدع فان قلت المؤمن يقول اقل مما قالت الملائكة او اكثر فهو محال وان كنت تقول مثل ما قالت الملائكة فما الفرق بينك وبين الملائكة واعلم ان الملائكة فضلوا علينا بالاعمال والافعال لا بالايمان فان الايمان واحد وايضا قل للمخالف هل آمن جبريل باحد انت تؤمن به او آمن باحد انت لا تؤمن به فان آمن باحد انت لم تؤمن به فهذا لا يكون ايمانا بل يكون كفرا وان آمن باحد انت تؤمن به فايمانك وايمانه سواء ومن قال ان ايماننا خير من ايمان جبريل عليه السلام لان الله تعالى خلق جبريل واعطاه العقل ولم يعطه الشهوة وخلقنا واعطانا العقل والشهوة وامرنا بالصلاة والصوم والحج والزكاة والاغتسال من الجنابة فاذا ادينا هذا كله كان ايماننا خيرا من ايمان جبريل فهو مبتدع والله تعالى يقول فان آمنوا بمثل ما امنتم به فقد اهتدوا وايضا قل للمخالف ما قولك فى رجل قال لا اله الا الله محمد رسول الله وملك قال مثل هذا فهل يكونان كلاهما مؤمنين صادقين اولا او يكون احدهما صادقا والاخر كاذبا فان قال احدهما صادق والاخر كاذب فهو مبتدع وان قال هما مؤمنان صادقان فلا يكون بين ايمان الملك والرجل فرق فمن آمن بالله وبما امر الله به وبما انزل الله تعالى على محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم كان مؤمنا وان كان زانيا او شارب الخمر او قاتل المؤمن فايمانه وايمان الملائكة والنبيين سواء ومن قال غير هذا فهو مبتدع وفى هذا كفاية للعاقل والله اعلم
The forty-ninth issue: And we said that he should know that the faith of the righteous doer (al-muhsin) and the wrongdoer (al-musi') are equal, and the faith of Gabriel and Michael and the rest of the angels, and the faith of all the prophets and messengers, and our faith are equal. So whoever says that the faith of the wrongdoer is less than the faith of the righteous doer has lied and is an innovator (mubtadi`). Because Allah the Exalted said: 'Allah bears witness that there is no god but He, and the angels and those of knowledge, standing in justice' – He meant the believers. So whoever says that the angels said this statement more than what Allah the Exalted said or less is an innovator. For if you say that the believer says less than what the angels said or more, it is impossible; and if you say the like of what the angels said, then what is the difference between you and the angels? And know that the angels are superior to us in actions and deeds, not in faith, for faith is one. Also say to the opponent: Did Gabriel believe in someone you believe in, or did he believe in someone you do not believe in? If he believed in someone you do not believe in, that is not faith but disbelief; and if he believed in someone you believe in, then your faith and his faith are equal. And whoever says that our faith is better than the faith of Gabriel, because Allah created Gabriel and gave him intellect but did not give him desire, and created us and gave us intellect and desire and commanded us with prayer, fasting, Hajj, Zakat, and washing from janabah; so when we perform all this, our faith is better than Gabriel's faith – he is an innovator. And Allah the Exalted says: 'Then if they believe in the like of what you believed in, they have been guided.' Also say to the opponent: What do you say about a man who says 'La ilaha illa Allah, Muhammadun Rasul Allah' and an angel says the same – are both truthful believers, or is one truthful and the other lying? If he says one is truthful and the other lying, he is an innovator; and if he says both are truthful believers, then there is no difference between the faith of the angel and the man. So whoever believes in Allah and what Allah commanded and what Allah revealed to Muhammad (peace be upon him) is a believer, even if he is an adulterer or a drinker of wine or a killer of a believer. His faith and the faith of the angels and prophets are equal. And whoever says other than this is an innovator. In this is sufficient for the intelligent. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage argues that the faith (iman) of all believers – the righteous, the wicked, angels, and prophets – is identical in essence. The author starts by stating the thesis that iman of the good and bad are equal, and iman of angels, prophets, and ordinary believers are equal. He then refutes anyone who claims that the iman of a sinner is less than that of a righteous person, calling such a person a liar and an innovator (mubtadi`). He cites the Qur'anic verse (3:18) where Allah, the angels, and those of knowledge testify to His oneness, and argues that the angels and believers all utter the same testimony; any claim of difference in quantity is innovation. He then uses a logical argument: if you ask whether Gabriel (Jibril) believes in the same Object of faith as you do, if yes, then your iman is the same; if no, then his belief would be kufr. Therefore iman is one. He also refutes the notion that because humans have more obligations and desires, their iman is greater; instead, angels are superior in actions, not iman. Finally, he presents a scenario of a man and an angel both saying the shahadah: if their statements are identical, then their iman is identical. Thus a believer remains a believer even if he commits major sins, and his iman is equal to that of angels and prophets. Those who disagree are innovators.

Key Terms
الإيمان
المحسن
المسيء
المبتدع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The iman of a sinful believer is less than that of a righteous one.
Correction: Samarqandi argues that iman is identical in essence; the difference lies in actions, not faith.

Checkpoint
According to Samarqandi, what does the Quranic verse (3:18) demonstrate?
A) That angels have more faith than believers
B) That believers and angels bear the same testimony to Allah's oneness
C) That only prophets have true faith
D) That the faith of wrongdoers is incomplete

Key Takeaway
The essence of iman is identical for all believers; it is not increased or decreased by actions.

The Iman of Prophets, Angels, and Sinners: Refuting False Distinctions
Samarqandi presents logical arguments and a scenario to affirm the equality of iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute claims that prophets or angels have superior iman to ordinary believers, and understand that even major sins do not negate the equality of iman.

Core Idea
Faith is measured by belief, not by deeds or status.

In this second part of the discussion, Imam Samarqandi uses logical arguments and a scriptural proof to show that iman is the same for all, including Gabriel, other angels, prophets, and even sinners. He counters the idea that humans' greater obligations make their iman superior.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the series of logical questions and examples.
This passage is more argumentative.
2
Analyze the argument about Gabriel
Samarqandi asks whether Gabriel believes in the same object of faith as you. Work through the logic: if yes, faith is equal; if no, his belief would be disbelief.
This is a powerful reductio ad absurdum.
3
Consider the shahadah scenario
Imagine a man and an angel both saying the shahadah. If both are truthful, their faith is equal. This confirms the thesis.
The conclusion extends to sinners.
