المسئلة التاسعة والاربعون وما قلنا انه ينبغي له ان يعلم ان ايمان المحسن والمسيء سواء وايمان جبريل وميكائيل وسائر الملائكة وايمان جميع الانبياء والرسل وايماننا سواء فمن قال ان ايمان المسيء اقل من ايمان المحسن فقد كذب وهو مبتدع لان الله تعالى قال شهد الله انه لا اله الا هو والملائكة وأولوا العلم قائما بالقسط اراد به المؤمنين فمن قال ان الملائكة قالت هذا القول اكثر مما قال الله تعالى او اقل فهو مبتدع فان قلت المؤمن يقول اقل مما قالت الملائكة او اكثر فهو محال وان كنت تقول مثل ما قالت الملائكة فما الفرق بينك وبين الملائكة واعلم ان الملائكة فضلوا علينا بالاعمال والافعال لا بالايمان فان الايمان واحد وايضا قل للمخالف هل آمن جبريل باحد انت تؤمن به او آمن باحد انت لا تؤمن به فان آمن باحد انت لم تؤمن به فهذا لا يكون ايمانا بل يكون كفرا وان آمن باحد انت تؤمن به فايمانك وايمانه سواء ومن قال ان ايماننا خير من ايمان جبريل عليه السلام لان الله تعالى خلق جبريل واعطاه العقل ولم يعطه الشهوة وخلقنا واعطانا العقل والشهوة وامرنا بالصلاة والصوم والحج والزكاة والاغتسال من الجنابة فاذا ادينا هذا كله كان ايماننا خيرا من ايمان جبريل فهو مبتدع والله تعالى يقول فان آمنوا بمثل ما امنتم به فقد اهتدوا وايضا قل للمخالف ما قولك فى رجل قال لا اله الا الله محمد رسول الله وملك قال مثل هذا فهل يكونان كلاهما مؤمنين صادقين اولا او يكون احدهما صادقا والاخر كاذبا فان قال احدهما صادق والاخر كاذب فهو مبتدع وان قال هما مؤمنان صادقان فلا يكون بين ايمان الملك والرجل فرق فمن آمن بالله وبما امر الله به وبما انزل الله تعالى على محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم كان مؤمنا وان كان زانيا او شارب الخمر او قاتل المؤمن فايمانه وايمان الملائكة والنبيين سواء ومن قال غير هذا فهو مبتدع وفى هذا كفاية للعاقل والله اعلم
The forty-ninth issue: And we said that he should know that the faith of the righteous doer (al-muhsin) and the wrongdoer (al-musi') are equal, and the faith of Gabriel and Michael and the rest of the angels, and the faith of all the prophets and messengers, and our faith are equal. So whoever says that the faith of the wrongdoer is less than the faith of the righteous doer has lied and is an innovator (mubtadi`). Because Allah the Exalted said: 'Allah bears witness that there is no god but He, and the angels and those of knowledge, standing in justice' – He meant the believers. So whoever says that the angels said this statement more than what Allah the Exalted said or less is an innovator. For if you say that the believer says less than what the angels said or more, it is impossible; and if you say the like of what the angels said, then what is the difference between you and the angels? And know that the angels are superior to us in actions and deeds, not in faith, for faith is one. Also say to the opponent: Did Gabriel believe in someone you believe in, or did he believe in someone you do not believe in? If he believed in someone you do not believe in, that is not faith but disbelief; and if he believed in someone you believe in, then your faith and his faith are equal. And whoever says that our faith is better than the faith of Gabriel, because Allah created Gabriel and gave him intellect but did not give him desire, and created us and gave us intellect and desire and commanded us with prayer, fasting, Hajj, Zakat, and washing from janabah; so when we perform all this, our faith is better than Gabriel's faith – he is an innovator. And Allah the Exalted says: 'Then if they believe in the like of what you believed in, they have been guided.' Also say to the opponent: What do you say about a man who says 'La ilaha illa Allah, Muhammadun Rasul Allah' and an angel says the same – are both truthful believers, or is one truthful and the other lying? If he says one is truthful and the other lying, he is an innovator; and if he says both are truthful believers, then there is no difference between the faith of the angel and the man. So whoever believes in Allah and what Allah commanded and what Allah revealed to Muhammad (peace be upon him) is a believer, even if he is an adulterer or a drinker of wine or a killer of a believer. His faith and the faith of the angels and prophets are equal. And whoever says other than this is an innovator. In this is sufficient for the intelligent. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage argues that the faith (iman) of all believers – the righteous, the wicked, angels, and prophets – is identical in essence. The author starts by stating the thesis that iman of the good and bad are equal, and iman of angels, prophets, and ordinary believers are equal. He then refutes anyone who claims that the iman of a sinner is less than that of a righteous person, calling such a person a liar and an innovator (mubtadi`). He cites the Qur'anic verse (3:18) where Allah, the angels, and those of knowledge testify to His oneness, and argues that the angels and believers all utter the same testimony; any claim of difference in quantity is innovation. He then uses a logical argument: if you ask whether Gabriel (Jibril) believes in the same Object of faith as you do, if yes, then your iman is the same; if no, then his belief would be kufr. Therefore iman is one. He also refutes the notion that because humans have more obligations and desires, their iman is greater; instead, angels are superior in actions, not iman. Finally, he presents a scenario of a man and an angel both saying the shahadah: if their statements are identical, then their iman is identical. Thus a believer remains a believer even if he commits major sins, and his iman is equal to that of angels and prophets. Those who disagree are innovators.

Key Terms
جبريل
ميكائيل
الملائكة
المبتدع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Humans can have greater iman than angels because of their struggle against desires.
Correction: Samarqandi states that such a claim is innovation; angels are superior in actions, not in iman, which is one.

Checkpoint
According to Samarqandi, what does the scenario of a man and an angel both saying the shahadah prove?
A) That the angel's faith is greater because it is an angel
B) That if both are truthful, their faith is identical
C) That the man's faith is less because he might sin
D) That the angel does not truly believe

Key Takeaway
Iman is defined solely by belief in Allah and His revelation; it is not augmented by righteous actions nor diminished by sins, as long as one remains a believer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever feel that your religious obedience makes your faith superior to that of someone who struggles with sin? How does the lesson's teaching that your iman equals that of an angel challenge your pride?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim committing a major sin, do you still consider them a believer with equal iman to you? What would change in your heart if you truly believed that?
?
If iman is solely about belief and not deeds, then is your daily practice merely a response of gratitude rather than a means to increase faith? How does this shift your motivation for worship?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
5 min
The Consensus of the Companions on Fundamental Creeds
Samarqandi lists the ten companions and other Sahaba who affirmed faith, iman, wiping over khuffs, and witr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the early companions unanimously affirmed that faith does not increase or decrease and established key practices like wiping over khuffs and witr prayer.

Core Idea
The companions agreed on the essence of faith and certain rituals, forming the foundation of Sunni orthodoxy.

This passage from Imam Samarqandi's al-Sawad al-A'zam lists the ten promised Paradise and many other companions who collectively affirmed that faith is stable and does not fluctuate with deeds. Their consensus also includes practical rulings such as wiping over leather socks during ablution, the iqama being recited twice, and witr being three rak'ahs with one tasleem. This lesson examines their unified stance and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of companions
Carefully read the names of the companions mentioned, including the ten promised Paradise and others. Notice the breadth of the list.
2
Identify the creedal statement
Find where they say 'كُلُّهُمْ قَالُوا: نَحْنُ الْمُؤْمِنُونَ حَقًّا وَالْإِيمَانُ لَا يَزِيدُ وَلَا يَنْقُصُ' and note what this refutes.
This refutes both the Khawarij and Murji'a views.
3
Note the practical rulings
Identify the specific practices mentioned: wiping over khuffs, iqama in twos, no recitation behind imam, witr three rak'ahs.
These are part of the agreed sunnah according to the Salaf.

And witnessed for them Paradise: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali, Talha, al-Zubayr, Sa'd, Sa'id, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, Abu Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah, and others like Abdullah ibn Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, al-Hasan, al-Husayn, Mu'adh ibn al-Yamani, Anas ibn Malik, Salman al-Farisi, Bilal al-Habashi, Abu Ayyub al-Ansari, Abu Umama al-Bahili, Aisha, Hafsa, Maimuna, Fatima al-Zahra', al-Bara' ibn Azib, Ubada ibn al-Samit, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, Ammar ibn Yasir, Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa, Ikrima, Khalid, Qatada, and many like them. But we limited ourselves. All of them said: 'We are truly the believers, and faith does not increase or decrease. And the imam leads the people in prayer. And we hold wiping over the khuffs, and the iqama is repeated twice, and one does not recite behind the imam, and witr is three rak'ahs with one tasleem.' On this we found the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. And it is narrated from al-Hasan al-Basri that he said: 'I saw three hundred companions of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, among them seventy who were present at Badr. Each one narrated to me from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that he said: Guard your tongues concerning those who say La ilaha illa Allah, and do not declare the believers disbelievers because of a sin.' And each one narrated to me that the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'The determination of good and evil is from Allah the Exalted. And I have been commanded to fight people until they say La ilaha illa Allah. When they say La ilaha illa Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, they have protected from me their blood and their property. And faith is affirmation by the tongue, and belief in the heart, and action according to the laws. And pray over those who die from the people of the qibla, and do not doubt your faith. And pray behind every pious and wicked person, and do not rebel against anyone from the people of the qibla with the sword.' And from the Tabi'un and righteous like Muhammad ibn Ka'b al-Qurazi, Ata' ibn Abi Rabah, Ja'far ibn Muhammad al-Sadiq, Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, Maymun ibn Mihran, Tawus al-Yamani, al-Rabi' ibn Khaytham, Wahb ibn Munabbih, Malik ibn Dinar, Ka'b al-Ahbar, Thabit al-Bunani, Muhammad ibn al-Munkadir, Muhammad ibn Sirin, Alqama, Ibrahim al-Taymi, Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, Ziyad ibn Wak i', Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak, and likewise about seven hundred of the Tabi'un and righteous said: 'We are truly believers. One does not recite behind the imam, and prays witr as three rak'ahs with one tasleem, and the iqama is in twos, and the imam leads the people. Faith does not increase or decrease. And one prays behind every pious and wicked person, and we do not declare anyone from the people of the qibla a disbeliever because of a sin. And we hold wiping over the khuffs, and we do not perform wudu with a small amount of stagnant water.' On this we found the Companions of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and those by whom the religion is established. And some scholars and righteous like Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi, 'Isam ibn Yusuf, Abu al-Layth, and Abu Hafs said.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a testimony to the consensus of the early Muslim community (Salaf) on key doctrinal and practical matters. It begins by listing the ten Companions promised Paradise (al-ashara al-mubashsharun) and many others, including major Companions, wives of the Prophet, and early converts. The author says these all affirmed the statement: 'We are truly the believers, and faith does not increase or decrease.' This is a direct refutation of the Murji'a (who say faith is only affirmation) and the Khawarij (who say sins nullify faith). They also affirmed: the imam leads the prayer, wiping over khuffs, the iqama is recited in twos, no recitation behind the imam in loud prayers, and witr is three rak'ahs with one tasleem. Then a hadith from Hasan al-Basri reports three hundred Companions, including seventy Badriyyun, narrating three key principles: (1) guard your tongue regarding those who say La ilaha illa Allah (do not declare them disbelievers), (2) the decree of good and evil is from Allah, (3) the command to fight until people say La ilaha illa Allah, and when they do, their blood and property are protected. The hadith also defines faith as affirmation by tongue, belief in heart, and action according to laws. It instructs to pray over the deceased from the qibla, not to doubt one's faith, to pray behind both pious and wicked rulers, and not to rebel against them with the sword. Then a list of about seven hundred Tabi'un and righteous scholars is given, who repeated the same creedal statements: no recitation behind imam, witr three rak'ahs, iqama in twos, imam leads, faith does not increase or decrease, pray behind pious and wicked, no takfir by sin, wipe over khuffs, and do not perform wudu with a small amount of stagnant water. The passage concludes that this is what was found with the Companions, the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and later authorities.

Key Terms

المسح على الخفين
الإقامة مثنى
لا يقرأ خلف الإمام
الوتر ثلاث ركعات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That faith increases and decreases with deeds (Khawarij) or that faith is only inner belief without actions (Murji'a)
Correction: The Salaf affirmed that faith is a stable reality that does not increase or decrease in its essence, though actions may vary.

Checkpoint
According to the consensus reported in this passage from the companions, which of the following is a stated belief?
A) Faith increases and decreases.
B) Faith does not increase or decrease.
C) Faith is only affirmation by the tongue.
D) Faith is only action.

Key Takeaway
The companions unanimously held that faith is a stable reality that does not increase or decrease, and they agreed on several practical rulings such as wiping over khuffs and witr prayer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You recite the Qur'an, but does the testimony of these companions make you ask: is my faith as certain as theirs, or do I let my fluctuating deeds determine my certainty? What would it take for you to say 'I am truly a believer' without hesitation?
?
The companions unanimously agreed on wiping over khuffs, iqama twice, and witr three rak'ahs. Have you ever submitted to their consensus even when your own preference or habit says otherwise? What is one practice you will change tonight to align with their way?
?
If the companions' faith did not increase or decrease, how does your own fluctuating spirituality reveal a hidden doubt about the completeness of your iman? Will you repent from this doubt and embrace the security of the Salaf's conviction?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner

The Prophetic Command: Guarding Tongues and the Definition of Faith
Samarqandi narrates a hadith from Hasan al-Basri with three principles and defines faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three key principles narrated from three hundred companions: not declaring believers disbelievers due to sin, that good and evil are decreed by Allah, and the condition for fighting. You will also learn the definition of faith as affirmation, belief, and action.

Core Idea
Faith is affirmed by tongue, believed in heart, and acted upon by limbs — and believers are not excommunicated due to sin.

Al-Hasan al-Basri reports that he saw three hundred companions, including seventy who fought at Badr, each narrating that the Prophet commanded to guard one's tongue about those who say 'La ilaha illa Allah', that the determination of good and evil is from Allah, and that fighting is only until people say the shahada. This lesson unpacks these three foundational principles and the accompanying definition of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith from Hasan al-Basri
Read the narration carefully, noting the chain of three hundred companions and the three commands.
2
Identify the three principles
Find the three things each companion narrated: guard tongues, decree of good and evil, and the command to fight until shahada.
3
Examine the definition of faith
Note the definition: 'الإيمان إقرار باللسان وتصديق بالقلب والعمل بالشرائع' (faith is affirmation by tongue, belief in heart, and action according to laws).
This definition includes all three dimensions.
4
Understand the implications
Reflect on how these principles prevent takfir by sin and establish the proper attitude towards rulers.
The passage also instructs to pray behind pious and wicked rulers and not to rebel.

تخرجوا على احد من اهل القبلة بالسيف ) وقال من التابعين والصالحين مثل محمد بن كعب القرطى وعطاء بن ابي رباح وجعفر بن محمد الصادق وعمر بن عبدالعزيز وميمون بن مهران وطاؤرت اليمانى والربيع بن خيم ووهب بن التابعين والصالحين قالوا نحن المؤمنون حقا ولا يقرأ خلف الامام ويصلى الوتر ثلاث ركعات بتسليمة واحدة والاقامة متى وحدث الامام حدث القوم والايمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص وتصلى خلف كل بر وفاجر ولا نكفر احدا من اهل القبلة بالذنب و ترى المسح على الخفين ولا نتوضأ بالماء القليل الراكد على هذا وجدنا اصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والحلفاء الراشدين ومن صح به الدين وقال بعض العلماء والصالحين مثل محمد بن مقاتل الرازي وعصام بن يوسف وابو الليث وابي حفص
And witnessed for them Paradise: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali, Talha, al-Zubayr, Sa'd, Sa'id, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, Abu Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah, and others like Abdullah ibn Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, al-Hasan, al-Husayn, Mu'adh ibn al-Yamani, Anas ibn Malik, Salman al-Farisi, Bilal al-Habashi, Abu Ayyub al-Ansari, Abu Umama al-Bahili, Aisha, Hafsa, Maimuna, Fatima al-Zahra', al-Bara' ibn Azib, Ubada ibn al-Samit, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, Ammar ibn Yasir, Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa, Ikrima, Khalid, Qatada, and many like them. But we limited ourselves. All of them said: 'We are truly the believers, and faith does not increase or decrease. And the imam leads the people in prayer. And we hold wiping over the khuffs, and the iqama is repeated twice, and one does not recite behind the imam, and witr is three rak'ahs with one tasleem.' On this we found the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. And it is narrated from al-Hasan al-Basri that he said: 'I saw three hundred companions of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, among them seventy who were present at Badr. Each one narrated to me from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that he said: Guard your tongues concerning those who say La ilaha illa Allah, and do not declare the believers disbelievers because of a sin.' And each one narrated to me that the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'The determination of good and evil is from Allah the Exalted. And I have been commanded to fight people until they say La ilaha illa Allah. When they say La ilaha illa Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, they have protected from me their blood and their property. And faith is affirmation by the tongue, and belief in the heart, and action according to the laws. And pray over those who die from the people of the qibla, and do not doubt your faith. And pray behind every pious and wicked person, and do not rebel against anyone from the people of the qibla with the sword.' And from the Tabi'un and righteous like Muhammad ibn Ka'b al-Qurazi, Ata' ibn Abi Rabah, Ja'far ibn Muhammad al-Sadiq, Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, Maymun ibn Mihran, Tawus al-Yamani, al-Rabi' ibn Khaytham, Wahb ibn Munabbih, Malik ibn Dinar, Ka'b al-Ahbar, Thabit al-Bunani, Muhammad ibn al-Munkadir, Muhammad ibn Sirin, Alqama, Ibrahim al-Taymi, Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, Ziyad ibn Wak i', Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak, and likewise about seven hundred of the Tabi'un and righteous said: 'We are truly believers. One does not recite behind the imam, and prays witr as three rak'ahs with one tasleem, and the iqama is in twos, and the imam leads the people. Faith does not increase or decrease. And one prays behind every pious and wicked person, and we do not declare anyone from the people of the qibla a disbeliever because of a sin. And we hold wiping over the khuffs, and we do not perform wudu with a small amount of stagnant water.' On this we found the Companions of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and those by whom the religion is established. And some scholars and righteous like Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi, 'Isam ibn Yusuf, Abu al-Layth, and Abu Hafs said.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a testimony to the consensus of the early Muslim community (Salaf) on key doctrinal and practical matters. It begins by listing the ten Companions promised Paradise (al-ashara al-mubashsharun) and many others, including major Companions, wives of the Prophet, and early converts. The author says these all affirmed the statement: 'We are truly the believers, and faith does not increase or decrease.' This is a direct refutation of the Murji'a (who say faith is only affirmation) and the Khawarij (who say sins nullify faith). They also affirmed: the imam leads the prayer, wiping over khuffs, the iqama is recited in twos, no recitation behind the imam in loud prayers, and witr is three rak'ahs with one tasleem. Then a hadith from Hasan al-Basri reports three hundred Companions, including seventy Badriyyun, narrating three key principles: (1) guard your tongue regarding those who say La ilaha illa Allah (do not declare them disbelievers), (2) the decree of good and evil is from Allah, (3) the command to fight until people say La ilaha illa Allah, and when they do, their blood and property are protected. The hadith also defines faith as affirmation by tongue, belief in heart, and action according to laws. It instructs to pray over the deceased from the qibla, not to doubt one's faith, to pray behind both pious and wicked rulers, and not to rebel against them with the sword. Then a list of about seven hundred Tabi'un and righteous scholars is given, who repeated the same creedal statements: no recitation behind imam, witr three rak'ahs, iqama in twos, imam leads, faith does not increase or decrease, pray behind pious and wicked, no takfir by sin, wipe over khuffs, and do not perform wudu with a small amount of stagnant water. The passage concludes that this is what was found with the Companions, the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and later authorities.

Key Terms
الإيمان إقرار باللسان وتصديق بالقلب والعمل بالشرائع
لا نكفر أحدا بالذنب
تقدير الخير والشر من الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in this passage, what is the definition of faith?
A) Only affirmation by the tongue.
B) Only belief in the heart.
C) Affirmation by the tongue, belief in the heart, and action according to the laws.
D) Action alone.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet commanded not to declare believers disbelievers due to sin, affirmed divine decree, and defined faith as comprising tongue, heart, and actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim commit a sin, do you find yourself thinking less of their faith? How does the Prophet's command to 'guard your tongues' challenge that inner judgment, and what would it look like to truly entrust their account to Allah?
?
The hadith says 'do not doubt your faith'. In times when your actions fall short of your beliefs, do you doubt the reality of your own iman? What would it mean to trust in Allah's mercy while still striving to align your actions with your heart?
?
Faith is defined as 'action according to the laws.' Is there an area of your life where your outer actions do not match your inner belief? What one step can you take today to bring them into harmony, not out of fear but out of love for the One who defined faith this way?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
4 min
The Consensus of the Successors on the Same Creed
Samarqandi lists the Tabi'un and their agreement on creed and practical matters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the generation after the companions, including prominent scholars like Abu Hanifa, unanimously upheld the same creedal positions, reinforcing the continuity of Sunni orthodoxy.

Core Idea
The Tabi'un and early scholars reaffirmed the companion's creed, establishing it as the orthodox position.

After listing the companions, Imam Samarqandi then cites about seven hundred Tabi'un and righteous scholars who echoed the same statements: faith does not increase or decrease, no recitation behind the imam, witr as three rak'ahs, iqama in twos, praying behind pious and wicked, and not performing wudu with a small amount of stagnant water. This lesson shows how the early community maintained a united front on these issues.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of Tabi'un and scholars
Read the names of the Tabi'un and early scholars, including Muhammad ibn Ka'b al-Qurazi, Ata', Ja'far al-Sadiq, Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, Abu Hanifa, etc.
2
Identify the creedal statements they affirmed
Find the repeated creed: faith does not increase or decrease, no recitation behind imam, witr three rak'ahs, iqama in twos, etc.
3
Note the additional point about wudu
Notice they also stated: 'ولا نتوضأ بالماء القليل الراكد' (we do not perform wudu with a small amount of stagnant water).
This is a fiqh issue related to purity.

?

?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
6 min
Consensus of the Salaf on the Creed
Lists authorities and ascetics who agreed on the core beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the early scholars and ascetics (Salaf) unanimously agreed upon the core creedal positions of Ahl al-Sunnah, and you will be able to list several of those positions.

Core Idea
The Salaf unanimously agreed on core creed; opposing them is innovation.

This passage from Imam al-Samarqandi's al-Sawad al-Azam presents a powerful summary of the consensus of the early Muslim community (Salaf) on the essential beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah. The author lists a multitude of renowned scholars and ascetics from Khurasan, Iraq, and Transoxiana, all of whom affirmed a specific set of doctrines. By grounding the creed in this broad agreement, the author establishes it as the orthodox path inherited from the Prophet's companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of authorities
Notice the sheer number and geographic diversity of the scholars mentioned. This establishes the weight of consensus.
The author names about four hundred religious leaders.
2
Identify the creedal statements
The passage then transitions into a series of 'we' statements that summarize core beliefs. Underline each distinct belief.
These statements cover faith, prayer, and community relations.
3
Understand the significance of hand-raising
The statement 'we do not raise our hands except in the first takbir' is a specific practice that was contested. Reflect on how the Salaf's practice is cited as authoritative.
This distinguishes their practice from other schools.
4
Consider the closing warning
The author says none oppose except an innovator. What does this tell us about the role of consensus in Sunni theology?
Consensus is a source of authority in creed.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البخارى وخلف بن ايوب و جارودبن معاذ وعلى بن اسحق وابي عمرو الضرير وابي سليمان الجرجاني وابى بكر الجرجاني وابى القاسم الصغار وابي احمد العياض ومن مثلهم نحو اربعمائة نفر من ائمة الدين بخراسان والعراق وما وراء النهر كلهم كانوا على ما ذكرنا وقالوا كلهم نحن وجدنا سادات هذه الامة وزهادها وعبادها على مثل هذا مثل صالح المرى وذوى النون المصرى وفضيل بن عياض وابى بكر الوراق واحمد بن حضرويه وابى بكر الوسطى وابى يزيد البسطامى وابراهيم بن احمد وشقيق بن إبراهيم الباخى وخاتم الاسم وحامد اللفاف ومعاذا التقني وابراهيم السمر قندى وعمران ابن ابى بكر وابي زكريا وعتبة الغلام وابي تراب النخشى وابي القاسم الحكيم السمر قندى ومن مثلهم من زهاد قالوا نحن المؤمنون حتا ونوتر بثلاث ركعات بتسليمة واحدة ولا نشك في ايماننا و الايمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص والاقامة متى منى ولا ترفع ايدينا الا فى التكبيرة الاولى ولا نقرأ خلف الامام ولا نكفر احدا من اهل القبلة بالذنب ونصلى خلف كل بر وفاجر ولا نتكلم فى اهل القبلة الاخير ونخاف من الله تعالى وترجوا فضله وجدنا على هذا اعتنا من اهل خراسان والعراق واهل ماوراء النهر كلهم قوله مقبول في هذا كله فلما كان هؤلاء السادات وائمة الهدى على ذلك فلا يخالفهم الامبتدع وفي هذا خمس مائة حديث عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ولكن افته مرنا كي لا ينقل على المعلم وبالله الحول والقوة وهذا كفاية للعاقل والله اعلم بالصواب
Al-Bukhari, Khalaf ibn Ayyub, Jarud ibn Mu'adh, Ali ibn Ishaq, Abu Amr al-Darir, Abu Sulayman al-Jurjani, Abu Bakr al-Jurjani, Abu al-Qasim al-Saghar, Abu Ahmad al-'Iyad, and about four hundred like them from the religious leaders of Khurasan, Iraq, and Transoxiana – all of them were upon what we mentioned – and they all said: We found the masters of this ummah, its ascetics, and its worshipers upon the likes of this, such as Salih al-Murri, Dhu al-Nun al-Misri, Fudayl ibn 'Iyad, Abu Bakr al-Warraq, Ahmad ibn Hadruyah, Abu Bakr al-Wasti, Abu Yazid al-Bistami, Ibrahim ibn Ahmad, Shaqiq ibn Ibrahim al-Balkhi, Khatam al-Asamm, Hamid al-Laffaf, Mu'adh al-Taqani, Ibrahim al-Samarqandi, 'Imran ibn Abi Bakr, Abu Zakariyya, 'Utba al-Ghulam, Abu Turab al-Nakhshi, Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim al-Samarqandi, and ascetics like them. They said: We are the believers truly, we pray witr with three rak'ahs with one taslim, we do not doubt our faith, faith does not increase nor decrease, we say the iqamah whenever we wish, we do not raise our hands except in the first takbir, we do not recite behind the imam, we do not declare anyone from the people of the qibla (direction of prayer) as a disbeliever due to a sin, we pray behind every righteous and sinful person, we do not speak about the people of the qibla in an evil manner, we fear Allah Almighty and hope for His bounty. We found upon this our elders from the people of Khurasan, Iraq, and the people of Transoxiana, all of them; their word is accepted in all of this. Since these masters and guiding imams were upon that, none oppose them except an innovator. In this there are five hundred hadiths from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, but we abbreviated so that it not be burdensome to the teacher. And power and strength are from Allah. This is sufficient for the intelligent person. And Allah knows best the correct.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a summary statement of the consensus of the early scholars and ascetics on the core creed of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah. The author begins by listing numerous prominent scholars from Khurasan, Iraq, and Transoxiana, totaling about four hundred religious leaders, all of whom agreed upon the doctrines mentioned earlier. He then cites a group of famous ascetics (zuhhad) who affirmed the same beliefs. The passage then presents a concise declaration of faith (a mini-creed) containing key points: they are truly believers; they perform witr prayer with three rak'ahs and one taslim; they do not doubt their faith; faith does not increase or decrease; they say the iqamah when they wish; they do not raise hands except in the first takbir; they do not recite behind the imam; they do not excommunicate any Muslim for sin; they pray behind both righteous and sinful leaders; they do not speak ill of the people of the qibla; they fear Allah and hope for His grace. The author emphasizes that this was the way of their predecessors from all three regions, and their word is accepted in all these matters. He warns that only an innovator would oppose these imams, and mentions that there are five hundred hadiths supporting these positions, but he abbreviates for brevity. The passage concludes with a statement of reliance on Allah and a note that this suffices for the intelligent.

Key Terms
الايمان
الوتر
الاقامة
التكبير
القراءة
التكفير
الصلاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the statement 'faith does not increase or decrease' denies that faith can be stronger or weaker in the heart.
Correction: The passage rejects the Mu'tazili and Kharijite view that sin decreases faith, but it does not deny varying degrees of certainty; rather, it affirms that the essence of faith remains constant.

Checkpoint
According to the creedal summary in this passage, which of the following is NOT a belief of the Salaf regarding prayer?
A) They do not recite behind the imam
B) They raise their hands in every takbir
C) They pray behind both righteous and sinful leaders
D) They say the iqamah whenever they wish

Key Takeaway
The Salaf unanimously agreed on specific creedal positions, and opposing their consensus is a sign of innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Salaf, about 400 imams and many ascetics, all agreed on a specific set of beliefs. When you consider that number, do you feel a sense of awe or indifference? Are you willing to examine your own positions and see if they match theirs, even when it challenges your habits or the opinions of your peers? What is one belief from this list that you find hardest to accept, and what will you do to align your heart with it this week?
?
The passage says 'we do not doubt our faith.' Do you live with that same certainty? When you sin or feel distant from Allah, do you doubt that you are still a believer, or do you hold fast to the Salaf's understanding that faith does not increase or decrease? What would change in your daily life if you truly internalized this?
?
The Salaf agreed to pray behind every righteous and sinful person and not to speak evil of any Muslim. Is there a Muslim leader or fellow believer you have spoken ill of or refused to pray behind? Can you repent from that and adopt the Salaf's way, trusting that Allah is the Judge? What step will you take today to show that you are with the Salaf, not the innovators?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
5 min
Faith Does Not Increase or Decrease - The Core Doctrine and the Quranic Proof Refuted
Samarqandi states the doctrine and refutes a Quranic proof text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that faith is not subject to increase or decrease and how the apparent meaning of Quran 48:4 is reinterpreted by authoritative commentators.

Core Idea
Faith is created if it can increase or decrease.

Samarqandi opens by stating the fifty-fifth issue: faith does not increase or decrease. He immediately warns that those who believe otherwise are innovators (mubtadi'). His reasoning is straightforward: increase and decrease apply only to created things. If faith could increase or decrease, it would be created—a conclusion unacceptable for the essence of faith. He then addresses the verse opponents often cite: 'that they may increase in faith upon their faith' (48:4). He shows that early authorities like Ibn Abbas and Hasan al-Basri interpreted 'faith' here as certainty (yaqin), not the essence of faith itself. This lesson explores this argument and the broader hermeneutic principle that not every verse is taken at face value.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once through. Notice the strong opening statement and the immediate accusation of innovation against those who disagree.
The passage is dense. Take your time.
2
Identify the logical argument
Find the sentences where Samarqandi connects increase/decrease to createdness. Understand why this is a reductio ad absurdum for the opponent.
The key phrase: 'الزيادة والنقصان لا يدخلان الا فى شىء مخلوق'.
3
Examine the reinterpretation of the verse
Look at how the commentators reinterpreted 'faith' in Quran 48:4. What alternative meanings did they give? Why does this refute the opponent's proof?
The commentators mentioned are Ibn Abbas, Ali, Ja'far al-Sadiq, and Hasan al-Basri.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة الخامسة والخمسون - ينبغي ان يعلم ان الايمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص لان من يرى الزيادة والنقصان في الايمان فهو مبتدع والزيادة والنقصان انما تكون فى الافعال لا فى الايمان والزيادة والنقصان لا يدخلان الا فى شىء مخلوق فان كان عندك ان الايمان يزيد وينقص فقد اقررت انه مخلوق والذى احتجوابه قوله تعالى ليزدادوا ايمانا مع ايمانهم قال المفسرون الذين قدصح منهم التفسير مثل ابن عباس وعلى وجعفر بن محمد الصادق والحسن البصرى الايمان ههنا اليقين وقال بعضهم التصديق وقال بعضهم البقاء ولم يقل احد من العلماء والصالحين ان الايمان يزيد وينقص وليس كل شيء من القرآن ينبغي لك ان نفسره على وجهه الظاهر ولكن ينبغي لك أن تنظر الى معناه لان في القرآن آیا كثيرة في الظاهر لها معنى والباطن غير ذلك فاتقوا الله ولا تفسروا كلام الله برأيكم لان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من فسر القرآن برأيه فقد كفر والتفسير الصحيح ماجاء عن الصحابة والعلماء قال الله تعالى ربنا واجعلنا مسلمين لك معناه ثبتنا على اسلام ولو فسرت على الظاهر فانظر الى قوله واسأل القرية يعنى واسأل اهل القرية وقوله تعالى فإن تنازعتم فى شىء فردوه إلى الله والرسول يعنى إلى كتاب وكلام الله وقوله تعالى المتركيف فعل ربك يعنى الم تخبر وكثير مثل هذا في القرآن ولكن اقتصرنا على ذلك فيجب عليك ان لا تفسر كلام الله برأيك ولا تحسب كل مدور جوزا كيلا تكفر وتدخل النار فان قال المختلف روى عن النبي صلى لله عليه وسلم أنه قال يخرج من النار من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من الايمان فاذا كان فى الايمان مثقال ذرة علمنا ان الايمان يزيد وينقص فقل له هل يكون الايمان اقل من قول لا اله الا الله فان قال لا فقل لا اله الا الله اكثر ام مثقال ذرة وقد جاء في الخبر عن النبي صلى عليه وسلم أنه قال لوان السموات السبع والارضين السبع وضعت في كفة الميزان وقول لا اله الا الله في كفة اخرى لكان قول لا اله الا الله
The fifty-fifth issue: He should know that faith does not increase nor decrease, because whoever holds increase and decrease in faith is an innovator. Increase and decrease only occur in actions, not in faith. Increase and decrease only enter into created things. If you hold that faith increases and decreases, you have confessed that it is created. And what they use as evidence is His saying, the Most High: 'that they may increase in faith upon their faith' (Quran 48:4). The commentators whose interpretation is established, such as Ibn Abbas, Ali, Ja'far ibn Muhammad al-Sadiq, and al-Hasan al-Basri – they said: 'faith' here means certainty (yaqin). And some said: affirmation (tasdiq). And some said: perseverance (baqa'). No one among the scholars and righteous said that faith increases and decreases. And not everything in the Quran should be interpreted according to its apparent meaning; rather, you must look to its meaning, because in the Quran there are many verses whose apparent meaning has a different inner meaning. So fear Allah and do not interpret the speech of Allah according to your own opinion, because the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Whoever interprets the Quran according to his own opinion has disbelieved.' The correct interpretation is what comes from the Companions and the scholars. Allah the Most High said: 'Our Lord, make us Muslims submissive to You' (Quran 2:128); its meaning is 'establish us upon Islam.' If you interpret it according to its apparent meaning, then consider His saying: 'And ask the village' (Quran 12:82) meaning 'ask the people of the village'; and His saying, the Most High: 'Then if you dispute over something, refer it to Allah and the Messenger' (Quran 4:59) meaning 'to the Book and speech of Allah'; and His saying, the Most High: 'Do you not see how your Lord dealt?' (Quran 105:1) meaning 'have you not been informed?' And many such examples in the Quran. But we have confined ourselves to that. So it is necessary that you do not interpret the speech of Allah according to your own opinion, and do not consider every round thing a nut, lest you disbelieve and enter the Fire. If the opponent says: It is narrated from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that he said: 'He will be brought out of the Fire who has in his heart a mustard seed's weight of faith.' So if faith is a mustard seed's weight, we know that faith increases and decreases. So say to him: Can faith be less than the statement 'La ilaha illa Allah'? If he says no, then say: Is 'La ilaha illa Allah' more or a mustard seed's weight? And it has come in the report from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that he said: 'If the seven heavens and the seven earths were placed on one scale and the statement 'La ilaha illa Allah' on the other, the statement 'La ilaha illa Allah' would outweigh them.'
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument (mas'alah) defending the position that faith (iman) does not increase or decrease, a key tenet of the Maturidi/Hanafi creed against certain sectarian views. The author begins by stating the ruling: one must know that faith neither increases nor decreases, and whoever believes it does is an innovator (mubtadi'). The reasoning is that increase and decrease apply only to actions or created things; if faith were subject to them, it would be created, which is unacceptable. The author then addresses the proof text used by opponents: the Quranic verse 'that they may increase in faith upon their faith' (48:4). He cites early commentators – Ibn Abbas, Ali, Ja'far al-Sadiq, and Hasan al-Basri – who interpreted 'faith' here as certainty (yaqin), or as affirmation (tasdiq), or as perseverance (baqa'), not as the essence of faith itself. He then makes a broader hermeneutical point: not every Quranic verse should be taken at its literal (zahir) meaning; many have interior meanings. He warns against interpreting the Quran by personal opinion, citing the hadith that doing so is disbelief. He gives examples of verses whose apparent meaning is not intended, such as 'ask the village' meaning 'ask the people of the village', and 'refer it to Allah and the Messenger' meaning to the Book, and 'do you not see' meaning 'have you not been informed'. He concludes that one must not interpret by opinion. Then he addresses a specific objection from a hadith about a mustard seed's weight of faith being sufficient to save from Hell, arguing that this implies faith can be less (i.e., a small amount). The author's response is to compare that tiny measure to the statement 'La ilaha illa Allah' – asking whether faith can be less than that statement. He then cites another hadith that 'La ilaha illa Allah' outweighs the heavens and earth, implying that the statement itself is of immense weight, so the mustard seed analogy is not a measure of quantity but of purity. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the argument is clear: the essence of faith is not quantifiable.

Key Terms
الايمان
الزيادة
النقصان
اليقين
التصديق
تفسير بالرأي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'that they may increase in faith' (48:4) proves that faith itself can increase and decrease.
Correction: Early commentators interpreted 'faith' in this verse as certainty (yaqin), affirmation (tasdiq), or perseverance (baqa'), not the essence of faith itself. Thus the verse does not imply that the core of faith is subject to change.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the interpretation of 'faith' in the verse 'that they may increase in faith' by Ibn Abbas and others?
A) It means actions
B) It means certainty (yaqin)
C) It means the number of prophets
D) It means the Quran

Key Takeaway
Faith itself is not subject to increase or decrease; the verse 'increase in faith' refers to certainty, not the essence of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read Quranic verses that seem to describe faith increasing, do you trust your own understanding or defer to the early commentators? What is at stake if you interpret by your own opinion?
?
If faith is not subject to increase or decrease, how does that challenge your own experience of spiritual highs and lows? Are you willing to accept that your faith itself remains unchanged even when your actions fluctuate?
?
The author warns against interpreting the Quran by personal opinion, calling it disbelief. Have you ever interpreted a verse based on what seemed reasonable to you without checking the scholarly consensus? What does this lesson demand of you next time you encounter a difficult verse?

Refuting the Hadith Objection on the Mustard Seed
Samarqandi answers an objection from a hadith and reinforces the warning against personal interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Samarqandi refutes the argument that the hadith about a mustard seed's weight of faith implies faith is quantifiable and increases or decreases.

Core Idea
A mustard seed's weight of faith does not imply quantity.

Having established that faith does not increase or decrease, Samarqandi now addresses a common objection from a hadith. He argues that the mustard seed analogy refers to purity, not quantity, and uses another hadith to show the immense weight of the declaration of faith. He also emphasizes the importance of following authoritative interpretation rather than personal opinion.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the section beginning with 'فان قال المختلف'. Understand the opponent's argument from the hadith and Samarqandi's response.
The opponent uses the hadith to imply faith can be a tiny amount, hence variable.
2
Analyze the logical trap
Samarqandi asks whether faith can be less than 'La ilaha illa Allah'. If not, then compare it to a mustard seed. He then cites a hadith that the statement outweighs the heavens and earth, showing its immensity.
The key point: the mustard seed analogy is not about quantity but about the quality of faith.
3
Understand the warning against personal interpretation
Review the preceding warnings about interpreting the Quran by personal opinion. This ties into the overall argument.
The warning is that misinterpreting leads to disbelief.

Source Text

?
Do you treat the statement 'La ilaha illa Allah' as a profound reality that outweighs everything in your life, or is it just a phrase you repeat mechanically? What one change will you make today to give it the weight it deserves in your heart?
?
The hadith promises salvation for even a mustard seed's weight of faith. Does this fact make you careless about your sins, or does it press you to purify that faith so it is not merely a quantity but a quality that transforms your actions?
?
If your faith were weighed on a scale against the heavens and the earth, would it tip the balance because of your sincere devotion, or would it be light because of your neglect? What specific step will you take this week to strengthen the reality of tawheed in your daily life?

Faith and Disbelief

Faith Does Not Increase or Decrease – The Ruling and Argument
Samarqandi gives the ruling and rational argument against increase/decrease of iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Samarqandi asserts that faith does not increase or decrease and the rational argument he makes against those who say it does.

Core Idea
Increase and decrease apply only to created things; faith is uncreated.

Samarqandi begins by stating a foundational belief of Ahl al-Sunna: faith (iman) does not vary. He then provides a concise rational argument: increase and decrease can only happen to created things, so if someone says faith increases, they are implicitly saying faith is created. This lesson unpacks that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice how direct and definitive the author's tone is.
The Arabic uses 'yanbaghi' – it is necessary to know.
2
Identify the key claim and its opposite
The author states that anyone who believes faith increases or decreases is an innovator (mubtadi'). Underline this strong classification.
3
Trace the logical argument
The author argues that increase/decrease only apply to actions or created things. Since faith is not an action, it cannot be created – so it cannot increase. Follow the logic: if it increases, it is created.
This is a simple syllogism.
4
Reflect on the consequence
The author warns that holding the belief of increase makes one admit faith is created. Consider why this is a serious charge in kalam.
The createdness of faith was a contentious issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الخامسة والخمسون: ينبغي أن يعلم أن الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص لأن من يرى الزيادة والنقصان في الإيمان فهو مبتدع والزيادة والنقصان إنما تكون في الأفعال لا في الإيمان والزيادة والنقصان لا يدخلان إلا في شيء مخلوق فإن كان عندك أن الإيمان يزيد وينقص فقد أقررت أنه مخلوق والذي احتجوا به قوله تعالى {ليزدادوا إيمانا مع إيمانهم} قال المفسرون الذين قد صح منهم التفسير مثل ابن عباس وعلي وجعفر بن محمد الصادق والحسن البصري الإيمان ههنا اليقين وقال بعضهم التصديق وقال بعضهم البقاء ولم يقل أحد من العلماء والصالحين أن الإيمان يزيد وينقص وليس كل شيء من القرآن ينبغي لك أن تفسره على وجهه الظاهر ولكن ينبغي لك أن تنظر إلى معناه لأن في القرآن آيات كثيرة في الظاهر لها معنى والباطن غير ذلك فاتقوا الله ولا تفسروا كلام الله برأيكم لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من فسر القرآن برأيه فقد كفر والتفسير الصحيح ما جاء عن الصحابة والعلماء قال الله تعالى {ربنا واجعلنا مسلمين لك} معناه ثبتنا على الإسلام ولو فسرت على الظاهر فانظر إلى قوله {واسأل القرية} يعني واسأل أهل القرية وقوله تعالى {فإن تنازعتم في شيء فردوه إلى الله والرسول} يعني إلى كتاب الله وكلام الله وقوله تعالى {ألم تر كيف فعل ربك} يعني ألم تخبر وكثير مثل هذا في القرآن ولكن اقتصرنا على ذلك فيجب عليك أن لا تفسر كلام الله برأيك ولا تحسب كل مدور جوزا كيلا تكفر وتدخل النار.
Issue fifty-five: He should know that faith (iman) does not increase nor decrease, because whoever holds that faith increases and decreases is an innovator (mubtadi'). Increase and decrease occur only in actions, not in faith. Increase and decrease enter only into a created thing. So if you think that faith increases and decreases, you have admitted that it is created. What they argue with is His saying: 'That they may increase in faith upon their faith' (Al-Imran: 173). The exegetes whose interpretation is sound—such as Ibn Abbas, Ali, Ja'far ibn Muhammad al-Sadiq, and al-Hasan al-Basri—said: 'Faith here means certainty (yaqin).' Some said it means affirmation (tasdiq), and some said it means steadfastness (baqa'). None of the scholars and righteous said that faith increases and decreases. Not everything in the Quran should you interpret according to its apparent meaning; rather you should look at its intended meaning, because in the Quran there are many verses whose apparent meaning is one thing but their hidden meaning is otherwise. So fear Allah and do not interpret the speech of Allah with your own opinion, for the Prophet (s) said: 'Whoever interprets the Quran with his opinion has disbelieved.' Correct interpretation is what comes from the Companions and the scholars. Allah said: 'Our Lord, make us Muslims to You' (Al-Baqara: 128). Its meaning is: establish us in Islam. If you interpret it according to the apparent meaning? Look at His saying: 'And ask the village' (Yusuf: 82) meaning ask the people of the village. And His saying: 'If you dispute in anything, refer it to Allah and the Messenger' (Al-Nisa: 59) meaning refer it to the Book of Allah and His speech. And His saying: 'Do you not see how your Lord acted?' (Al-Fil: 1) meaning have you not been informed? There are many such examples in the Quran, but we restrict ourselves to that. Therefore you must not interpret the speech of Allah with your own opinion, and do not suppose that every round thing is a walnut, lest you disbelieve and enter Hellfire.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage opens the discussion on faith (iman) not increasing or decreasing. The author first declares the position as necessary knowledge (yanbaghi an ya'lam). He states a key principle: increase and decrease pertain only to actions or to created things; since faith is uncreated (as will be argued), it cannot vary. He refutes an objection based on the Quranic verse 'to increase in faith' by citing authoritative exegetes who interpret 'faith' in that verse as certainty (yaqin), affirmation (tasdiq), or steadfastness (baqa')—not as the intrinsic faith itself. The author then gives a broader warning against literalistic interpretation of the Quran, emphasizing that many verses have an apparent meaning different from the intended meaning. He warns that interpreting the Quran by one's own opinion (tafsir bi al-ra'y) is kufr. The correct method is to rely on the interpretations of the Companions and scholars. This lesson establishes the hermeneutical principle that apparent meanings must not always be taken literally, especially in matters of faith.

Key Terms
إيمان
زيادة
نقصان
مبتدع
مخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think faith can increase or decrease because of Quranic verses.
Correction: Samarqandi argues that increase is only possible in created things, so if faith increases, it must be created. Since faith is uncreated, it cannot increase.

Checkpoint
What does Samarqandi say about someone who believes faith increases or decreases?
A) He is a believer
B) He is an innovator
C) He is excused
D) He is a sinner

Key Takeaway
Faith is uncreated and therefore cannot increase or decrease; to claim otherwise is innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever measured your faith by your outward actions, feeling strong when you pray and weak when you sin? How does this lesson's insistence that faith itself does not increase or decrease change the way you view your spiritual ups and downs? Will you stop using 'weak iman' as an excuse for sin?
?
If faith cannot increase, then what is the real source of your fluctuating religious practice? Is it your resolve, your attention, or your hypocrisy? What would it mean to take full responsibility for your actions without blaming a change in faith?
?
The author says that believing faith increases makes it a created thing. Do you treat your faith as something you produce by your own effort, or as a gift from Allah that you must merely maintain? Which attitude leads to more gratitude and humility?

Interpreting Quranic Verses About Faith – The Danger of Literalism
Samarqandi refutes a Quranic objection and warns against personal interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Samarqandi interprets the Quranic verse 'to increase in faith' and why he warns against interpreting the Quran by personal opinion.

Core Idea
The Quran's apparent meaning is not always its intended meaning.

After declaring that faith does not increase, Samarqandi anticipates an objection from a Quranic verse that seems to imply increase. He responds by citing authoritative early exegetes who reinterpret the verse. Then he issues a broader warning: many Quranic verses have an apparent meaning that differs from their true meaning, and interpreting by one's own opinion leads to disbelief. This lesson teaches the principle of ta'wil and respect for scholarly interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the second half of the source passage. Notice how the author introduces the objection and then refutes it by citing exegetes.
2
Identify the verse and its interpretations
The verse is from Al-Imran 3:173. Find the three interpretations given: yaqin (certainty), tasdiq (affirmation), baqa' (steadfastness).
These are not contradicting but complementary.
3
Understand the hermeneutical principle
The author gives examples (like 'ask the village' meaning 'ask the people') to show that literal reading is not always valid. This is called tafsir bi al-ma'thur (interpretation by tradition) vs. tafsir bi al-ra'y.
The hadith warns: 'Whoever interprets the Quran with his opinion has disbelieved.'
4
Apply the lesson
Conclude that one must rely on the interpretations of the Companions and scholars, not on personal opinion.

Refuting the Objection on Faith's Increase and Decrease
Samarqandi answers the objection and cites supporting narrations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Samarqandi refutes the objection that faith increases or decreases using the hadith of the mustard seed and other narrations.

Core Idea
Faith is not a quantity; it is either present or absent.

This lesson presents Imam Samarqandi's comprehensive response to an objection based on the hadith about a mustard seed's weight of faith. He shows that the hadith refers to outward actions, not the essence of faith, and supports his position with multiple narrations from the Companions and early Muslims. The lesson establishes that faith does not increase or decrease, and that holding otherwise is innovation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection from opponents
The opponent cites the hadith 'whoever has in his heart a mustard seed's weight of faith' to argue that faith can be measured and thus increases/decreases.
Note how the opponent interprets the seeming quantization of faith.
2
Study Samarqandi's initial response
Samarqandi questions whether faith can be less than the testimony 'la ilaha illa Allah', then points out that this testimony outweighs all creation, so the hadith is about actions, not faith itself.
He reinterprets the hadith: the 'mustard seed weight' refers to actions, not the core faith.
3
Examine additional supporting narrations
Narrations from Ibn Umar, Abu Huraira, and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz reinforce that faith is not subject to increase/decrease, and those who claim otherwise are innovators.
Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz's argument from the Night of Ascension is particularly powerful.
4
Grasp the final ruling
The lesson concludes that faith does not increase or decrease; anyone who says otherwise is an innovator. This is the position of the Ahl al-Sunna.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال المخالف: روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: 'يخرج من النار من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من الإيمان' فإذا كان في الإيمان مثقال ذرة علمنا أن الإيمان يزيد وينقص. فقل له: هل يكون الإيمان أقل من قول لا إله إلا الله؟ فإن قال لا، فقل: لا إله إلا الله أكثر أم مثقال ذرة؟ وقد جاء في الخبر عن النبي صلى عليه وسلم أنه قال: 'لو أن السموات السبع والأرضين السبع وضعت في كفة الميزان وقول لا إله إلا الله في كفة أخرى لكان قول لا إله إلا الله أرجح' لكن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أراد ههنا عملا غير الإيمان إلا أنه جاء في الخبر عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: 'إن الله تعالى يخرج من النار بشفاعة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من قال لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله'. قل: ما قولك يا مخالف أين فراهم بإيمان كامل أو بإيمان ناقص وهو لم يعمل عملا صالحا؟ فإن كان الإيمان قولا وعملا لم يخرج من النار لأنه ليس فيه عمل. وروي عن عبد الله بن عمر عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: 'من قال إني مؤمن إن شاء الله فقد خرج من أمر الله'. ومن قال إن الإيمان يزيد وينقص فليس له في الإسلام نصيب. ومن قال إن الإيمان مخلوق فقد كفر. وروي عن أبي هريرة أنه قال: جاء أناس إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فسألوه عن زيادة الإيمان ونقصان الإيمان فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: 'زيادته ونقصانه كفر والإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص'. وروي عن عمر بن عبد العزيز أنه قال على المنبر: لو كان الإيمان على تلك الصفة التي صفوها أهل الأهواء لكان يقبل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ليلة المعراج على أمته في آناء الليل والنهار خمسين صلاة وصوم ستة أشهر من كل سنة مثل ما كان على بني إسرائيل، ولكن سأل الله تعالى التخفيف على أمته حتى خفف الله خمسين صلاة إلى خمس صلوات وخفف صوم ستة أشهر إلى صوم شهر واحد، فمن قال إن الإيمان قول وعمل أو يزيد وينقص فينبغي أن يقول إيمان موسى أكثر من إيمان محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، وهذا كفر. واعلم أن الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص ومن قال يزيد وينقص فهو مبتدع وهذا كفاية للمعاقل والله أعلم بالصواب.
If the opponent says: It is narrated from the Prophet (s) that he said: 'He will be brought out of Hellfire whoever has in his heart a mustard seed's weight of faith.' So if faith can be a mustard seed's weight, we know that faith increases and decreases. Say to him: Is faith ever less than the statement 'There is no god but Allah'? If he says no, then say: Is 'There is no god but Allah' greater or is a mustard seed's weight? And it has come in the report that the Prophet (s) said: 'If the seven heavens and the seven earths were placed in one pan of the balance and the statement 'There is no god but Allah' in the other pan, the statement 'There is no god but Allah' would outweigh them.' But the Prophet (s) intended here action other than faith. However, it has come in the report that the Messenger of Allah (s) said: 'Indeed Allah will bring out of Hellfire, through the intercession of the Prophet (s), whoever says 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah.'' Say: What is your opinion, O opponent? Their opinions? With complete faith or with deficient faith, while he performed no righteous deed? For if faith is statement and action, he would not come out of Hellfire because there is no action in him. And it is narrated from Abdullah ibn Umar from the Messenger of Allah (s) that he said: 'Whoever says 'I am a believer if Allah wills' has departed from the command of Allah.' And whoever says that faith increases and decreases has no share in Islam. And whoever says that faith is created has disbelieved. And it is narrated from Abu Huraira that he said: Some people came to the Messenger of Allah (s) and asked him about the increase and decrease of faith. The Messenger of Allah (s) said: 'Its increase and decrease is disbelief; faith does not increase nor decrease.' And it is narrated from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz that he said on the minbar: If faith were as the people of desires describe it, then the Prophet (s) on the night of the Ascension would have accepted for his community fifty prayers day and night and fasting six months every year as was upon the Children of Israel. But he asked Allah for lightening for his community until Allah lightened fifty prayers to five prayers, and lightened fasting six months to fasting one month. So whoever says that faith is statement and action, or increases and decreases, then he must necessarily say that the faith of Moses is greater than the faith of Muhammad (s), and that is disbelief. And know that faith does not increase nor decrease, and whoever says it increases and decreases is an innovator. This is sufficient for the intelligent, and Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This lesson continues the defense of the position that faith does not increase or decrease. The author presents an objection from an opponent based on the hadith about 'a mustard seed's weight of faith' that suggests faith can have a measure, thus increase and decrease. The answer is given: first, the minimum of faith is the testimony 'la ilaha illa Allah', which cannot be measured by a mustard seed weight; the Prophet's statement about the weight of the testimony shows its enormity, not a measurable amount. The author then clarifies that the hadith refers to action, not faith itself. Additional narrations from Ibn Umar, Abu Huraira, and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz are cited to support that the salaf considered the belief in increase/decrease of faith as innovation or even disbelief. The argument from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz is particularly striking: if faith could be more or less, then the earlier prophets would have had more faith than Muhammad (s) due to their greater acts of worship, which is an absurd conclusion. The lesson ends with the final ruling that faith does not increase or decrease, and those who say otherwise are innovators.

Key Terms
إيمان
مثقال ذرة
كفر
مبتدع
شفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith about a mustard seed's weight of faith proves that faith can be measured and thus increases and decreases.
Correction: The hadith refers to outward actions (deeds) performed by a believer, not to the essence of faith itself. Faith itself is the acceptance in the heart and the testimony of the tongue, which do not admit of variation.

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude about the hadith of the mustard seed's weight?
A) It proves faith can be measured
B) It refers to an action other than faith
C) It is a weak narration
D) It supports increase and decrease

Key Takeaway
Faith does not increase or decrease; the hadith about the mustard seed refers to righteous deeds, not the core of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever measure your faith by your actions, feeling it is 'less' when you sin? How does this lesson challenge you to separate the core of faith from your deeds?
?
If you truly believed that your faith is complete simply by saying the shahada, would your fear of hellfire change? What does your current fear or lack of fear reveal about your understanding of iman?
?
When you say 'I am a believer if Allah wills,' do you realize you are denying the certainty of your own faith? What step can you take today to affirm your iman without hesitation?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner
3 min
The States of Iblis and Abu Bakr and Umar
Samarqandi enumerates two examples to illustrate that faith and disbelief are based on current actions, not future outcomes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that a person's faith or disbelief is determined by their actual state at the time, not by future knowledge or predestination, as illustrated by the examples of Iblis and the two Companions.

Core Idea
Faith and disbelief are judged by one's present state, not by future destiny.

This lesson addresses a subtle theological point about how faith and disbelief are attributed. Imam al-Samarqandi clarifies that Iblis, before his rebellion, was a believer because he worshipped Allah, while Abu Bakr and Umar, before embracing Islam, were disbelievers because they worshipped idols. This underscores that divine knowledge does not override the actual status of a person at a given time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage uses a very direct style.
2
Identify the two examples
The passage presents two examples: Iblis as a believer when worshipping Allah, and Abu Bakr and Umar as disbelievers when worshipping idols. Understand the contrast.
3
Reflect on the warning
The passage warns that whoever says otherwise is an innovator and a Jabari. Consider why this distinction matters for avoiding fatalism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة السابعة والخمسون: وما قلنا: إنه ينبغي له أن يعلم أن إبليس لعنة الله لما كان يعبد الله سبحانه كان مؤمنا عند الله وعند الملائكة وفي اللوح، وأبو بكر وعمر رضي الله عنهما لما كانا يعبدان الصنم كانا كافرين عند الله وعند الملائكة وفي اللوح. ومن قال غير هذا فهو مبتدع جبري. روي عن ابن عباس...
Issue fifty-seven: And what we said: He should know that Iblis (may Allah curse him) when he used to worship Allah, the Blessed and Exalted, was a believer in the sight of Allah, in the sight of the angels, and in the Preserved Tablet. And Abu Bakr and Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) when they used to worship the idol were disbelievers in the sight of Allah, in the sight of the angels, and in the Preserved Tablet. Whoever says other than this is an innovator, a Jabari (fatalist). It is narrated from Ibn Abbas...
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This lesson addresses a theological point about the state of individuals before revelation. Iblis, before his rebellion, was a believer despite his future fate. Abu Bakr and Umar, before Islam, were disbelievers. This emphasizes that faith and disbelief are based on one's actual state at the time, not on predestination or future knowledge. Those who deny this are accused of being Jabari (fatalists) who believe all actions are forced. The narration from Ibn Abbas is cut off.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that Iblis was always a disbeliever or that Abu Bakr and Umar were always believers because of their future status.
Correction: The passage asserts that Iblis was a believer at the time of worship, and Abu Bakr and Umar were disbelievers at the time of idol worship.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the state of Abu Bakr and Umar before Islam?
A) They were believers in the sight of Allah
B) They were disbelievers in the sight of Allah
C) They were neither believers nor disbelievers
D) Their state was unknown

Key Takeaway
Faith and disbelief are based on one's actual state at the time, not on future events or predestination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that Iblis was once a believer. If you were to die at this moment, would your present actions label you as a believer or disbeliever in the sight of Allah? What needs to change right now?
?
You are not yet in the grave. Your future is unknown—you could end up like Iblis or like Abu Bakr. Are you taking your current state of faith for granted? What one action will you take today to solidify your present belief?
?
Think of someone you know who is currently a disbeliever. If they could become a believer like Abu Bakr, what is your role in that transformation? Are you willing to be the means of their guidance, even if they are now in a state of disbelief?

The Intercession Proof: Faith Is Not Dependent on Deeds
Logical argument using the intercession hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of intercession proves that faith does not require good deeds and therefore cannot increase or decrease based on actions.

Core Idea
If faith were action, intercession would not save the deedless.

The author begins by addressing a key hadith about the Prophet's intercession saving even those who only uttered the testimony of faith. This hadith poses a powerful challenge to those who define faith as both statement and action. The lesson unpacks this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith of intercession
Read the hadith where the Prophet says Allah will bring out of the Fire those who said the testimony of faith.
This hadith is central to the argument.
2
Understand the opponent's position
The opponent claims faith is statement and action. Consider what that implies.
3
See the logical consequence
If faith required action, a person with only the testimony and no good deeds would not be saved. But the hadith promises salvation.
4
Realize the truth
Therefore, faith must be independent of deeds and does not increase or decrease.
This refutes the view of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يرجع لكن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أراده هنا عملا غير الإيمان إلا أنه جاء في الخبر عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: إن الله تعالى يخرج من النار بشفاعة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من قال لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله. قل: ما قولك يا مخالف أين فراهم بإيمان كامل أو بإيمان ناقص وهو لم يعمل عملا صالحا؟ فإن كان الإيمان قولا وعملا لم يخرج من النار لأنه ليس فيه عمل. وروي عن عبد الله بن عمر عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: من قال: أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله فقد خرج من أمر الله، ومن قال: إن الإيمان يزيد وينقص فليس له في الإسلام نصيب، ومن قال: إن الإيمان مخلوق فقد كفر. وروي عن أبي هريرة أنه قال: جاء أناس إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فسألوه عن زيادة الإيمان ونقصان الإيمان فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: زيادته ونقصانه كفر، والإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص. وروي عن عمر بن عبد العزيز أنه قال على المنبر: لو كان الإيمان على تلك الصفة التي صفوها أهل الأهواء لكان يقبل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ليلة المعراج على أمته في آناء الليل والنهار خمسين صلاة وصوم ستة أشهر من كل سنة مثل ما كان على بني إسرائيل، ولكن سأل الله تعالى التخفيف على أمته حتى خفف الله خمسين صلاة إلى خمس صلوات، وخفف صوم ستة أشهر إلى صوم شهر واحد، فمن قال: إن الإيمان قول وعمل أو يزيد وينقص فيبنى أن يقول: إيمان موسى أكثر من إيمان محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، وهذا كفر. واعلم أن الإيمان لا يزيد ولا ينقص، ومن قال يزيد وينقص فهو مبتدع. وهذا كفاية للعاقل والله أعلم بالصواب.
But the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, intended here an action other than faith. However, it came in the report from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that he said: 'Indeed Allah, exalted is He, will bring out from the Fire by the intercession of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, whoever said: There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah.' Say: What is your saying, O opponent? Where do you place them—with complete faith or deficient faith—while he did no righteous deed? For if faith were statement and action, he would not come out of the Fire because there is no action in him. And it was narrated from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that he said: 'Whoever says: I am a believer if Allah wills, has departed from the command of Allah; and whoever says that faith increases and decreases has no share in Islam; and whoever says that faith is created has disbelieved.' And it was narrated from Abu Hurayra that he said: 'People came to the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and asked him about the increase and decrease of faith, so the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: Its increase and its decrease are disbelief, and faith does not increase nor decrease.' And it was narrated from 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz that he said on the pulpit: 'If faith were of the description that the people of desires describe, then the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, on the night of the Mi'raj would have imposed upon his community fifty prayers throughout the night and day and fasting six months every year, as was upon the Children of Israel. But he asked Allah, exalted is He, for lightening for his community until Allah lightened fifty prayers to five prayers, and lightened fasting six months to fasting one month. So whoever says that faith is statement and action, or increases and decreases, it follows that he would say: The faith of Moses is greater than the faith of Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and this is disbelief.' And know that faith does not increase nor decrease, and whoever says it increases and decreases is an innovator. And this is sufficient for the intelligent, and Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view that faith (iman) increases and decreases. The author begins by citing the well-known hadith that the Prophet's intercession will bring out from the Fire anyone who uttered the testimony of faith, even if they did no good deed. He then poses a question to the opponent: if faith were both statement and action, such a person would have no action and thus would not be saved—yet the hadith promises salvation, proving that faith is not dependent on action. He then provides several hadiths: from 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar that declaring 'I am a believer if Allah wills' departs from Allah's command, and that claiming increase or decrease excludes one from Islam; from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet explicitly called increase and decrease of faith disbelief and stated that faith neither increases nor decreases; and from 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz who argued from the Mi'raj and fasting reductions that if faith could increase, the obligations would have remained heavy for the Prophet's community, but instead they were lightened, implying that the faith of earlier prophets was not greater in essence. The author then concludes that if faith increased and decreased, one would be forced to say that Moses' faith was greater than Muhammad's—a manifest heresy. Finally, he states unequivocally that faith does not increase or decrease, and anyone who says otherwise is an innovator (mubtadi'). The passage is a classic Sunni position against the Mu'tazila and Khawarij who held that faith increases with good deeds and decreases with sins.

Key Terms
الإيمان
شفاعة
قولا وعملا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that faith increases with good deeds and decreases with sins, meaning that a person with no good deeds cannot be a true believer.
Correction: The hadith of intercession shows that a person with no good deeds but who uttered the testimony of faith will be saved, proving that faith is not dependent on deeds and does not increase or decrease.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this passage, who will be brought out of the Fire by the Prophet's intercession?
A) Only those with many good deeds
B) Whoever said 'La ilaha illa Allah, Muhammad Rasul Allah' even without good deeds
C) Only prophets
D) Only those who never sinned

Key Takeaway
The hadith of intercession proves that faith is merely the testimony of faith, not dependent on deeds, and thus does not increase or decrease.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your salvation rested solely on your saying 'La ilaha illa Allah' with sincerity – not on your prayers, charity, or fasting – would you be at peace? Or does that thought make you uneasy? Why?
?
Examine your heart: Do you secretly believe that your good deeds earn you God's favor? How does the hadith of intercession challenge your reliance on your own actions?
?
Imagine standing before Allah with only your testimony and no deeds. Would your faith in His mercy be enough to grant you hope? What does your answer reveal about where you truly place your trust?

Hadith Evidence That Faith Neither Increases Nor Decreases
Compilation of hadiths and argument from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the multiple hadiths that explicitly state that faith does not increase or decrease, and the argument from the Mi'raj that shows that if it did, earlier prophets would have greater faith.

Core Idea
The Prophet and the early caliphs explicitly declared that faith does not increase or decrease.

The author continues with three additional narrations: from Ibn Umar, Abu Hurayra, and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz. Each provides direct evidence that faith is a fixed entity. The lesson examines these proofs and the logical conclusion that those who claim increase or decrease are innovators.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith from Ibn Umar
This hadith warns against conditional faith and equates the belief in increase/decrease with exclusion from Islam.
2
Read the hadith from Abu Hurayra
The Prophet directly states that both increase and decrease of faith are disbelief, and that faith itself does not change.
This is a clear textual proof.
3
Read the argument from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz
He uses the reduction of prayers and fasting to argue that if faith increased, earlier prophets' faith would be greater—a blasphemy.
This is a rational argument based on divine mercy.
4
Understand the conclusion
Faith is fixed; those who oppose are innovators.
The author ends with a stark warning.

?

?
