The Four Signs of True Love for God
The author enumerates four signs of genuine love for God and refutes a false notion of immunity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four signs that validate a claim to love God, and why the notion that love exempts from obligations is false.

Core Idea
Love for God is proven by action, not mere words.

Imam al-Samarqandi provides a practical test for those who claim to love God. He lists four characteristics that must be present in every claimant, and then immediately refutes a dangerous misconception: that love makes one immune to the consequences of sin. This lesson introduces these signs and the initial refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the four signs
Read the Arabic passage listing the four signs. Notice the sequence and the key terms for each.
The signs are: fulfilling God's rights, avoiding prohibitions, accepting decrees, and mercy for creation.
2
Understand each sign
Reflect on each sign and what it implies for daily life. Consider how each sign tests the sincerity of one's love.
3
Examine the false claim
Read the refutation of those who say love prevents harm from sin. Understand why the author calls this false.
The author insists that love does not drop God's commands.
4
Learn the overarching principle
The key principle is that God's commands in this world are not lifted from the lover by virtue of his love. This sets the stage for the proofs in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة الثامنة والخمسون و ما قلنا انه ينبغي له ان يعلم ان امر الله تعالى في الدنيا لا سقط عن المحب بمحبته فمن ادعى محبة الله تعالى تصدقه في اربع خصال الأولى ان لا يقصر في حق مولاء والثانية ان لا يقصر في نهى مولاه والثالثة ان يرضى بجميع حكم مولاء والرابعة ان يترحم على جميع خلق مولاء ومن قال ان احباء الله تعالى اذا وجدوا محبة الله لا يضرهم شيء لان المحبة لا تتضرر بترك الصلاة وركوب المعاصى وهذا باطل ( واعلم ) ان الله تعالى قال قل ان كنتم تحبون الله فاتبعوني بحبكم الله واتباعنا ان نعمل بفرائض الله تعالى وسنن رسوله فمن ترك سنة رسوله فهو فاسق والفاسق لا يصاح المحبة الله تعالى ومن لم ير ذلك فهو مبتدع ولا يكون المبتدع حبيب الله فاذا كان بترك سنة رسوله هكذا فكيف بترك فرائض الله سبحانه وتعالى فينبنى له ان يعمل عمل المحبوب حتى يصدق قوله فعله وقد قال الله تعالى اليه يصعد الكلم الطيب والعمل الصالح يرفعه ولوسقط عن احد من عباد الله تعالى لكان يسقط عن خليله ابراهيم عليه السلام لان الله تعالى اتخذه خليلا فكان اذا صلى سمع قلبه من هيبة الله تعالى ميلا من ميل ولو سقط عن احد من احباء الله تعالى امر الله تعالى لمكان سقط عن محمد صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم لان الله تعالى احبه واختاره خلقه فكان اذا صلى يسمع الجوفه ازيز كازيز المرجل وقد آمنه الله تعالى من خوفه وقال تعالى ليغفر لك الله ما تقدم من ذنبك وما تأخر ومع هذا عبد الله تعالى وصلى حتى تورمت قدماه فلما لم يسقط أمر الله تعالى عن سيد ولد آدم محمد و عن خليله ابراهيم عليهما السلام فكيف يسقط عن غير هما و هذا كفاية للعاقل والله اعلم ) المسئلة ) وجيب من
The fifty-eighth question. And we say: it is necessary for him to know that the command of God Almighty in this world is not dropped from the lover due to his love. So whoever claims love of God Almighty, you should verify him by four characteristics: first, that he does not fall short in the right of his Master; second, that he does not fall short in the prohibition of his Master; third, that he is pleased with all the decrees of his Master; fourth, that he has mercy on all the creatures of his Master. And whoever says that the beloved of God Almighty, when they find the love of God, nothing harms them, because love is not harmed by abandoning prayer and committing sins—this is false. And know that God Almighty said: 'Say: If you love God, follow me, and God will love you' (Quran 3:31). And following us is to act upon the obligations of God Almighty and the traditions of His Messenger. So whoever abandons the tradition of His Messenger is a transgressor, and the transgressor is not accompanied by the love of God Almighty. And whoever does not see that is an innovator, and the innovator is not a beloved of God. So if it is so regarding abandoning the tradition of His Messenger, then what about abandoning the obligations of God Almighty? Therefore, it is necessary for him to act like the beloved so that his action confirms his word. God Almighty said: 'To Him ascends good speech, and righteous work raises it' (Quran 35:10). And if the command of God were dropped from any of God's servants, it would have been dropped from His friend Ibrahim, peace be upon him, because God took him as a friend. So when he prayed, his heart would be heard from the awe of God Almighty a mile away. And if the command of God were dropped from any of God's beloved, it would have been dropped from Muhammad, peace be upon him, because God loved him and chose him from His creation. So when he prayed, his chest would be heard seething like the seething of a cauldron. And God had secured him from fear and said: 'That God may forgive you your past and future sins' (Quran 48:2). Yet despite this, he worshipped God and prayed until his feet swelled. So when the command of God was not dropped from the master of the children of Adam, Muhammad, nor from His friend Ibrahim, peace be upon them, then how could it be dropped from others? And this suffices for the intelligent. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the signs that validate one's claim to love God. The author begins with the principle that love for God does not exempt anyone from His commands. He then lists four characteristics by which a claimant's sincerity is tested: not falling short in performing God's rights (obligations), not falling short in avoiding His prohibitions, being content with His decree, and having mercy on all creatures. The author refutes the false notion that love makes one immune to the harm of sin. He then grounds his argument in Quranic verses: the verse commanding to follow the Prophet as proof of love, and the verse about good speech and righteous deeds. He uses the examples of Ibrahim and Muhammad—the highest of God's beloved—to show that they did not neglect worship despite their closeness to God. Ibrahim prayed in such fear that his heart could be heard from a mile away; Muhammad prayed until his feet swelled, even though his sins were forgiven. Thus, if even they did not have God's commands dropped for them, no one else can claim exemption. The passage ends with a warning that abandoning the Prophet's sunnah makes one a transgressor (fasiq) and an innovator (mubtadi'), not a true lover of God.

Key Terms
محبة الله
الصلاة
المعاصى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if you truly love God, your sins will not harm you or that you are exempt from obligations.
Correction: The author explicitly states that God's commands are not dropped from the lover, and that such a belief is false.

Checkpoint

A) He does not fall short in the right of his Master.

Key Takeaway
True love for God is proven by fulfilling His commands, avoiding prohibitions, accepting His decrees, and showing mercy to creation.

Proof from Quran and Prophetic Examples
The author provides Quranic and prophetic evidence that obligations are not dropped for lovers of God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran commands following the Prophet as proof of love, and how the examples of Ibrahim and Muhammad demonstrate that obligations are not dropped even for the most beloved.

Core Idea
Even the prophets were not exempt; how could anyone else be?

Imam al-Samarqandi now provides scriptural and historical evidence for the principle that love does not exempt one from God's commands. He cites Quran 3:31, which links love of God to following the Prophet, and explains that abandoning the sunnah leads to transgression. He then gives the powerful examples of Prophet Ibrahim and Prophet Muhammad—the most beloved of God—who worshiped with utmost devotion despite their high status.

Guided Path

Read the Quranic evidence

The author says one who abandons Sunnah is a transgressor (fasiq) and an innovator (mubtadi'), and such a person cannot be a true lover of God.

These examples show that even the highest prophets did not neglect worship; they increased it.
4

If God's commands were not dropped for them, they cannot be dropped for anyone else. This is the final proof.

Love of Allah Does Not Exempt from Obligations
Samarqandi refutes the claim that love of Allah exempts one from obligations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that true love of Allah is proven by obedience to His commands and following the Prophet, and that love does not exempt one from religious duties.

Core Idea
Love of Allah demands action—faith without obedience is false.

Many people mistakenly think that if they love God, their sins don’t matter. Imam Samarqandi refutes this by providing clear signs of genuine love and showing that even the greatest prophets, who were beloved to Allah, never neglected their duties. Let’s read this powerful passage and learn the true meaning of loving Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the translation. Notice the structure: a statement of principle, four signs, a refutation, and then examples.
2
Identify the four signs of love
The author gives four characteristics to test a claim of love. List them and think about why each is necessary.
3
Examine the refutation
The author rejects the idea that love protects from sin. He uses a Qur’anic verse and logical reasoning. Notice the link between love, following the Prophet, and avoiding sin.
4
Reflect on the examples of prophets
The author invokes Ibrahim and Muhammad. Why does he use them? What do their examples teach us about love and worship?

المسئلة الثامنة والخمسون
و ما قلنا انه ينبغي له ان يعلم ان امر الله تعالى في الدنيا لا سقط عن المحب بمحبته فمن ادعى محبة الله تعالى تصدقه في اربع خصال الأولى ان لا يقصر في حق مولاء والثانية ان لا يقصر في نهى مولاه والثالثة ان يرضى بجميع حكم مولاء والرابعة ان يترحم على جميع خلق مولاء ومن قال ان احباء الله تعالى اذا وجدوا محبة الله لا يضرهم شيء لان المحبة لا تتضرر بترك الصلاة وركوب المعاصى وهذا باطل ( واعلم ) ان الله تعالى قال قل ان كنتم تحبون الله فاتبعوني بحبكم الله واتباعنا ان نعمل بفرائض الله تعالى وسنن رسوله فمن ترك سنة رسوله فهو فاسق والفاسق لا يصاح المحبة الله تعالى ومن لم ير ذلك فهو مبتدع ولا يكون المبتدع حبيب الله فاذا كان بترك سنة رسوله هكذا فكيف بترك فرائض الله سبحانه وتعالى فينبنى له ان يعمل عمل المحبوب حتى يصدق قوله فعله وقد قال الله تعالى اليه يصعد الكلم الطيب والعمل الصالح يرفعه ولوسقط عن احد من عباد الله تعالى لكان يسقط عن خليله ابراهيم عليه السلام لان الله تعالى اتخذه خليلا فكان اذا صلى سمع قلبه من هيبة الله تعالى ميلا من ميل ولو سقط عن احد من احباء الله تعالى امر الله تعالى لمكان سقط عن محمد صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم لان الله تعالى احبه واختاره خلقه فكان اذا صلى يسمع الجوفه ازيز كازيز المرجل وقد آمنه الله تعالى من خوفه وقال تعالى ليغفر لك الله ما تقدم من ذنبك وما تأخر ومع هذا عبد الله تعالى وصلى حتى تورمت قدماه فلما لم يسقط أمر الله تعالى عن سيد ولد آدم محمد و عن خليله ابراهيم عليهما السلام فكيف يسقط عن غير هما و هذا كفاية للعاقل والله اعلم
Issue Fifty-Eight. And what we said: that he should know that the command of Allah Almighty in this world is not dropped from the lover due to his love. So whoever claims love of Allah Almighty, you verify him by four characteristics: first, that he does not fall short in the right of his Master; second, that he does not fall short in the prohibition of his Master; third, that he is satisfied with all the decree of his Master; fourth, that he shows mercy to all the creation of his Master. And whoever says that the lovers of Allah Almighty, when they find the love of Allah, nothing harms them because love is not harmed by leaving prayer and committing sins, this is false. (Know) that Allah Almighty said: 'Say: If you love Allah, then follow me, Allah will love you.' And our following is that we act upon the obligations of Allah and the Sunnah of His Messenger. So whoever abandons the Sunnah of His Messenger is a sinner, and the sinner does not accompany the love of Allah Almighty. And whoever does not see that is an innovator, and the innovator is not a beloved of Allah. If this is the case with abandoning the Sunnah of His Messenger, then how about abandoning the obligations of Allah Almighty? So he must act the action of the beloved so that his action verifies his words. And Allah Almighty said: 'To Him ascends good speech, and righteous work raises it.' And if it were dropped from any of the servants of Allah Almighty, it would have been dropped from His intimate friend Ibrahim, peace be upon him, because Allah Almighty took him as an intimate friend. When he prayed, his heart would be heard from the awe of Allah Almighty for a mile. And if the command of Allah Almighty were dropped from any of the lovers of Allah Almighty, it would have been dropped from Muhammad, peace be upon him, because Allah Almighty loved him and chose him from His creation. When he prayed, a sound like the sound of a boiling pot was heard from his chest. And Allah Almighty had given him security from his fear and said: 'That Allah may forgive you your former and later sins.' Yet despite this, he worshipped Allah and prayed until his feet swelled. So when the command of Allah Almighty was not dropped from the master of the children of Adam, Muhammad, nor from His intimate friend Ibrahim, peace be upon them, how can it be dropped from others? This is sufficient for the intelligent. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage refutes the idea that love of Allah exempts one from religious obligations. The author begins by stating that the commands of Allah are not dropped for someone who claims love. Then he gives four signs to test such a claim: (1) not falling short in duties to the Master, (2) not falling short in avoiding prohibitions, (3) satisfaction with all divine decrees, and (4) mercy for all creation. He then refutes the false notion that love protects from sin, calling it false, and cites the Quranic verse 'Say: If you love Allah, follow me'. He argues that following the Prophet means performing obligations and Sunnah. Abandoning the Sunnah makes one a sinner, and a sinner cannot claim true love; denying that is innovation. The author uses the examples of Prophets Ibrahim and Muhammad, who despite their high status were extremely diligent in worship, concluding that since Allah's commands were not dropped for them, they cannot be dropped for anyone else.

الاتباع (following)
الفاسق (sinner)
المبتدع (innovator)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Love of Allah absolves one from sin and religious duties.
Correction: Love requires obedience; sins are not automatically forgiven without repentance and observance.

Fear of the Final End is Obligatory
Samarqandi mandates fear of Allah for the final end and cites evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why fear of the final end (khatima) is an obligation on every Muslim and the evidence from Quran, hadith, and Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
No one knows their final state—fear of Allah for the end is mandatory.

In this passage, Imam al-Samarqandi emphasizes a crucial aspect of Islamic faith: the necessity of fearing Allah for one’s final end. He argues that because no one knows whether they will die as a believer or disbeliever, fear of the end is an obligation. The passage provides scriptural evidence and a warning about complacency.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the flow from the main claim to evidence to warning.
The passage begins with the ruling and then lists proofs.
2
Identify the main claim
Find where Samarqandi states that fear of the final end is obligatory (fard). Understand why: because no one knows how they will die.
The key phrase is 'خوف الخاتمة فريضة على جميع المسلمين'.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Look at the three verses cited. Reflect on how each verse supports the idea of fear and warns against false security.
The verses are from Surah al-A'raf, al-Ma'ida, and al-Hashr.
4
Study the hadith qudsi
Read the hadith carefully. It contrasts fear in this world with security in the Hereafter, and vice versa.
This hadith is a powerful incentive to maintain fear of Allah.
5
Consider the warning from Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa states that faith is often taken at death. Relate this to the danger of being a Murji' or Jabri who neglects fear of the end.
The term 'مربى جبرى' combines Murji'ah and Jabriyyah, two deviant sects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة التاسعة والخمسون
وما ذكرنا انه ينبغي له ان يخاف الله تعالى لاجل خاتمته ويرى الخوف من الله تعالى لانه لايدرى ايمون بالاسلام او بالكفر كمن قبله من العباد الذين خرجوا من الدنيا بغير الاسلام وخوف الخاتمة فريضة على جميع المسلمين والدليل عليه قوله تعالى فلا يأ من مكر الله الا القوم الخاسرون وقوله تعالى ان الله شديد العقاب وقوله تعالى ولتنظر نفس ما قدمت اند وقال عليه السلام قال الله لاا. على عبدى خوفين ولا امنين من خافى فى الدنيا آمنته فى الآخرة ومن امتى فى الدنيا اخفته فى الآخرة وقال امام المسلمين ابو حنيفة رضى الله عنه اكثر ما يلب الايمان من العبد عند النزع فمن لا يخاف الخاتمة ومن لم يتق الله لاجل الخاتمة فهو مربى جبرى وهذا كفاية للعاقل والله تعالى اعلم
Issue Fifty-Nine. And what we mentioned: that he should fear Allah Almighty for the sake of his final end, and he should see fear of Allah Almighty because he does not know whether he will die in Islam or in disbelief, like those before him among the servants who left the world without Islam. And fear of the final end is an obligation upon all Muslims. The evidence for it is His statement: 'So none feels secure from the plan of Allah except the losing people.' And His statement: 'Indeed Allah is severe in punishment.' And His statement: 'And let every soul look to what it has sent forth for tomorrow.' And he (peace be upon him) said: 'Allah said: I will not combine two fears for My servant, nor two securities. Whoever fears Me in this world, I will secure him in the Hereafter; and whoever feels secure from Me in this world, I will make him fear in the Hereafter.' And the imam of the Muslims, Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'Most of the time, faith is taken from the servant at the moment of death.' So whoever does not fear the final end and does not fear Allah for the sake of the final end is a Murji' Jahmi. This is sufficient for the intelligent. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage focuses on the necessity of fearing Allah due to the uncertainty of one's final state (khatima). The author argues that one should fear because no one knows whether they will die as a Muslim or disbeliever, citing examples of those who died without Islam. He states that fear of the end is an obligation (fard) on all Muslims. He provides evidence from the Quran: 'Do they feel secure from the plan of Allah? None feels secure from the plan of Allah except the losing people' (Quran 7:99), 'Indeed Allah is severe in punishment' (Quran 5:2), and 'Let every soul look to what it has sent forth for tomorrow' (Quran 59:18). He then quotes a hadith qudsi in which Allah says He will not combine two fears or two securities: he who fears Allah in this world is secured in the Hereafter, while he who feels secure in this world is made to fear in the Hereafter. Finally, he quotes Abu Hanifa stating that faith is often taken from a person at the moment of death, warning that those who do not fear the end are Murji'ah or Jabriyyah (deviant sects).

Key Terms
الخوف (fear)
الخاتمة (khatima, final end)
المكر (plan)
الأمن (security)
النزع (agony of death)
مربى جبرى (Murji' Jahmi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can be certain of going to Paradise due to faith alone without any fear of the end.
Correction: The passage shows that fear of the final end is an obligation and that feeling secure from Allah's plan is a trait of the losing people. Constant fear keeps one mindful of the possibility of a bad end.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith quoted in this passage say about the one who fears Allah in this world?
A) He will be safe in the Hereafter.
B) He will be tested.
C) He will be given wealth.
D) He will become a prophet.

Key Takeaway
Fear of the final end is an obligation; feeling secure from Allah's plan leads to loss, and faith is often taken at death—so one must constantly fear Allah for a good end.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Right now, if you were to die, do you have any area in your life where you feel 'secure' that you will be fine? How does the hadith qudsi in this lesson expose that security as dangerous?
?
Think of a specific sin you commit regularly and tell yourself 'Allah will forgive me anyway.' How does Imam Abu Hanifa's statement that faith is often taken at death shatter that comfortable assumption?
?
If you truly believed that you could lose your faith at any moment, what is one habit you would change today? Write it down and commit to start now.

Faith and Disbelief
beginner

Despair of Mercy is Disbelief
Samarqandi forbids despair of Allah's mercy and cites Quran 12:87.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why despairing of Allah's mercy is an act of disbelief and the evidence from the Quran.

Core Idea
Despairing of Allah's mercy is disbelief, not just a sin.

Samarqandi begins by addressing a critical error: losing hope in Allah's mercy. He emphasizes that no matter how many sins a person commits, they must never despair, because despair itself is a form of disbelief. This lesson presents the core ruling and its Quranic proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the prohibition of despair
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how strongly the author states that despair is kufr.
The term 'Haruri' refers to the Khawarij sect.
2
Identify the Quranic evidence
Find the verse cited as proof. Reflect on why despair is equated with disbelief in the Quran.
The verse is from Surah Yusuf 12:87.
3
Reflect on the severity
Consider the implication: even a believer who commits all sins must not despair. Why? Because despair contradicts reliance on Allah's mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسئلة الستون
وما ذكرنا من انه ينبغي له ان لا يقنط من رحمة الله تعالى وان كان قد اتى بكيرة اوكبائر كثيرة لان من قنط من رحمة الله تعالى يكون كافرا يسمى حروريا ( واعلم ) لوان احدا من المؤمنين اتى بجميع ذنوب اهل الارض لاينبنى له القنوط من رحمة الله تعالى لانه كفر والدليل عليه قوله تعالى انه لا ييأس من روح الله الا القوم الكافرون ولو ان مؤمنا قتل الف مؤمن اوزنى بالف مؤمنة ولم يصل ولم يهم ولم يزك ولم يحح ولم يغتسل من الجنابة وفصل اكثر من ذلك مادام انه لا يكفر فهو مؤمن حقاوان تاب تاب الله عليه وان خرج من الدنيا بغير توبة فهو فى مشيئة الله تعالى ان شاء عذبه بعد له وانشاء غفر له فضله ويدخل الجنة برحمته ومن قال ان هذا المؤمن يكفر بالله بهذه الذنوب فهو كافر يسمى حروريا ومن قال ان هذا المؤمن اذا اتى بهذه الذنوب وخرج من الدنيا بغير توبة يخلد في النار ابدا فهو كافر يسمى معتزليا ومن قال ان هذا المؤمن لا تضره هذه الذنوب بعد ما آمن بالله تعالى فهو كافر يسمى مرحبا واعلم ان الله تعالى قال ان الله لا ينفر ان يشرك به ويغفر ما دون ذلك لمن يشاء وقال تعالى قل ياعبادى الذين أسرفوا على انفسهم لا تقنطوا من رحمة الله ان الله يغفر الذنوب جميعا انه هو الغفور الرحيم وقال تعالى والذين اذا فعلوا فاحشة او ظلموا انفسهم ذكروا الله فاستغفر والذنوبهم ومن يغفر الذنوب الا الله وقال تعالى ومن يعمل سوء او يظلم نفسه ثم يستغفر الله مجد الله غفورا رحيما وهذا كفاية للعاقل والله سبحانه وتعالى اعلم بالصواب
Issue Sixty. And what we mentioned: that he should not despair of the mercy of Allah Almighty, even if he has committed a major sin or many major sins, because whoever despairs of the mercy of Allah Almighty is a disbeliever, called a Haruri (Kharijite). (Know) that if a believer were to commit all the sins of the people of the earth, it is not permitted for him to despair of the mercy of Allah Almighty, because that is disbelief. The evidence for it is His statement: 'Indeed, none despairs of the relief of Allah except the disbelieving people.' And if a believer kills a thousand believers, or commits adultery with a thousand believing women, and does not pray, does not fast, does not give zakat, does not perform Hajj, does not perform ghusl from janaba, and does more than that, as long as he does not disbelieve, he is truly a believer. If he repents, Allah accepts his repentance. If he leaves the world without repentance, he is under the will of Allah Almighty: if He wills, He will punish him for his sin; if He wills, He will forgive him by His bounty, and he will enter Paradise by His mercy. Whoever says that this believer disbelieves due to these sins is a disbeliever, called a Haruri (Kharijite). Whoever says that if this believer commits these sins and leaves the world without repentance, he will be eternally in Hellfire forever, is a disbeliever, called a Mu'tazili. Whoever says that these sins do not harm this believer after he has believed in Allah Almighty is a disbeliever, called a Murji'i. And know that Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive association with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills.' And He said: 'Say, O My servants who have transgressed against themselves, do not despair of the mercy of Allah. Indeed, Allah forgives all sins. Indeed, He is the Forgiving, the Merciful.' And He said: 'And those who, when they commit an immorality or wrong themselves, remember Allah and seek forgiveness for their sins – and who can forgive sins except Allah?' And He said: 'And whoever does a wrong or wrongs himself but then seeks forgiveness of Allah will find Allah Forgiving and Merciful.' This is sufficient for the intelligent. And Allah Almighty knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage addresses the correct Islamic position on hope and despair, and the fate of a believer who commits major sins. The author begins by stating that one should not despair of Allah's mercy even after major sins, because despair is disbelief, specifically the characteristic of the Khawarij (Haruriyya). He then makes a hyperbolic example: even if a believer committed all sins of the entire earth, he should not despair, citing the Quranic verse 'None despairs of the relief of Allah except the disbelieving people' (Quran 12:87). He continues with a more concrete example: a believer who kills a thousand believers, commits adultery with a thousand women, abandons prayer, fasting, zakat, Hajj, ghusl, and does more, as long as he does not commit disbelief (kufr), he remains a true believer. His fate after death without repentance is in Allah's will: He may punish or forgive, and he will ultimately enter Paradise. The author then condemns three deviant sects: (1) The Khawarij (Haruriyya) who declare such a believer a disbeliever; (2) The Mu'tazila who say he will be eternally in Hell; (3) The Murji'a (Marjab) who say sins do not harm. Each of these positions is declared as kufr. He then supports his view with Quranic verses emphasizing Allah's forgiveness, including the famous verse 'Do not despair of the mercy of Allah, indeed Allah forgives all sins' (Quran 39:53).

Key Terms
القنوط (despair)
الحرورية (Khawarij)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that despairing of Allah's mercy is merely a sin or a sign of weakness, but not disbelief.
Correction: Samarqandi explicitly states that despair is kufr, citing the Quran. Thus, it removes a person from the fold of Islam.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on one who despairs of Allah's mercy?
A) He is a sinner but still a believer.
B) He is a disbeliever.
C) He is a hypocrite.
D) He is an innovator.

Key Takeaway
Despair of Allah's mercy is an act of disbelief that removes a person from the fold of Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that a sin you committed is too great for Allah to forgive? This lesson declares that such despair is disbelief. How will you actively combat that thought the next time it arises?
?
The Khawarij were known for their despair and harsh judgment of others. In your daily interactions, do you ever find yourself feeling that certain people are beyond redemption? What will you do to replace that attitude with hope in Allah's mercy?
?
If you truly believe that despair of mercy is kufr, what practical step will you take today to strengthen your trust in Allah's forgiveness, especially after a major sin?

Major Sinners Under Allah's Will
Samarqandi gives an example of a sinner who remains a believer and explains his fate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunna position on a believer who commits major sins: he remains a believer, and his fate is in Allah's will.

Core Idea
A major sinner remains a believer; Allah may punish or forgive.

Samarqandi presents an extreme example to illustrate that no amount of sin (short of disbelief) removes a person from faith. He then clarifies that such a person's ultimate fate is entirely in Allah's hands—He may punish or forgive by His mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the extreme example
Read the passage describing a believer who commits countless sins but remains a believer. Notice the conditions: as long as he does not disbelieve.
2
Understand the ruling on repentance
Note that if he repents, Allah accepts repentance. If he dies without repentance, his matter is with Allah.
This refutes both the Khawarij (who say he is a disbeliever) and the Mu'tazila (who say he will be eternally punished).
3
Reflect on the middle path
The Ahl al-Sunna hold that major sins do not nullify faith, nor are they harmless. The believer is vulnerable to punishment but ultimately may enter Paradise through Allah's mercy.

Source Text

?

?

?
This lesson says that even killing a thousand believers does not remove faith. Are you using this as a license to sin, telling yourself 'I can always repent later'? What would real repentance look like for you right now?

Refutation of Three Deviant Sects
Samarqandi refutes Khawarij, Mu'tazila, and Murji'a on major sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the positions of the Khawarij, Mu'tazila, and Murji'a on major sinners are considered disbelief.

Core Idea
Three extreme views on major sinners are all false and amount to kufr.

Samarqandi refutes three sects that deviate from the Sunni middle path regarding the fate of major sinners. Each sect is described and explicitly labeled as committing kufr. This lesson exposes these errors and underscores the balanced position of Ahl al-Sunna.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation of each sect
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice that each sect's view is presented and then declared as kufr.
The Khawarij (Haruriyya) declare the sinner a disbeliever; the Mu'tazila say eternal hell; the Murji'a say sins do not harm.
2
Understand why each is wrong
Khawarij go to extremes by excommunicating; Mu'tazila deny Allah's will to forgive; Murji'a negate the harm of sins, leading to licentiousness.
The middle path: major sins are harmful but do not nullify faith, and punishment is subject to Allah's will.
3
Reflect on the term 'kufr' applied here
The author labels these positions as kufr, meaning that holding them can remove one from Islam. This shows the seriousness of theological errors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the one who says major sins do not harm a believer?
A) He is a sinner.
B) He is a disbeliever called Murji'i.
C) He is correct.
D) He is a believer with weak faith.

Key Takeaway
The extreme positions on major sinners—excommunication, eternal damnation, and harmlessness—are all considered disbelief by Ahl al-Sunna.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of these three extreme views do you find yourself subtly leaning towards in your heart? Do you ever judge a fellow Muslim as beyond Allah's mercy (Khawarij), or doubt that Allah's mercy can forgive even the worst sins (Mu'tazila), or take your own sins lightly because 'I have faith' (Murji'a)? How does this lesson expose a hidden illness in your soul?
?
Imagine you have committed a major sin. According to this lesson, what is the correct path between despair and presumption? Are you truly trusting in Allah's mercy while fearing His justice, or have you fallen into one of these extremes? What concrete change will you make today to align your heart with the Ahl al-Sunna position?
?
If you have ever thought that someone else's sin makes them a disbeliever, or that their sin is unforgivable, consider: are you not then guilty of the Kharijite error? How does the source's warning that such a view itself is kufr shake you? Will you repent from harshness and seek to see others with mercy?
